  \label{eq:pnrqcd-tree-coulomb-potential}
\end{equation}
with \(C_F=(N_c^2-1)/N_c\) and the same trace-delta coupling used throughout
this chapter.  This formula is invariant under conversion to the common
half-trace convention because \(g_{\rm ht}^2=2g^2\) and
\(C_F^{\rm ht}=C_F/2\).

\paragraph{Tree-level singlet color factor.}
In the trace convention of \eqref{eq:qcd-casimir-definitions}, the color
factor for one-gluon exchange in a normalized quark-antiquark singlet is
\(-C_F\).  Hence the attractive Coulomb potential is
\eqref{eq:pnrqcd-tree-coulomb-potential}.

The normalized singlet color tensor is
\(\delta^i{}_j/\sqrt{N_c}\).  The antiquark generator is the negative
transpose of the quark generator.  Acting with \(t^a\otimes(-t^{aT})\) on the
singlet gives
\[
  -\frac1{\sqrt{N_c}}(t^at^a)^i{}_j
  =
  -C_F\frac{\delta^i{}_j}{\sqrt{N_c}} .
\]
The spatial Fourier transform of the Coulomb kernel is
\[
  \int\frac{\dd^3\mathbf q}{(2\pi)^3}\,
  \frac{\ee^{\ii\mathbf q\cdot\mathbf r}}{|\mathbf q|^2}
  =
  \frac1{4\pi r},
\]
so the product of the exchange kernel \(g^2/|\mathbf q|^2\) with the singlet
color eigenvalue gives \eqref{eq:pnrqcd-tree-coulomb-potential}.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Ultrasoft dipole sector in weak-coupling pNRQCD]
\label{ca:qcd-pnrqcd-ultrasoft-dipole-window}
A weak-coupling pNRQCD prediction is not specified by the static singlet
potential alone.  After the soft scale \(m_Qv_{\rm rel}\) has been integrated
out, the lower-energy gauge field still fluctuates on the ultrasoft scale
\(m_Qv_{\rm rel}^2\).  The multipole expansion around the center coordinate
\(\mathbf R\) is a separate expansion in
\[
  r\,\partial_{\rm us}\sim v_{\rm rel},
  \qquad r\sim (m_Qv_{\rm rel})^{-1}.
\]
To leading dipole order the singlet and adjoint-octet bilocals are coupled by
the chromoelectric field at \(\mathbf R\),
\begin{equation}
  S_{\rm us}^{SO}
  =
  \int \dd t\,\dd^3\mathbf R\,\dd^3\mathbf r\,
  V_A(r;\mu)\,
  r^i E_i^a(t,\mathbf R)
  \left[O^{a\dagger}(t,\mathbf R,\mathbf r)S(t,\mathbf R,\mathbf r)
  +S^\dagger(t,\mathbf R,\mathbf r)O^a(t,\mathbf R,\mathbf r)\right],
  \label{eq:qcd-pnrqcd-ultrasoft-dipole-coupling}
\end{equation}
where \(V_A\) includes the normalization convention for the gauge field and
for the octet basis used in \eqref{eq:pnrqcd-octet-bilocal}.  In a canonical
half-trace field normalization the same term is usually written with an
explicit gauge coupling; here the normalization is fixed by matching
renormalized QCD matrix elements in the same trace-delta convention as
\eqref{eq:pnrqcd-tree-coulomb-potential}.

The octet is not an optional decoration.  At tree level its color factor is
\(+1/N_c\) in the trace-delta convention, so
\begin{equation}
  V_O^{(0)}(r)=+\frac{g^2}{4\pi N_c r},
  \qquad
  V_O^{(0)}(r)-V_S^{(0)}(r)
  =
  \frac{g^2N_c}{4\pi r}.
  \label{eq:qcd-pnrqcd-tree-octet-gap}
\end{equation}
Thus an ultrasoft chromoelectric fluctuation can virtually promote a singlet
quarkonium state to an octet-heavy-pair state, propagate with the octet
Hamiltonian, and return to the singlet.  For an isolated singlet level
\(|n\rangle\) with singlet Hamiltonian \(H_S|n\rangle=E_n|n\rangle\), the
leading dipole contribution has the renormalized coordinate form
\begin{equation}
  \Delta E_{n,{\rm us}}
  =
  -\ii
  \int_0^\infty \dd t\,
  \langle n|
    r^i\,
    \ee^{-\ii(H_O-E_n)t}\,
    r^j
  |n\rangle\,
  V_A^2\,
  K_{EE}^{ij}(t;\mu)
  +\Delta E_{n,{\rm ct}}(\mu),
  \label{eq:qcd-pnrqcd-ultrasoft-energy-shift}
\end{equation}
with
\[
  K_{EE}^{ij}(t;\mu)
  =
  \left\langle
  E_i^a(t,\mathbf R)\,
  \Phi_{\rm adj}^{ab}(t,0;\mathbf R)\,
  E_j^b(0,\mathbf R)
  \right\rangle_{\rm us,R,\mu}.
\]
The adjoint Wilson transporter \(\Phi_{\rm adj}\) is required for gauge
covariance of the chromoelectric correlator.  The counterterm
\(\Delta E_{n,{\rm ct}}\) subtracts the ultraviolet part already assigned to
the matched potentials and fixes the \(\mu\)-dependence of \(V_S\).  If the
octet-ultrasoft intermediate channel crosses a physical cut, the same
resolvent gives an imaginary part and hence a transition width; below such
cuts it gives a Lamb-shift-like real contribution.  Either way, the physical
object is an energy or width extracted after integrating over ultrasoft
fluctuations, not the static source geometry alone.

A controlled use of \eqref{eq:qcd-pnrqcd-ultrasoft-energy-shift} must state:
the singlet and octet Hamiltonians and mass scheme; the matching scale and
coefficient \(V_A\); the renormalized chromoelectric correlator and its
counterterm convention; the spectral window separating the chosen singlet
level from nearby thresholds; and residual estimates for omitted multipoles,
higher potentials, relativistic corrections, and nonperturbative ultrasoft
input.  Without this data, a potential-model spectrum is only the leading
coordinate of the pNRQCD expansion.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\paragraph{Leading Coulombic \(1S\) quarkonium level.}
Assume a weak-coupling pNRQCD chart in which the spin-independent singlet
Hamiltonian is truncated to
\begin{equation}
  H_C
  =
  -\frac{\nabla_{\mathbf r}^2}{m_Q}
  -\frac{\alpha_C}{r},
  \qquad
  \alpha_C:=\frac{g^2C_F}{4\pi},
  \qquad r=|\mathbf r|.
  \label{eq:qcd-coulombic-pnrqcd-hamiltonian}
\end{equation}
Here \(m_Q\) is the heavy-quark mass coordinate in the same short-distance
scheme as the potential coordinate.  The normalized \(1S\) eigenfunction
\begin{equation}
  \psi_{1S}(\mathbf r)
  =
  \left(\frac{\kappa^3}{\pi}\right)^{1/2}\ee^{-\kappa r},
  \qquad
  \kappa:=\frac{m_Q\alpha_C}{2},
  \label{eq:qcd-coulombic-one-s-wavefunction}
\end{equation}
has energy
\begin{equation}
  E_{1S}^{(0)}
  =
  -\frac{m_Q\alpha_C^2}{4},
  \qquad
  |\psi_{1S}(0)|^2=
  \frac{(m_Q\alpha_C)^3}{8\pi}.
  \label{eq:qcd-coulombic-one-s-energy-origin}
\end{equation}
The corresponding leading spin-averaged quarkonium mass coordinate is
\[
  M_{1S}^{(0)}=2m_Q+E_{1S}^{(0)}
\]
before the additive mass--potential rearrangements of
Section~\ref{sec:qcd-heavy-mass-static-energy} and before ultrasoft,
relativistic, and spin-dependent corrections are included.

For \(r>0\),
\[
  \nabla^2\ee^{-\kappa r}
  =
  \left(\kappa^2-\frac{2\kappa}{r}\right)\ee^{-\kappa r}.
\]
Thus
\[
  H_C\ee^{-\kappa r}
  =
  \left[
    -\frac{\kappa^2}{m_Q}
    +
    \left(\frac{2\kappa}{m_Q}-\alpha_C\right)\frac1r
  \right]\ee^{-\kappa r}.
\]
With \(\kappa=m_Q\alpha_C/2\) the \(1/r\) term cancels and the eigenvalue is
\(-\kappa^2/m_Q=-m_Q\alpha_C^2/4\).  The normalization follows from
\[
  4\pi
  \left(\frac{\kappa^3}{\pi}\right)
  \int_0^\infty r^2\ee^{-2\kappa r}\,\dd r
  =
  4\kappa^3\frac{2}{(2\kappa)^3}=1,
\]
and the value at the origin is the square of the normalization constant.
The mass formula is then the definition of the spin-averaged singlet energy
coordinate in this leading Hamiltonian.  This calculation does not define the
physical charmonium or bottomonium spectrum by itself: it computes the first
term in a declared pNRQCD expansion whose mass scheme, matching scale, and
omitted operators must be specified.

\paragraph{Quarkonium fine and hyperfine spin algebra.}
Fix a quarkonium radial level and orbital angular momentum \(L\) in a
pNRQCD specification.  Let
\[
  \mathbf S_Q=\frac12\boldsymbol\sigma_Q,\qquad
  \mathbf S_{\bar Q}=\frac12\boldsymbol\sigma_{\bar Q},\qquad
  \mathbf S=\mathbf S_Q+\mathbf S_{\bar Q},\qquad
  \mathbf J=\mathbf L+\mathbf S .
\]
Assume that, to first order in the spin-dependent part of the matched
Hamiltonian, the restriction to this radial-orbital subspace has the form
\begin{equation}
  H_{nL}^{\rm sd}
  =
  A_{nL}\,\mathbf S_Q\cdot\mathbf S_{\bar Q}
  +
  B_{nL}\,\mathbf L\cdot\mathbf S
  +
  C_{nL}\,\mathcal T_{LS},
  \label{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-dependent-hamiltonian}
\end{equation}
where \(A_{nL},B_{nL},C_{nL}\) are radial matrix elements or matching
coefficients in the chosen scheme, and \(\mathcal T_{LS}\) is the rotational
scalar obtained by coupling a traceless rank-two orbital tensor to a
traceless rank-two spin tensor.  Then
\begin{equation}
  \mathbf S_Q\cdot\mathbf S_{\bar Q}
  =
  \begin{cases}
  -\frac34, & S=0,\\[2mm]
  \frac14, & S=1,
  \end{cases}
  \label{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-spin-eigenvalues}
\end{equation}
and, on the triplet \(S=1\) states,
\begin{equation}
  \mathbf L\cdot\mathbf S
  =
  \frac12\bigl(J(J+1)-L(L+1)-2\bigr)
  =
  \begin{cases}
  -(L+1), & J=L-1,\\
  -1, & J=L,\\
  L, & J=L+1 .
  \end{cases}
  \label{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-orbit-eigenvalues}
\end{equation}
If \(M(^1L_L)\) denotes the singlet mass and \(M(^3L_J)\) the triplet masses
computed to this first order from a common spin-independent radial level
\(E_{nL}^{(0)}\), then the triplet centroid obeys
\begin{equation}
  \overline M(^3L)
  :=
  \frac{\sum_{J=L-1}^{L+1}(2J+1)M(^3L_J)}{3(2L+1)}
  =
  E_{nL}^{(0)}+\frac14 A_{nL},
  \label{eq:qcd-quarkonium-triplet-centroid}
\end{equation}
with the obvious omission of the nonexistent \(J=L-1\) term when \(L=0\).
The centroid hyperfine difference is therefore
\begin{equation}
  \overline M(^3L)-M(^1L_L)=A_{nL}.
  \label{eq:qcd-quarkonium-hyperfine-centroid}
\end{equation}
The two heavy spins are spin-\(\frac12\) representations.  Since
\[
  \mathbf S^2
  =
  \mathbf S_Q^2+\mathbf S_{\bar Q}^2
  +2\mathbf S_Q\cdot\mathbf S_{\bar Q},
  \qquad
  \mathbf S_Q^2=\mathbf S_{\bar Q}^2=\frac34,
\]
one has
\[
  \mathbf S_Q\cdot\mathbf S_{\bar Q}
  =
  \frac12\left(S(S+1)-\frac32\right),
\]
which gives \eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-spin-eigenvalues} for
\(S=0,1\).  Similarly
\[
  \mathbf J^2
  =
  \mathbf L^2+\mathbf S^2+2\mathbf L\cdot\mathbf S
\]
gives the first equality in
\eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-orbit-eigenvalues}; substituting
\(S=1\) and \(J=L-1,L,L+1\) gives the displayed three values.

It remains to check the centroid.  The trace of \(\mathbf L\cdot\mathbf S\)
on the tensor product of the orbital \(L\) space and the triplet spin space
vanishes:
\[
  \operatorname{Tr}_{L\otimes S=1}(\mathbf L\cdot\mathbf S)
  =
  \sum_i \operatorname{Tr}_{L}(L_i)\operatorname{Tr}_{S=1}(S_i)=0,
\]
because every generator of an irreducible \(SU(2)\) representation is
traceless.  The operator \(\mathcal T_{LS}\) is a contraction of traceless
rank-two tensors, so its trace on the same tensor product also vanishes.  The
weighted sum
\(\sum_J(2J+1)M(^3L_J)\) is precisely this trace after decomposition into
irreducible \(J\) summands.  Therefore only the spin-independent energy and
the triplet spin-spin eigenvalue \(\frac14A_{nL}\) survive in the centroid,
proving \eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-triplet-centroid}.  The singlet has
\(\mathbf L\cdot\mathbf S=0\), no rank-two spin tensor, and spin-spin
eigenvalue \(-\frac34\); subtracting its first-order mass from the triplet
centroid gives \eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-hyperfine-centroid}.
The spin algebra above is the part of quarkonium spectroscopy that follows
from angular momentum and the matched operator form alone.  The numerical
values of
\(A_{nL},B_{nL},C_{nL}\) are QCD matching data.  In weak-coupling pNRQCD they
are computed from perturbative potentials and wavefunctions in a stated mass
scheme; in strong-coupling pNRQCD they are Wilson-loop and chromofield
insertion matrix elements.  In either case the symbols
``hyperfine splitting'' and ``fine structure'' refer to the spectral
differences defined by
\eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-orbit-eigenvalues}--\eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-hyperfine-centroid},
rather than to a freestanding constituent-potential model.

\paragraph{Leading weak-coupling \(1S\) hyperfine coordinate.}
In the weak-coupling \(1S\) chart above, retain the leading
chromomagnetic contact operator
\begin{equation}
  H_{\rm ss}^{1S}
  =
  \frac{8\pi\alpha_C\,c_F(\mu)^2}{3m_Q^2}\,
  \mathbf S_Q\cdot\mathbf S_{\bar Q}\,
  \delta^{(3)}(\mathbf r),
  \label{eq:qcd-pnrqcd-contact-spin-spin}
\end{equation}
where \(c_F(\mu)\) is the chromomagnetic matching coefficient in the same
short-distance mass and coupling scheme as \(m_Q\) and \(\alpha_C\).  To first
order in this operator,
\begin{equation}
  M(^3S_1)-M(^1S_0)
  =
  \frac{8\pi\alpha_C\,c_F(\mu)^2}{3m_Q^2}
  |\psi_{1S}(0)|^2
  =
  \frac{m_Q\,c_F(\mu)^2\,\alpha_C^4}{3}.
  \label{eq:qcd-one-s-hyperfine-contact-result}
\end{equation}
The displayed number is a leading coordinate in the declared weak-coupling
pNRQCD scheme.  It is not by itself a precision prediction for charmonium or
bottomonium until the mass scheme, higher-order potentials, ultrasoft terms,
nonperturbative corrections, and continuum-limit uncertainties have been
specified.
First-order perturbation theory in the normalized Coulombic \(1S\) state gives
\[
  \langle H_{\rm ss}^{1S}\rangle_{S}
  =
  \frac{8\pi\alpha_C\,c_F(\mu)^2}{3m_Q^2}
  |\psi_{1S}(0)|^2\,
  \langle\mathbf S_Q\cdot\mathbf S_{\bar Q}\rangle_S .
\]
For the triplet \(S=1\) the spin expectation value is \(1/4\), and for the
singlet \(S=0\) it is \(-3/4\), as shown in
\eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-spin-eigenvalues}.  Their difference is one, so
the triplet-singlet mass splitting is exactly the contact coefficient times
\(|\psi_{1S}(0)|^2\).  Substituting
\eqref{eq:qcd-coulombic-one-s-energy-origin},
\[
  |\psi_{1S}(0)|^2=\frac{(m_Q\alpha_C)^3}{8\pi},
\]
gives the second equality in
\eqref{eq:qcd-one-s-hyperfine-contact-result}.  The proof uses only the
declared pNRQCD contact operator and the Coulombic \(1S\) wavefunction; all
other terms belong to the stated remainder of the weak-coupling chart.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Quarkonium scale separation]
\label{ca:nrqcd-pnrqcd-scale-separation}
Let \(v_{\rm rel}\) be the velocity coordinate assigned to a family of
quarkonium states.  The weak-coupling potential expansion assumes
\[
  m_Q\gg m_Qv_{\rm rel}\gg m_Qv_{\rm rel}^2,
  \qquad
  m_Qv_{\rm rel}\gg \Lambda_{\rm QCD},
\]
so that the soft relative-momentum scale can be integrated out
perturbatively.  Strong-coupling pNRQCD instead treats the potential as a
nonperturbative matching coefficient defined by static Wilson-loop and
chromofield-insertion matrix elements.  In both regimes a claim of accuracy
requires a norm or class of smeared matrix elements and an explicit remainder
estimate in powers of \(v_{\rm rel}\), \(1/m_Q\), and
\(\Lambda_{\rm QCD}/(m_Qv_{\rm rel})\) when that ratio is used.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\section{Heavy-Quark Mass Coordinates and Static Energies}
\label{sec:qcd-heavy-mass-static-energy}

The mass \(m_Q\) appearing in HQET, NRQCD, and pNRQCD is a coordinate in a
regulated Lagrangian and in its matched effective descriptions.  In a confining
four-dimensional QCD theory an isolated colored quark is not an asymptotic
particle, so a quark pole mass is not a gauge-invariant spectral observable.
Perturbation theory in a fixed gauge nevertheless defines formal mass
coordinates, including an on-shell coordinate order by order.  Such
coordinates are useful only after their infrared sensitivity and their
relation to gauge-invariant quantities have been stated.

The gauge-invariant static quark-antiquark energy is extracted from Wilson
loops.  With a specified line-renormalization prescription, define
\begin{equation}
  E_{\rm stat}(r;\mu)
  =
  -\lim_{T\to\infty}\frac1T
  \log \langle W_{\square}(r,T)\rangle_{\rm ren,\mu},
  \label{eq:qcd-static-energy-renormalized}
\end{equation}
where \(W_{\square}(r,T)\) is the rectangular fundamental Wilson loop of
spatial size \(r\) and time extent \(T\).  The subscript records the
ultraviolet and line-renormalization convention.  Additive constants in
\(E_{\rm stat}\) are not absolute observables; energy differences and matched
hadron masses are.

At distances \(r\) in a weak-coupling matching range, the pNRQCD singlet
potential is a coordinate in the decomposition
\begin{equation}
  E_{\rm stat}(r;\mu)
  =
  2m_{\rm sd}(\mu_f)+V_{\rm sd}(r;\mu,\mu_f)+\Delta_{\rm us}(r;\mu,\mu_f),
  \label{eq:qcd-static-energy-sd-decomposition}
\end{equation}
where \(m_{\rm sd}\) is a short-distance heavy-quark mass coordinate,
\(V_{\rm sd}\) is the corresponding singlet potential coordinate, and
\(\Delta_{\rm us}\) denotes lower-energy contributions retained in pNRQCD.
The auxiliary scale \(\mu_f\) separates contributions assigned to the mass
coordinate from contributions assigned to the potential coordinate.

\begin{remark}[Constant mass-coordinate transformations]
\label{rem:qcd-heavy-mass-potential-shift}
Let \(\delta m\) be a finite scheme change independent of \(r\).  The
coordinate transformation
\begin{equation}
  m_{\rm sd}'=m_{\rm sd}+\delta m,
  \qquad
  V_{\rm sd}'(r)=V_{\rm sd}(r)-2\delta m
  \label{eq:qcd-heavy-mass-potential-shift}
\end{equation}
leaves the static energy \eqref{eq:qcd-static-energy-sd-decomposition}
unchanged when \(\Delta_{\rm us}\) is held fixed.  If a pNRQCD Hamiltonian is
shifted by \(V_{\rm sd}\mapsto V_{\rm sd}-2\delta m\), every singlet
eigenvalue \(E_n\) is shifted by \(-2\delta m\), and
\(2m_{\rm sd}+E_n\) is unchanged.
\par
Substitution into \eqref{eq:qcd-static-energy-sd-decomposition} gives
\[
  2(m_{\rm sd}+\delta m)+(V_{\rm sd}-2\delta m)+\Delta_{\rm us}
  =
  2m_{\rm sd}+V_{\rm sd}+\Delta_{\rm us}.
\]
For a Hamiltonian \(H_{\rm sd}=T+V_{\rm sd}\), the transformed Hamiltonian is
\(H_{\rm sd}'=H_{\rm sd}-2\delta m\).  If
\(H_{\rm sd}\psi_n=E_n\psi_n\), then
\(H_{\rm sd}'\psi_n=(E_n-2\delta m)\psi_n\).  Therefore
\[
  2(m_{\rm sd}+\delta m)+(E_n-2\delta m)=2m_{\rm sd}+E_n .
\]
The statement is finite-dimensional spectral algebra applied to the
regularized Hamiltonian, and then to any limit in which the relevant
eigenvalue exists.
\end{remark}

One useful short-distance coordinate is the potential-subtracted mass.  Start
from a formal perturbative pole coordinate \(m_{\rm pole}\) and define
\begin{equation}
  m_{\rm PS}(\mu_f)
  =
  m_{\rm pole}-\delta m_{\rm PS}(\mu_f),
  \qquad
  \delta m_{\rm PS}(\mu_f)
  =
  -\frac12
  \int_{|\mathbf q|<\mu_f}
  \frac{\dd^3\mathbf q}{(2\pi)^3}\,
  \widetilde V(\mathbf q),
  \label{eq:qcd-ps-mass-definition}
\end{equation}
where \(\widetilde V(\mathbf q)\) is the perturbative momentum-space singlet
potential in the same convention.  At tree level
\[
  \widetilde V^{(0)}(\mathbf q)=-\frac{g^2C_F}{|\mathbf q|^2}.
\]
Consequently
\begin{equation}
  \delta m_{\rm PS}^{(0)}(\mu_f)
  =
  \frac{g^2C_F}{4\pi^2}\,\mu_f .
  \label{eq:qcd-ps-leading-subtraction}
\end{equation}
In the common half-trace convention this is the same expression because
\(g_{\rm ht}^2C_F^{\rm ht}=g^2C_F\).

Using spherical coordinates in momentum space,
\[
  \int_{|\mathbf q|<\mu_f}
  \frac{\dd^3\mathbf q}{(2\pi)^3}\,\frac1{|\mathbf q|^2}
  =
  \frac{4\pi}{(2\pi)^3}\int_0^{\mu_f}\dd q
  =
  \frac{\mu_f}{2\pi^2}.
\]
Multiplying by \(g^2C_F/2\), as dictated by
\eqref{eq:qcd-ps-mass-definition} and
\(\widetilde V^{(0)}=-g^2C_F/|\mathbf q|^2\), gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-ps-leading-subtraction}.

\begin{remark}[Renormalon language in the heavy-quark sector]
\label{rem:qcd-heavy-renormalon-status}
The leading infrared sensitivity of the formal perturbative pole coordinate
and the additive constant in the perturbative static potential are tied to the
same long-distance momentum region.  In perturbative large-order language this
is described as a cancellation of the leading static-energy renormalon between
\(2m_{\rm pole}\) and \(V_{\rm pole}(r)\).  The mathematically precise
statement used here is the finite coordinate transformation
\eqref{eq:qcd-heavy-mass-potential-shift} and the definition of
short-distance coordinates such as \eqref{eq:qcd-ps-mass-definition}.  A claim
about a Borel singularity, its residue, or its cancellation is a claim about a
specified perturbative expansion and summation prescription, not a
nonperturbative definition of the quark mass.
\end{remark}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Mass schemes in quarkonium predictions]
\label{ca:qcd-heavy-mass-scheme-control}
A quarkonium prediction based on pNRQCD must state the mass coordinate, the
potential coordinate, the subtraction scale \(\mu_f\) when one is used, and the
class of matrix elements or energy levels being approximated.  Replacing
\((m,V)\) by a short-distance pair \((m',V')\) is exact at the level of the
matched Hamiltonian if \eqref{eq:qcd-heavy-mass-potential-shift} is imposed.
Truncating perturbative series introduces residual \(\mu_f\)- and
scheme-dependence; the size of that dependence is an error diagnostic only
after the truncation order, velocity counting, and ultrasoft treatment have
been fixed.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\section{Color and Physical External States}

The gauge-fixed quark and gluon fields are useful local variables in
perturbation theory.  Physical states are BRST cohomology classes, and local
physical operators are represented by gauge-invariant or BRST-closed
operators.  This has an immediate consequence for scattering: LSZ reduction
applied to the elementary quark or gluon fields does not by itself define a
physical hadron \(S\)-matrix.  Physical external states in QCD are created by
color-singlet operators, such as
\[
  \bar q_I q_J,\qquad
  \bar q_I\gamma^\mu q_J,\qquad
  \epsilon_{i_1\cdots i_{N_c}}
  q^{i_1}_{I_1}\cdots q^{i_{N_c}}_{I_{N_c}},
  \qquad
  \operatorname{tr}(F_{\mu\nu}F^{\mu\nu}).
\]
The first three are mesonic current, vector-current, and baryonic examples;
the last is a gluonic example.

Confinement, in the spectral sense used here, is the assertion that isolated
finite-energy asymptotic particles carry no color.  In four-dimensional QCD
this assertion is a nonperturbative physical input, supported by the observed
hadron spectrum and by lattice evidence, rather than a theorem presently
derived from the continuum Lagrangian.  The monograph uses this precise
spectral hypothesis when discussing QCD phenomenology: the asymptotic states
are hadrons, while the short-distance operator expansion is expressed in terms
of quark and gluon fields because those are the local variables of the
renormalized gauge theory.

\begin{openproblem}[Asymptotic completeness of physical QCD]
\label{op:qcd-asymptotic-completeness}
Starting from a nonperturbative four-dimensional QCD Hilbert space
\(\mathcal H_{\rm phys}\), its unitary translation representation, and its
gauge-invariant local observable algebra, construct the physical incoming and
outgoing scattering theory.  The required asymptotic space
\[
  \mathcal H_{\rm as}^{\rm QCD}
\]
should be built from stable color-singlet Wigner particles in the relevant
superselection sectors: mesons, baryons, glueballs in pure Yang--Mills
subsectors, and, in chiral limits, the massless Goldstone modes with their
long-distance scattering structure.  Unstable hadronic resonances should enter
through the analytic structure of the color-singlet scattering operator rather
than as ordinary external vectors.  The wave operators
\[
  \Omega_{\rm in/out}^{\rm QCD}:
  \mathcal H_{\rm as}^{\rm QCD}\longrightarrow \mathcal H_{\rm phys}
\]
should be isometric, should intertwine translations, and should have common
closed range equal to the finite-energy physical sector under consideration:
\[
  \overline{\operatorname{Ran}\Omega_{\rm in}^{\rm QCD}}
  =
  \overline{\operatorname{Ran}\Omega_{\rm out}^{\rm QCD}}
  =
  \mathcal H_{\rm phys}^{\rm sector}.
\]
One must also construct the detector limits, such as the energy-flow
operators below, on the same scattering domain and prove that the inclusive
calorimetric observables used in high-energy QCD are obtained from this
Hilbert-space scattering theory.

This problem is logically stronger than asymptotic freedom, factorization, a
mass gap in pure Yang--Mills theory, or the spectral confinement hypothesis
used above.  Asymptotic freedom controls short-distance operator products and
partonic coefficient functions.  Factorization gives a perturbative expansion
for selected inclusive observables after the relevant operator matrix elements
have been defined.  Asymptotic completeness is a large-time statement about
the range of physical wave operators in the gauge-invariant Hilbert space.
\end{openproblem}

\section{Hadron Spectroscopy as Ab Initio QCD}
\label{sec:qcd-hadron-spectroscopy-ab-initio}

\subsection{Spectral Sources and Finite-Volume Data}
\label{subsec:qcd-spectroscopy-sources-finite-volume}

Hadron spectroscopy is not a list of model names assigned to observed peaks.
It is a collection of spectral and scattering statements about the
gauge-invariant Hilbert space of QCD.  A spectroscopic claim must therefore
state which Hilbert-space object is being computed.  Stable hadrons are
isolated eigenvalues of the mass operator \(M^2=P_\mu P^\mu\) in color-singlet
superselection sectors.  Resonances are poles of color-singlet scattering
amplitudes on specified nonphysical sheets, as in
Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-resonances-dressed-propagators}; they are not
additional vectors in the asymptotic Hilbert space.  Finite-volume energy
levels are regulator observables whose infinite-volume interpretation requires
a quantization map, not a direct equality between a box eigenvalue and a
resonance mass.

Let \(I,J\) denote flavor labels and let \(i,j\) be color labels.  Typical
local color-singlet sources are
\begin{align}
  M_{\Gamma,IJ}(x)
  &=
  \bar q_I(x)\Gamma q_J(x),
  \label{eq:qcd-meson-local-source}\\
  B_{\alpha_1\cdots\alpha_{N_c};I_1\cdots I_{N_c}}(x)
  &=
  \epsilon_{i_1\cdots i_{N_c}}\,
  q^{i_1}_{\alpha_1 I_1}(x)\cdots
  q^{i_{N_c}}_{\alpha_{N_c} I_{N_c}}(x),
  \label{eq:qcd-baryon-local-source}\\
  G_{\mathcal P}(x)
  &=
  \operatorname{tr}\mathcal P(F_{\mu\nu},D_\rho)(x).
  \label{eq:qcd-glueball-local-source}
\end{align}
Here \(\Gamma\) is a Dirac matrix, possibly with covariant derivatives
inserted and with Lorentz indices projected to a definite spin channel, and
\(\mathcal P\) is a gauge-covariant polynomial whose color indices are traced
using the convention fixed in \eqref{eq:qcd-casimir-definitions}.  Nonlocal
sources are allowed, but their Wilson lines, smearing kernels, and endpoint
renormalizations are part of the operator definition.  For example, a hybrid
meson source may be represented by
\[
  \bar q_I(x)\Gamma^{\mu\nu} F_{\mu\nu}(x) q_J(x),
\]
or by a point-split bilinear with a Wilson-line path and a field-strength
insertion on that path.  These are different regulator coordinates unless a
continuum matching relation has been supplied.

\begin{definition}[Hadron spectral extraction setup]
\label{def:qcd-hadron-spectral-extraction-setup}
A QCD hadron spectral extraction setup consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the quark masses, gauge group, global form, spacetime volume, boundary
  conditions, and regulator action;
  \item a list of gauge-invariant interpolating operators, including their
  flavor, parity, charge conjugation, spin or cubic-group channel, smearing,
  and renormalization prescriptions;
  \item the Euclidean correlation matrix
  \[
    C_{AB}(t)=
    \langle \mathcal O_A(t)\mathcal O_B^\dagger(0)\rangle
    -\langle \mathcal O_A\rangle\langle\mathcal O_B^\dagger\rangle ;
  \]
  \item a declared estimator of finite-volume color-singlet energies from the
  transfer matrix or Euclidean correlators, including its source basis, fit
  window, covariance treatment, and stability diagnostics;
  \item a map from finite-volume energies to infinite-volume observables:
  isolated stable masses for one-particle states, and scattering amplitudes or
  pole positions for resonances;
  \item continuum, chiral, heavy-quark, and infinite-volume extrapolations,
  with the systematics stated separately.
\end{enumerate}
The setup is called \emph{ab initio} only when the matrix elements are defined
from the QCD path integral or Hilbert space itself.  A constituent model may
be useful as a coordinate chart or mnemonic, but it is not an ab initio
definition of the spectrum.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Operator-sector spectroscopy chart]
\label{def:qcd-operator-sector-spectroscopy-chart}
Fix a finite-volume regulator and a symmetry channel \(\Gamma\).  Let
\(\mathcal V_\Gamma\) be a finite-dimensional vector space of renormalized
gauge-invariant interpolating operators in that channel, modulo operators
whose matrix elements vanish on the finite-volume Hilbert subspace being
sampled.  A spectroscopy chart is a choice of ordered basis
\((\mathcal O_1,\ldots,\mathcal O_m)\) of \(\mathcal V_\Gamma\), together
with any declared decomposition
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal V_\Gamma
  =
  \mathcal V_{\rm loc}\oplus
  \mathcal V_{\rm two\text{-}hadron}\oplus
  \mathcal V_{\rm flux}\oplus\cdots .
  \label{eq:qcd-spectroscopy-source-decomposition}
\end{equation}
The summands in \eqref{eq:qcd-spectroscopy-source-decomposition} are source
subspaces, not Hilbert-space superselection sectors.  For example,
\(\mathcal V_{\rm loc}\) may contain local \(q\bar q\), baryon, or pure-glue
operators, \(\mathcal V_{\rm two\text{-}hadron}\) may contain products of
separately projected hadron operators, and \(\mathcal V_{\rm flux}\) may
contain point-split bilinears with field-strength insertions or extended
Wilson-line paths.  The decomposition is part of the chart; it is not an
invariant classification of states unless a regulator, renormalization
scheme, and continuum matching prescription have also been supplied.
\end{definition}

For a finite spatial torus and a reflection-positive lattice regulator, the
spectral decomposition has the same form as
\eqref{eq:volxi-glueball-spectral-matrix}:
\[
  C_{AB}(t)=
  \sum_{n\ge0}Z_A^{(n)}\overline{Z_B^{(n)}}\ee^{-E_n t},
  \qquad
  Z_A^{(n)}=\bra{\Omega}\mathcal O_A\ket{n,L}.
\]
The vectors \(\ket{n,L}\) are finite-volume color-singlet eigenvectors.  If
an eigenvalue converges, after removing the center-of-mass motion and taking
the regulator limits, to an isolated one-particle mass below all relevant
thresholds, the resulting number is a stable-hadron mass.  Above threshold the
finite-volume levels instead sample the scattering operator.  In a single
elastic two-particle channel with total momentum zero, particle masses
\(m_1,m_2\), relative momentum \(k\), and energy
\[
  E=\sqrt{m_1^2+k^2}+\sqrt{m_2^2+k^2},
\]
the simplest unmixed partial-wave quantization condition is
\begin{equation}
  \delta_\ell(k)+\phi_{\ell}(q)=n\pi,
  \qquad
  q=\frac{kL}{2\pi},
  \label{eq:qcd-luscher-single-channel-condition}
\end{equation}
where \(\delta_\ell\) is the infinite-volume elastic phase shift and
\(\phi_\ell\) is a known geometric function built from the finite-volume zeta
function.  Equation~\eqref{eq:qcd-luscher-single-channel-condition} is not a
model of a resonance.  It is a finite-volume reconstruction theorem under
elasticity, locality, and regulator hypotheses.  In realistic QCD channels
one must use the coupled-channel determinant version, because cubic symmetry
mixes partial waves and inelastic thresholds are often nearby.

\paragraph{Source coordinates and invariant output.}
The QCD output of the preceding construction is not a preferred source basis.
At finite regulator the invariant spectral data are the color-singlet
transfer-matrix energies and their symmetry labels; after the continuum and
infinite-volume limits they become stable masses, scattering amplitudes, or
sheet-labeled pole data according to the channel.  Source-overlap phrases such
as ``mostly two-hadron'', ``mostly hybrid'', or ``mostly glueball'' are
coordinate statements about the chosen operator family.  They acquire
unambiguous meaning only after the source subspaces in
\eqref{eq:qcd-spectroscopy-source-decomposition}, their renormalization and
smearing prescriptions, and the positive form used to compare overlap
covectors have all been declared.  Changing these source coordinates can
change the quoted overlap fractions without changing the finite-volume energy
or the reconstructed pole.  This chapter therefore records the QCD-specific
operators and the spectral or scattering quantity being extracted, while the
finite-regulator estimator itself is part of the numerical methodology.

\begin{remark}[Spectroscopic names as derived coordinates]
\label{rem:qcd-spectroscopic-names-derived}
In the finite-volume QCD framework above, the invariant output of a stable
sector is an energy level and its quantum numbers, while the invariant output
of a resonance sector is a sheet-labeled pole and residue data after a
finite-volume-to-infinite-volume reconstruction.  Names such as conventional
meson, glueball, hybrid, molecule, tetraquark, or flux-tube excitation are
therefore derived coordinates on source overlaps, pole residues, large-\(N_c\)
scaling, and deformation behavior.  They are not additional definitions of
QCD states.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Elastic Finite-Volume Reconstruction}
\label{subsec:qcd-elastic-finite-volume-reconstruction}

\begin{definition}[Periodic Green function and \(S\)-wave zeta coordinate]
\label{def:qcd-periodic-green-zeta-coordinate}
For a cubic spatial torus of side \(L\), let
\[
  \mathbf p_{\mathbf n}:=\frac{2\pi}{L}\mathbf n,\qquad
  \mathbf n\in\mathbb Z^3,
\]
and let \(k>0\) be such that \(k^2\ne \mathbf p_{\mathbf n}^{\,2}\) for all
\(\mathbf n\).  The periodic Helmholtz Green function is the distribution
\begin{equation}
  G_L(\mathbf r;k)
  :=
  \frac1{L^3}
  \sum_{\mathbf n\in\mathbb Z^3}
  \frac{\ee^{\ii\mathbf p_{\mathbf n}\cdot\mathbf r}}
       {\mathbf p_{\mathbf n}^{\,2}-k^2},
  \qquad
  (\Delta+k^2)G_L(\mathbf r;k)=-\delta_L(\mathbf r),
  \label{eq:qcd-periodic-helmholtz-green}
\end{equation}
where \(\delta_L\) is the periodic delta distribution.  Its singular expansion
at the origin is written
\begin{equation}
  G_L(\mathbf r;k)
  =
  \frac{1}{4\pi|\mathbf r|}
  +
  c_L(k)
  +O(|\mathbf r|),
  \qquad
  \mathbf r\to0.
  \label{eq:qcd-periodic-green-constant-term}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, with \(q=kL/(2\pi)\), define the analytically continued
Luescher zeta coordinate \(\mathcal Z_{00}(1;q^2)\) by
\begin{equation}
  4\pi c_L(k)
  =
  \frac{2}{\sqrt\pi\,L}\,
  \mathcal Z_{00}(1;q^2),
  \qquad
  \mathcal Z_{00}(s;q^2)
  :=
  \frac1{\sqrt{4\pi}}
  \sum_{\mathbf n\in\mathbb Z^3}
  \frac{1}{(\mathbf n^2-q^2)^s}
  \quad(\operatorname{Re}s>\tfrac32),
  \label{eq:qcd-luscher-zeta-coordinate}
\end{equation}
continued meromorphically to \(s=1\).  The singular summands at
\(\mathbf n^2=q^2\) are absent from the elastic interval under discussion;
when a free two-particle level is crossed, the condition is read by the usual
limiting prescription from adjacent \(q^2\).
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[\(S\)-wave finite-volume quantization from wave matching]
\label{prop:qcd-swave-luscher-wave-matching}
Consider a single elastic two-particle channel in the center-of-mass frame.
Assume the two stable particles have masses \(m_1,m_2\), the interaction range
in the relative coordinate is contained in \(|\mathbf r|<R\), the box obeys
\(L>2R\), and the finite-volume corrections from virtual particles wrapping
around the torus are bounded by \(C\ee^{-m_{\rm gap}L}\) for some positive
mass scale \(m_{\rm gap}\) in the omitted exchange channel.  In an exact
finite-range model this exponential remainder is absent.  Assume also that
the cubic irrep isolates the \(S\)-wave, so higher partial waves are not
retained in the truncation.  Let \(k\) be the relative momentum determined by
\[
  E=\sqrt{m_1^2+k^2}+\sqrt{m_2^2+k^2}.
\]
Then the finite-volume energy is allowed precisely when
\begin{equation}
  k\cot\delta_0(k)=4\pi c_L(k)
  =
  \frac{2}{\sqrt\pi\,L}\mathcal Z_{00}(1;q^2),
  \qquad q=\frac{kL}{2\pi}.
  \label{eq:qcd-swave-luscher-kcot-form}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
  q\cot\delta_0(k)=\frac1{\pi^{3/2}}\mathcal Z_{00}(1;q^2),
  \qquad
  \delta_0(k)+\phi_0(q)=n\pi,
  \qquad
  \cot\phi_0(q)=
  -\frac{\mathcal Z_{00}(1;q^2)}{\pi^{3/2}q}.
  \label{eq:qcd-swave-luscher-phase-form}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Outside the interaction region the relative wave function
\(\psi(\mathbf r)\) satisfies the free Helmholtz equation
\((\Delta+k^2)\psi=0\) and periodic boundary conditions.  In the \(S\)-wave
truncation any such finite-volume solution with a source at the origin is
proportional, in the exterior region \(R<|\mathbf r|<L/2\), to the periodic
Green function \(G_L(\mathbf r;k)\).  The proportionality constant is
irrelevant; the quantization condition is obtained by comparing the ratio of
the regular and singular terms in the short-distance expansion.

The infinite-volume elastic \(S\)-wave outside the interaction range has the
standard real form
\[
  \psi_{\infty}(r)
  =
  A\,\frac{\sin(kr+\delta_0(k))}{kr},
  \qquad r>R .
\]
Expanding this expression at small \(r\) gives
\[
  \psi_{\infty}(r)
  =
  A\left[
    \frac{\sin\delta_0(k)}{kr}
    +
    \cos\delta_0(k)
    +O(r)
  \right].
\]
Thus the ratio of the regular coefficient to the \(1/r\) coefficient is
\begin{equation}
  \frac{A\cos\delta_0(k)}
       {A\sin\delta_0(k)/k}
  =
  k\cot\delta_0(k).
  \label{eq:qcd-swave-boundary-ratio}
\end{equation}
On the other hand, the finite-volume exterior solution proportional to
\eqref{eq:qcd-periodic-helmholtz-green} has expansion
\[
  B\,G_L(\mathbf r;k)
  =
  B\left[
    \frac1{4\pi r}+c_L(k)+O(r)
  \right],
  \qquad r=|\mathbf r|.
  \]
Its regular-to-singular ratio is \(4\pi c_L(k)\).  Matching the exterior
finite-volume solution to the infinite-volume scattering boundary condition
therefore gives the first equality in
\eqref{eq:qcd-swave-luscher-kcot-form}.  The second equality is the zeta
coordinate definition \eqref{eq:qcd-luscher-zeta-coordinate}.

Multiplying the first form by \(L/(2\pi)\) and using \(q=kL/(2\pi)\) gives
the first equation in \eqref{eq:qcd-swave-luscher-phase-form}.  The phase
form follows by defining \(\phi_0\) through
\(\cot\phi_0=-\mathcal Z_{00}(1;q^2)/(\pi^{3/2}q)\):
\[
  \cot\delta_0(k)=-\cot\phi_0(q)
  =
  \cot\bigl(n\pi-\phi_0(q)\bigr),
  \]
which is equivalent to
\(\delta_0(k)+\phi_0(q)=n\pi\) modulo \(\pi\).  The only physics input beyond
the spectral existence of the two-particle level is the replacement of the
interacting QFT outside the range by the elastic scattering boundary
condition, with exponential finite-volume corrections controlled by the
lightest omitted exchange.  Thus the formula is a reconstruction statement
with explicit hypotheses, not a model of the resonance.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Single- and Coupled-Channel Pole Coordinates}
\label{subsec:qcd-single-coupled-channel-pole-coordinates}

For the single-channel finite-volume pole reconstruction target, assume that,
on an open real energy interval \(I\), a QCD channel is
elastic, has two stable color-singlet particles of masses \(m_1,m_2\), and
has been reduced, by a stated cubic-irrep analysis, to a single partial wave
\(\ell\).  Put \(J=\{E^2:E\in I\}\) and
\[
  \rho_{12}(s)=\frac{2k(s)}{\sqrt s},
  \qquad
  E=\sqrt{m_1^2+k(s)^2}+\sqrt{m_2^2+k(s)^2},
\]
for \(s=E^2\in J\), and use the partial-wave normalization
\[
  S_\ell(s)=1+2\ii \rho_{12}(s)t_\ell^{(I)}(s)
  =\ee^{2\ii\delta_\ell(s)} .
\]
Then the physical-sheet elastic amplitude is equivalently written
\begin{equation}
  t_\ell^{(I)}(s)=
  \frac{1}{K_\ell^{-1}(s)-\ii\rho_{12}(s)},
  \qquad
  K_\ell^{-1}(s)=\rho_{12}(s)\cot\delta_\ell(s),
  \label{eq:qcd-single-channel-kmatrix-definition}
\end{equation}
where \(K_\ell^{-1}(s)\) is real on \(J\).  Each finite-volume energy
\(E_n\in I\) satisfying
\eqref{eq:qcd-luscher-single-channel-condition} determines the real-axis
coordinate
\begin{equation}
  K_\ell^{-1}(E_n^2)
  =
  -\rho_{12}(E_n^2)\cot\phi_\ell(q_n),
  \qquad
  q_n=\frac{k(E_n)L}{2\pi}.
  \label{eq:qcd-luscher-kmatrix-sample}
\end{equation}
If \(K_\ell^{-1}\) and \(\rho_{12}\) have the chosen analytic continuations
to a simply connected neighborhood of a candidate resonance pole and no
additional channel threshold crosses that neighborhood, the corresponding
second-sheet pole \(s_\ast\) is a zero of
\begin{equation}
  K_\ell^{-1}(s_\ast)+\ii\rho_{12}(s_\ast)=0 .
  \label{eq:qcd-single-channel-second-sheet-pole}
\end{equation}

This is the algebraic target of a one-channel finite-volume resonance
extraction, not by itself a proof that the required analytic continuation has
been controlled.  Elastic unitarity in the normalization above says
\(S_\ell^\ast S_\ell=1\) on \(I\).  Hence
\[
  t_\ell^{(I)}(s)
  =
  \frac{\ee^{2\ii\delta_\ell(s)}-1}{2\ii\rho_{12}(s)}
  =
  \frac{\ee^{\ii\delta_\ell(s)}\sin\delta_\ell(s)}
       {\rho_{12}(s)}
\]
and therefore
\[
  \bigl(t_\ell^{(I)}(s)\bigr)^{-1}
  =
  \rho_{12}(s)\bigl(\cot\delta_\ell(s)-\ii\bigr).
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:qcd-single-channel-kmatrix-definition} and identifies
the real coordinate \(K_\ell^{-1}=\rho_{12}\cot\delta_\ell\).  At a
finite-volume level satisfying
\(\delta_\ell(k_n)+\phi_\ell(q_n)=n\pi\),
\[
  \cot\delta_\ell(k_n)
  =
  \cot\bigl(n\pi-\phi_\ell(q_n)\bigr)
  =
  -\cot\phi_\ell(q_n),
\]
which gives \eqref{eq:qcd-luscher-kmatrix-sample}.  Across the elastic
unitarity cut the chosen branch of the two-body momentum changes sign, so
\(\rho_{12}\) changes sign while \(K_\ell^{-1}\), being the real analytic
coordinate fixed on the cut, continues through the same germ.  Thus the
amplitude on the adjacent sheet is
\[
  t_\ell^{(II)}(s)=
  \frac{1}{K_\ell^{-1}(s)+\ii\rho_{12}(s)} ,
\]
and its isolated poles are precisely the zeros of the denominator, giving
\eqref{eq:qcd-single-channel-second-sheet-pole}.

A concrete determination of \(s_\ast\) also contains an analytic representation
or parametrization of \(K_\ell^{-1}\), regulator and volume limits for the
input energies, and separate bounds for neglected partial waves and inelastic
channels.

\begin{lemma}[Coupled-channel \(K\)-matrix determinant and sheet continuation]
\label{lem:qcd-coupled-channel-kmatrix-sheet}
Let \(a,b=1,\ldots,N\) label finitely many stable two-particle
color-singlet channels in a fixed set of conserved quantum numbers, and let
\(\alpha,\beta\) label the partial waves and cubic-irrep components retained
in a finite-volume analysis.  On a real interval below the next omitted
threshold, let \(\rho(s)\) be the positive diagonal matrix with entries
\(\rho_a(s)=2k_a(s)/\sqrt s\), repeated on the retained angular-momentum
indices.  With the normalization
\[
  S=1+2\ii\,\rho^{1/2}t^{(I)}\rho^{1/2},
\]
elastic coupled-channel unitarity is equivalent, on the interval, to
\begin{equation}
  t^{(I)}(s)=\bigl(K^{-1}(s)-\ii\rho(s)\bigr)^{-1},
  \qquad
  K^{-1}(s)^\dagger=K^{-1}(s).
  \label{eq:qcd-coupled-channel-kmatrix}
\end{equation}
Suppose, in addition, that the coupled-channel finite-volume reconstruction
theorem has been established for this channel and written in the same
normalization, so that the finite-volume energies in a cubic irrep
\(\Gamma\) obey
\begin{equation}
  \det\!\bigl(K^{-1}(E^2)+F^\Gamma(E,L)\bigr)=0,
  \label{eq:qcd-coupled-channel-luscher-determinant}
\end{equation}
where \(F^\Gamma(E,L)\) is the real geometric matrix determined by the box,
total momentum, masses, and irrep projection.  In the one-channel unmixed
limit \(F^\Gamma=\rho_{12}\cot\phi_\ell\), so
\eqref{eq:qcd-coupled-channel-luscher-determinant} reduces to
\eqref{eq:qcd-luscher-kmatrix-sample}.  If \(\Sigma\) is the diagonal matrix
whose entry is \(+1\) on a channel kept on the physical branch and \(-1\) on
a channel analytically continued through its unitary cut, the corresponding
sheet amplitude is
\begin{equation}
  t^{(\Sigma)}(s)=
  \bigl(K^{-1}(s)-\ii\,\Sigma\rho(s)\bigr)^{-1},
  \qquad
  \det\!\bigl(K^{-1}(s_\ast)-\ii\,\Sigma\rho(s_\ast)\bigr)=0 .
  \label{eq:qcd-coupled-channel-sheet-pole}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
From \(S^\dagger S=1\) and
\(S=1+2\ii\rho^{1/2}t^{(I)}\rho^{1/2}\), one obtains
\[
  t^{(I)}-t^{(I)\dagger}
  =
  2\ii\,t^{(I)\dagger}\rho\,t^{(I)}.
\]
Multiplying by \(\bigl(t^{(I)\dagger}\bigr)^{-1}\) on the left and by
\(\bigl(t^{(I)}\bigr)^{-1}\) on the right gives
\[
  \bigl(t^{(I)\dagger}\bigr)^{-1}
  -
  \bigl(t^{(I)}\bigr)^{-1}
  =
  2\ii\rho,
  \qquad
  \bigl(t^{(I)}\bigr)^{-1}
  -
  \bigl(t^{(I)\dagger}\bigr)^{-1}
  =
  -2\ii\rho .
\]
Thus \(K^{-1}:=\bigl(t^{(I)}\bigr)^{-1}+\ii\rho\) is Hermitian on the
physical interval, and \eqref{eq:qcd-coupled-channel-kmatrix} follows.  The
finite-volume determinant relation is the stated reconstruction input
expressed in this \(K\)-matrix coordinate.  In the one-channel unmixed
reduction, its zero condition is
\[
  K_\ell^{-1}(E^2)+\rho_{12}(E^2)\cot\phi_\ell(q)=0,
  \qquad
  K_\ell^{-1}(E^2)
  =
  -\rho_{12}(E^2)\cot\phi_\ell(q),
\]
which is exactly \eqref{eq:qcd-luscher-kmatrix-sample}.  Finally, analytic
continuation through a chosen channel cut changes the sign of that channel's
two-body momentum, hence of the corresponding diagonal entry of \(\rho\),
while the \(K^{-1}\) germ is held fixed.  Repeating this sign choice for all
channels gives the matrix \(\Sigma\), the sheet amplitude in
\eqref{eq:qcd-coupled-channel-sheet-pole}, and the determinant pole
condition.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[QCD resonance pole data]
\label{def:qcd-resonance-pole-data}
The resonance pole data in a hadronic channel consist of a channel space of stable
color-singlet asymptotic states, a physical-region scattering matrix
\(S_{ab}(s)\), a specified analytic continuation across specified unitary
cuts, and an isolated pole \(s_\ast\) of the continued matrix or of an
equivalent partial-wave amplitude.  The mass and width coordinates
\[
  \sqrt{s_\ast}=M_\ast-\frac{\ii}{2}\Gamma_\ast
\]
are pole coordinates after a branch of the square root has been declared.
For a broad or overlapping resonance, line-shape parameters on the real axis
are not invariant substitutes for \(s_\ast\).
\end{definition}

This definition is the correct language for the \(\rho\), the light scalar
isoscalar pole usually denoted \(f_0(500)\), many excited baryons, and
near-threshold exotic candidates.  The notation ``tetraquark'', ``molecule'',
``hybrid'', or ``glueball component'' is then a statement about operator
overlaps, pole motion under controlled deformations, large-\(N_c\) scaling,
or residue factorization.  It is not a separate definition of the state.

\begin{definition}[Controlled pole-motion chart]
\label{def:qcd-controlled-pole-motion-chart}
Let \(\eta\) be a real coordinate on a family of QCD-like theories or
regulators whose action, operator definitions, stable-channel spectrum, and
renormalization prescription have been specified for \(\eta\) in an open
interval \(I\).  Examples include a quark-mass coordinate, \(1/N_c\) in a
large-\(N_c\) family, a finite-volume boundary condition used as an auxiliary
probe before the infinite-volume limit, or a coupling to a source that is set
to zero after differentiating.  A pole-motion chart in a fixed set of
conserved quantum numbers consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item a channel space \(\mathcal C_\eta\) of stable color-singlet
  asymptotic states for each \(\eta\), with an identification of these
  channel spaces over the interval where no threshold crossing changes the
  channel list;
  \item an analytic family of continued partial-wave amplitudes
  \(t^{(\Sigma)}_{ab}(s;\eta)\) on a declared sheet \(\Sigma\);
  \item an isolated simple pole \(s_\ast(\eta)\) and residue vectors
  \(g_a(\eta)\) satisfying
  \[
    t_{ab}^{(\Sigma)}(s;\eta)
    =
    \frac{g_a(\eta)g_b(\eta)}{s_\ast(\eta)-s}
    +h_{ab}(s;\eta),
  \]
  with \(h_{ab}\) holomorphic near \(s_\ast(\eta)\).
\end{enumerate}
The derivative \(\dd s_\ast/\dd\eta\), the projective residue vector
\([g_a(\eta)]\), and their behavior near thresholds are coordinates on the
declared chart.  They are not intrinsic labels unless the family, channel
identification, and sheet have been included in the statement.
\end{definition}

\subsection{Near-Threshold Effective-Range Coordinates}
\label{subsec:qcd-near-threshold-effective-range-coordinates}

For a shallow \(S\)-wave bound-state effective-range chart, consider one
stable two-hadron channel with reduced mass \(\mu\), threshold
energy set to \(E=0\), and center-of-mass momentum
\(k=\sqrt{2\mu E}\), where the physical branch has \(k>0\) for \(E>0\) and
\(\operatorname{Im}k>0\) below threshold.  Suppose that in an energy disk
whose radius is large compared with the binding energy but small compared
with the first omitted left-hand or inelastic singularity, the elastic
\(S\)-wave amplitude is represented by the effective-range form
\begin{equation}
  f(k)
  =
  \frac{1}{-a^{-1}+\frac12 r_e k^2-\ii k},
  \label{eq:qcd-effective-range-amplitude}
\end{equation}
where \(a\) is the scattering length and \(r_e\) is the effective range in
this normalization.  If \(f\) has a bound-state pole at
\(E=-B=-\kappa^2/(2\mu)\), with \(\kappa>0\), then
\begin{equation}
  \frac1a=\kappa-\frac12 r_e\kappa^2.
  \label{eq:qcd-effective-range-bound-pole-condition}
\end{equation}
Moreover, near \(E=-B\),
\begin{equation}
  f(E)
  =
  -\,\frac{g_{\rm eff}^2}{E+B}+O(1),
  \qquad
  g_{\rm eff}^2
  =
  \frac{\kappa}{\mu(1-r_e\kappa)}.
  \label{eq:qcd-effective-range-bound-residue}
\end{equation}
When \(1-r_e\kappa\ne0\), the dimensionless coordinate
\begin{equation}
  X_{\rm ERE}
  :=
  \frac{a\kappa}{2-a\kappa}
  =
  \frac{1}{1-r_e\kappa}
  \label{eq:qcd-effective-range-compositeness-coordinate}
\end{equation}
is determined by the low-energy pole and the first two effective-range
parameters.  It is a compositeness coordinate in this one-channel
effective-range chart, not a regulator-independent probability attached to a
QCD eigenstate without the hypotheses above.

The bound-state pole lies on the physical sheet at \(k=\ii\kappa\).  The
denominator of \eqref{eq:qcd-effective-range-amplitude} therefore vanishes:
\[
  -a^{-1}
  +\frac12 r_e(\ii\kappa)^2
  -\ii(\ii\kappa)
  =
  -a^{-1}-\frac12 r_e\kappa^2+\kappa=0,
\]
which gives \eqref{eq:qcd-effective-range-bound-pole-condition}.

Let
\[
  D(k)=-a^{-1}+\frac12 r_e k^2-\ii k.
\]
Since \(E=k^2/(2\mu)\), one has
\[
  \frac{\dd D}{\dd E}
  =
  (r_e k-\ii)\frac{\mu}{k}.
\]
Evaluating at \(k=\ii\kappa\) gives
\[
  \left.\frac{\dd D}{\dd E}\right|_{E=-B}
  =
  \frac{\mu(r_e\kappa-1)}{\kappa}.
\]
Thus
\[
  D(E)=\frac{\mu(r_e\kappa-1)}{\kappa}(E+B)+O((E+B)^2),
\]
and
\[
  f(E)=
  \frac{\kappa}{\mu(r_e\kappa-1)}\frac1{E+B}+O(1)
  =
  -\,\frac{\kappa}{\mu(1-r_e\kappa)}\frac1{E+B}+O(1),
\]
which is \eqref{eq:qcd-effective-range-bound-residue}.  Finally,
\eqref{eq:qcd-effective-range-bound-pole-condition} gives
\[
  a\kappa=\frac{1}{1-\frac12 r_e\kappa}.
\]
Substituting this expression into \(a\kappa/(2-a\kappa)\) yields
\[
  \frac{a\kappa}{2-a\kappa}
  =
  \frac{1}{1-r_e\kappa},
\]
proving \eqref{eq:qcd-effective-range-compositeness-coordinate}.

The calculation is deliberately local.  It does not classify every
near-threshold QCD pole.  In coupled channels, or when the omitted range scale
is not separated from \(\kappa^{-1}\), the residue vector and pole motion of
Definition~\ref{def:qcd-controlled-pole-motion-chart} are the appropriate
coordinates.  A statement that a pole is molecular, compact, hybrid, or
predominantly glueball-like must then be translated into source overlaps,
residues, large-\(N_c\) behavior, or a specified deformation path.

The light pseudoscalar sector has additional structure because chiral symmetry
and the anomaly constrain the low-energy coordinates.  Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-21}
derives the pion effective theory, the Gell-Mann--Oakes--Renner relation, and
the Witten--Veneziano large-\(N_c\) formula for the singlet mass.  The vector
and scalar resonances require the scattering-amplitude language above.

\subsection{Light-Meson Scattering and Roy Coordinates}
\label{subsec:qcd-light-meson-roy-coordinates}

\begin{definition}[\(\pi\pi\) isospin amplitudes]
\label{def:qcd-pipi-isospin-amplitudes}
For equal pion masses let \(s+t+u=4m_\pi^2\) and write the
\(SU(2)_V\)-invariant four-pion amplitude as in
\eqref{eq:pion-scattering-isospin-decomposition},
\[
  \mathcal A_{ab\to cd}
  =
  \delta_{ab}\delta_{cd}A(s,t,u)
  +\delta_{ac}\delta_{bd}A(t,s,u)
  +\delta_{ad}\delta_{bc}A(u,t,s).
\]
The scalar function \(A\) is symmetric in its last two arguments; this is the
Bose symmetry obtained by interchanging the two pions in an equal-mass
initial or final pair while keeping the tensor decomposition above fixed.
The \(s\)-channel isospin amplitudes are
\begin{equation}
  \begin{pmatrix}T^0\\ T^1\\ T^2\end{pmatrix}
  =
  \begin{pmatrix}
    3&1&1\\
    0&1&-1\\
    0&1&1
  \end{pmatrix}
  \begin{pmatrix}
    A(s,t,u)\\ A(t,s,u)\\ A(u,t,s)
  \end{pmatrix}.
  \label{eq:qcd-pipi-isospin-amplitude-matrix}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\[
  T^0=3A(s,t,u)+A(t,s,u)+A(u,t,s),\quad
  T^1=A(t,s,u)-A(u,t,s),\quad
  T^2=A(t,s,u)+A(u,t,s).
\]
\end{definition}

\paragraph{Crossing matrices in the \(\pi\pi\) isospin basis.}
With \(\mathbf T:=(T^0,T^1,T^2)^T\), crossing \(s\leftrightarrow t\) and
\(s\leftrightarrow u\) is
\begin{equation}
  \mathbf T(t,s,u)=C_{st}\mathbf T(s,t,u),
  \qquad
  \mathbf T(u,t,s)=C_{su}\mathbf T(s,t,u),
  \label{eq:qcd-pipi-crossing-matrices}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
  C_{st}=
  \begin{pmatrix}
    \frac13&1&\frac53\\
    \frac13&\frac12&-\frac56\\
    \frac13&-\frac12&\frac16
  \end{pmatrix},
  \qquad
  C_{su}=
  \begin{pmatrix}
    \frac13&-1&\frac53\\
    -\frac13&\frac12&\frac56\\
    \frac13&\frac12&\frac16
  \end{pmatrix}.
  \label{eq:qcd-pipi-crossing-matrix-values}
\end{equation}
The matrices in \eqref{eq:qcd-pipi-crossing-matrix-values} are part of the
normalization of the Roy coordinates used below.
Let
\[
  \mathbf A:=
  \begin{pmatrix}
    A(s,t,u)\\ A(t,s,u)\\ A(u,t,s)
  \end{pmatrix},
  \qquad
  M:=
  \begin{pmatrix}
    3&1&1\\
    0&1&-1\\
    0&1&1
  \end{pmatrix}.
\]
Equation~\eqref{eq:qcd-pipi-isospin-amplitude-matrix} is
\(\mathbf T=M\mathbf A\), and
\[
  M^{-1}=
  \begin{pmatrix}
    \frac13&0&-\frac13\\
    0&\frac12&\frac12\\
    0&-\frac12&\frac12
  \end{pmatrix}.
\]
The exchange \(s\leftrightarrow t\) sends
\(\mathbf A\) to \(P_{st}\mathbf A\), where \(P_{st}\) interchanges the first
two components, and \(s\leftrightarrow u\) sends \(\mathbf A\) to
\(P_{su}\mathbf A\), where \(P_{su}\) interchanges the first and third
components.  Therefore \(C_{st}=MP_{st}M^{-1}\) and
\(C_{su}=MP_{su}M^{-1}\), which gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-pipi-crossing-matrix-values}.  In particular
\(C_{st}^2=C_{su}^2=1\), as required by applying the same crossing operation
twice.

For \(\pi\pi\) scattering, write the isospin partial waves as \(t_\ell^I(s)\)
by
\begin{equation}
  T^I(s,t(s,z),u(s,z))
  =
  32\pi\sum_{\ell=0}^{\infty}(2\ell+1)P_\ell(z)\,t_\ell^I(s),
  \qquad
  t(s,z)=-\frac{s-4m_\pi^2}{2}(1-z),
  \label{eq:qcd-pipi-partial-wave-normalization}
\end{equation}
with projection
\[
  t_\ell^I(s)=
  \frac1{64\pi}\int_{-1}^1
  P_\ell(z)T^I(s,t(s,z),u(s,z))\,\dd z .
\]
In this normalization physical-region elastic unitarity is
\[
  \operatorname{Im}t_\ell^I(s)
  =
  \rho_{\pi\pi}(s)|t_\ell^I(s)|^2,
  \qquad
  \rho_{\pi\pi}(s)=\sqrt{1-\frac{4m_\pi^2}{s}},
\]
below the first inelastic threshold.  The \(S\)-wave scattering-length
coordinates used in this section are
\[
  a_0^0:=t_0^0(4m_\pi^2),\qquad
  a_0^2:=t_0^2(4m_\pi^2).
\]

\begin{definition}[Roy input for \(\pi\pi\) scattering]
\label{def:qcd-pipi-roy-input}
Roy input on a real interval \(J\subset[4m_\pi^2,s_{\rm max})\) consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the pion mass, the isospin amplitudes \(\mathbf T\), and the partial
  wave normalization \eqref{eq:qcd-pipi-partial-wave-normalization};
  \item a domain of fixed-\(t\) analyticity in which twice-subtracted
  Cauchy representations are valid and the boundary values on the right- and
  left-hand cuts exist as tempered distributions;
  \item the crossing matrices \eqref{eq:qcd-pipi-crossing-matrix-values};
  \item subtraction constants \(a_0^0,a_0^2\);
  \item high-energy and high-partial-wave absorptive input sufficient for the
  two subtractions and for the convergence of the partial-wave projections.
\end{enumerate}
The subtraction polynomial projected to partial waves is
\begin{align}
  k_0^0(s;a_0^0,a_0^2)
  &=
  a_0^0
  +
  \frac{s-4m_\pi^2}{12m_\pi^2}\,(2a_0^0-5a_0^2),
  \label{eq:qcd-roy-subtraction-polynomial-00}\\
  k_1^1(s;a_0^0,a_0^2)
  &=
  \frac{s-4m_\pi^2}{72m_\pi^2}\,(2a_0^0-5a_0^2),
  \label{eq:qcd-roy-subtraction-polynomial-11}\\
  k_0^2(s;a_0^0,a_0^2)
  &=
  a_0^2
  -
  \frac{s-4m_\pi^2}{24m_\pi^2}\,(2a_0^0-5a_0^2),
  \label{eq:qcd-roy-subtraction-polynomial-02}
\end{align}
and \(k_\ell^I=0\) for the other partial waves in the twice-subtracted
polynomial.  This normalization fixes what is meant below by the Roy kernels
\(K_{\ell\ell'}^{II'}\).
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Roy projection from fixed-\(t\) analyticity and crossing]
\label{prop:qcd-roy-projection-construction}
Assume the Roy input of Definition~\ref{def:qcd-pipi-roy-input}.  Then, for
\(s\in J\), the real part of each retained partial wave obeys
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Re}t_\ell^I(s)
  =
  k_\ell^I(s;a_0^0,a_0^2)
  +
  \sum_{I',\ell'}\int_{4m_\pi^2}^{\infty}\dd s'\,
  K_{\ell\ell'}^{II'}(s,s')\,\operatorname{Im}t_{\ell'}^{I'}(s').
  \label{eq:qcd-roy-equation-projected}
\end{equation}
More explicitly, if the twice-subtracted fixed-\(t\) representation is written
after crossing the left-hand cut into the form
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Re}T^I(s,t(s,z))
  =
  P^I(s,z;a_0^0,a_0^2)
  +
  32\pi
  \sum_{I',\ell'}(2\ell'+1)
  \int_{4m_\pi^2}^{\infty}\dd s'\,
  R_{\ell'}^{II'}(s,z;s')\,
  \operatorname{Im}t_{\ell'}^{I'}(s'),
  \label{eq:qcd-fixed-t-roy-resolvent-form}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
  k_\ell^I(s)
  =
  \frac1{64\pi}\int_{-1}^1
  P_\ell(z)P^I(s,z)\,\dd z,
  \qquad
  K_{\ell\ell'}^{II'}(s,s')
  =
  \frac{2\ell'+1}{2}
  \int_{-1}^1
  P_\ell(z)R_{\ell'}^{II'}(s,z;s')\,\dd z .
  \label{eq:qcd-roy-kernel-projection-definition}
\end{equation}
The functions \(R_{\ell'}^{II'}\), hence the kernels
\(K_{\ell\ell'}^{II'}\), are determined by the Cauchy denominators, the two
subtractions, the crossing matrices \(C_{st},C_{su}\), and the Legendre
projection of the absorptive parts.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Fix \(t\) in the declared fixed-\(t\) analyticity domain.  The twice-subtracted
Cauchy representation expresses the boundary value of \(\mathbf T(s,t)\) as a
subtraction polynomial plus integrals over the discontinuities on the
right-hand and left-hand cuts.  By crossing, the left-hand discontinuity is
rewritten as a right-hand discontinuity of the crossed isospin vector,
multiplied by \(C_{st}\) or \(C_{su}\) according to which crossed channel has
become physical.  This is the step where
\eqref{eq:qcd-pipi-crossing-matrices} enters; without it the left-hand cut is
not a QCD input in the same isospin coordinates.

For \(s'\ge4m_\pi^2\), expand the absorptive part in partial waves,
\[
  \operatorname{Im}T^{I'}(s',t(s',z'))
  =
  32\pi
  \sum_{\ell'=0}^\infty
  (2\ell'+1)P_{\ell'}(z')\operatorname{Im}t_{\ell'}^{I'}(s').
  \]
Performing the \(z'\)-projection contained in the crossed-channel Cauchy
terms gives the functions \(R_{\ell'}^{II'}(s,z;s')\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-fixed-t-roy-resolvent-form}.  The convergence assumptions in
the Roy input justify interchanging this partial-wave expansion with the
subtracted dispersion integrals on \(J\).

Finally project the resulting fixed-\(t\) formula in the \(s\)-channel:
\[
  \operatorname{Re}t_\ell^I(s)
  =
  \frac1{64\pi}\int_{-1}^{1}P_\ell(z)
  \operatorname{Re}T^I(s,t(s,z))\,\dd z .
  \]
Substituting \eqref{eq:qcd-fixed-t-roy-resolvent-form} and using the
orthogonality normalization already built into
\eqref{eq:qcd-pipi-partial-wave-normalization} gives exactly
\eqref{eq:qcd-roy-equation-projected} with the projected polynomial and
kernel in \eqref{eq:qcd-roy-kernel-projection-definition}.  The explicit
polynomials \eqref{eq:qcd-roy-subtraction-polynomial-00}--\eqref{eq:qcd-roy-subtraction-polynomial-02}
are the projection of the two independent isospin-even subtraction constants;
the \(I=1\), \(\ell=1\) subtraction is proportional to the same combination
\(2a_0^0-5a_0^2\) because crossing fixes the first \(s-4m_\pi^2\) derivative
of the odd isospin amplitude at threshold.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Status of a Roy pole extraction]
A pole extraction from \eqref{eq:qcd-roy-equation-projected} is controlled
only after the high-energy absorptive input, inelastic channels, matching
point, subtraction constants, and error correlations have been specified.
For the \(\rho\), the relevant pole is obtained by continuing the \(I=1\),
\(\ell=1\) partial wave through the elastic cut.  For the light scalar
isoscalar pole \(f_0(500)\), the corresponding continuation is in the
\(I=0\), \(\ell=0\) wave and is especially sensitive to the subtraction
constants and low-energy crossing constraints.  The same logic governs
Roy--Steiner equations for \(\pi K\), \(\pi N\), and related channels, with
unequal masses and additional crossed-channel partial waves changing the
kernel construction but not the Cauchy-crossing-projection logic.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Light-Meson Pole Charts}
\label{subsec:qcd-light-meson-pole-charts}

\begin{definition}[Concrete light-meson pole chart]
\label{def:qcd-concrete-light-meson-pole-chart}
A concrete light-meson pole statement in this chapter consists of a
color-singlet channel, a partial wave, a reconstruction method, and a
sheet-labeled pole or stable mass.  The minimal chart used for the examples
below is:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item \(\pi,K,\eta,\eta'\).  The QCD channel is the pseudoscalar flavor
  sector.  The amplitude coordinate is a stable mass, together with mixing
  coordinates where appropriate.  The controlled route uses chiral effective
  theory matched to QCD, lattice masses, and the anomaly constraints of
  Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-20}.
  \item \(\rho\).  The QCD channel is \(I=1\), \(\ell=1\) \(\pi\pi\).  The
  amplitude coordinate is the second-sheet pole of \(t_1^1(s)\).  The
  controlled route is Roy input or finite-volume \(P\)-wave \(\pi\pi\)
  quantization followed by analytic continuation.
  \item \(f_0(500)\).  The QCD channel is \(I=0\), \(\ell=0\) \(\pi\pi\).
  The amplitude coordinate is a broad second-sheet pole of \(t_0^0(s)\).  The
  controlled route is Roy input with subtraction constants and correlated
  high-energy input.
  \item \(K^\ast\).  The QCD channel is \(I=\frac12\), \(P\)-wave \(\pi K\).
  The amplitude coordinate is the second-sheet pole of the unequal-mass
  partial wave.  The controlled route is Roy--Steiner input or finite-volume
  \(\pi K\) quantization.
  \item \(K_0^\ast\) channel.  The QCD channel is \(I=\frac12\), \(S\)-wave
  \(\pi K\).  The amplitude coordinate is nearby pole data, often broad.  The
  controlled route is Roy--Steiner input with explicit treatment of inelastic
  and left-hand input.
  \item Hybrid or exotic \(1^{-+}\) channels.  The QCD channel is specified
  by a finite operator-source family containing \(q\bar qF\) or Wilson-line
  operators.  The amplitude coordinate is pole data plus source-overlap and
  pole-motion coordinates.
  The controlled route supplies color-singlet finite-volume energies from the
  declared source family and then performs finite-volume scattering
  reconstruction.
\end{enumerate}
The entries are not model assignments.  They are instructions for which QCD
operator sector, partial wave, analytic sheet, and reconstruction theorem must
be supplied before the label denotes a spectroscopic output.
\end{definition}

\paragraph{Linear elastic pole coordinate near a narrow vector resonance.}
Consider a one-channel elastic partial wave in the normalization
\[
  t^{(I)}(s)=\frac{1}{K^{-1}(s)-\ii\rho(s)},
  \qquad
  t^{(II)}(s)=\frac{1}{K^{-1}(s)+\ii\rho(s)}.
\]
Let \(M_0^2\) be a real point in the elastic interval such that
\[
  K^{-1}(M_0^2)=0,\qquad
  A:=\left.\frac{\dd K^{-1}}{\dd s}\right|_{M_0^2}>0,
  \qquad
  \rho_0:=\rho(M_0^2)>0,
\]
and suppose that, in a neighborhood whose size is small compared with the
nearest omitted singularity,
\[
  K^{-1}(s)=A(s-M_0^2)+O((s-M_0^2)^2),
  \qquad
  \rho(s)=\rho_0+O(s-M_0^2).
\]
Then the adjacent-sheet pole in this linearized chart is
\begin{equation}
  s_\ast=M_0^2-\ii\,\frac{\rho_0}{A}
  +O\!\left(\frac{\rho_0^2}{A^2}\,
  \sup |(K^{-1})''|+\frac{\rho_0}{A}\sup|\rho'|\right),
  \label{eq:qcd-linear-elastic-pole-coordinate}
\end{equation}
where the suprema are taken on the same neighborhood.  If the pole is
parametrized by
\[
  \sqrt{s_\ast}=M_\ast-\frac{\ii}{2}\Gamma_\ast
\]
and the pole is narrow enough that
\(|s_\ast-M_0^2|\ll M_0^2\), then
\begin{equation}
  M_\ast=M_0+O(\Gamma_\ast^2/M_0),
  \qquad
  \Gamma_\ast=\frac{\rho_0}{A M_0}
  +O(\rho_0^2/A^2M_0^3).
  \label{eq:qcd-linear-elastic-width-coordinate}
\end{equation}
In the exactly linear and constant approximation the second-sheet pole
condition is
\[
  K^{-1}(s_\ast)+\ii\rho(s_\ast)=0
  \quad\Longrightarrow\quad
  A(s_\ast-M_0^2)+\ii\rho_0=0,
\]
which gives \(s_\ast=M_0^2-\ii\rho_0/A\).  The displayed remainder follows
by substituting
\[
  s_\ast=M_0^2-\ii\rho_0/A+\Delta
\]
into the full denominator and solving once for \(\Delta\) by Taylor's theorem
on the neighborhood where the derivative of
\(K^{-1}+\ii\rho\) remains bounded away from zero.  This is an ordinary
one-complex-variable implicit-function estimate; its small parameters are
the quadratic variation of \(K^{-1}\) and the variation of the phase-space
factor across the pole displacement.

Finally,
\[
  (M_\ast-\ii\Gamma_\ast/2)^2
  =
  M_\ast^2-\frac{\Gamma_\ast^2}{4}-\ii M_\ast\Gamma_\ast.
\]
Comparing the imaginary part with
\(\operatorname{Im}s_\ast=-\rho_0/A+O(\rho_0^2/A^2M_0^2)\) gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-linear-elastic-width-coordinate}; the real part then gives the
stated correction to \(M_\ast\).  The calculation supplies a coordinate
linearization of the pole equation.  It is appropriate for a narrow
\(\rho\)-type vector pole in an elastic window.  For a broad scalar such as
the \(f_0(500)\), the pole coordinate itself is the invariant output and a
real-axis mass-width pair is a secondary chart, if it is used at all.
\begin{remark}[How the chart is used]
For the \(\rho\), one may use the \(I=1\), \(\ell=1\) entry of
Definition~\ref{def:qcd-concrete-light-meson-pole-chart} and, when the
elastic window and narrowness assumptions are adequate, the linear pole
coordinate above.
For \(f_0(500)\), the same one-channel formula is not the correct primary
language: the broad pole is obtained by solving the analytically continued
Roy equations for \(t_0^0(s)\).  For \(\pi K\) resonances the unequal-mass
Roy--Steiner construction above fixes the kinematics and the crossing input.
For near-threshold exotic candidates, the effective-range and pole-motion
charts of Definition~\ref{def:qcd-controlled-pole-motion-chart} and the
shallow effective-range calculation above specify
what is meant by a molecular or compact coordinate.  In every case the QCD
statement is a pole or a stable mass extracted from a declared operator and
regulator setup.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Unequal-Mass and Baryon-Meson Channels}
\label{subsec:qcd-unequal-mass-baryon-meson-channels}

\begin{definition}[Unequal-mass elastic kinematics]
\label{def:qcd-unequal-mass-elastic-kinematics}
Let \(A(m_1)+B(m_2)\to A(m_1)+B(m_2)\) be elastic scattering of two stable
color-singlet hadrons, and set
\[
  s_\pm:=(m_1\pm m_2)^2,\qquad
  \lambda(s,m_1^2,m_2^2):=(s-s_+)(s-s_-).
\]
For \(s>s_+\), define the center-of-mass momentum
\[
  k_s(s):=\frac{\lambda(s,m_1^2,m_2^2)^{1/2}}{2\sqrt s}.
\]
If \(z_s\) is the cosine of the \(s\)-channel scattering angle, the
Mandelstam variables in the physical elastic region are
\begin{equation}
  t(s,z_s)=-2k_s(s)^2(1-z_s),
  \qquad
  u(s,z_s)=2(m_1^2+m_2^2)-s-t(s,z_s).
  \label{eq:qcd-unequal-mass-elastic-kinematics}
\end{equation}
The identity
\begin{equation}
  s+t+u=2(m_1^2+m_2^2)
  \label{eq:qcd-pik-mandelstam-sum}
\end{equation}
is part of the kinematic convention.  For \(\pi K\) scattering one takes
\((m_1,m_2)=(m_\pi,m_K)\).
\end{definition}

\paragraph{Elastic unequal-mass projection.}
In the kinematics of
Definition~\ref{def:qcd-unequal-mass-elastic-kinematics}, a scalar
amplitude \(T(s,t,u)\) with fixed internal quantum numbers has the
\(s\)-channel partial-wave expansion
\begin{equation}
  T(s,t(s,z_s),u(s,z_s))
  =
  16\pi
  \sum_{\ell=0}^{\infty}(2\ell+1)P_\ell(z_s)f_\ell(s),
  \label{eq:qcd-unequal-mass-partial-wave-expansion}
\end{equation}
with inverse
\begin{equation}
  f_\ell(s)
  =
  \frac1{32\pi}
  \int_{-1}^{1}P_\ell(z_s)T(s,t(s,z_s),u(s,z_s))\,\dd z_s .
  \label{eq:qcd-unequal-mass-partial-wave-projection}
\end{equation}
With
\[
  \rho_{12}(s):=\frac{2k_s(s)}{\sqrt s}
  =
  \frac{\lambda(s,m_1^2,m_2^2)^{1/2}}{s},
\]
elastic unitarity in this normalization is
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Im}f_\ell(s)=\rho_{12}(s)|f_\ell(s)|^2
  \label{eq:qcd-unequal-mass-elastic-unitarity}
\end{equation}
below the first inelastic threshold.
In the center-of-mass frame the incoming and outgoing spatial momenta have
magnitude \(k_s(s)\).  The energy of each species is the same before and
after scattering, hence the momentum transfer has zero energy component and
spatial magnitude squared
\[
  |\mathbf k-\mathbf k'|^2=2k_s(s)^2(1-z_s).
\]
With the Mandelstam convention used in this chapter this gives
\(t=-|\mathbf k-\mathbf k'|^2\), proving
\eqref{eq:qcd-unequal-mass-elastic-kinematics}.  The sum rule
\eqref{eq:qcd-pik-mandelstam-sum} follows directly from the definitions of
\(s,t,u\) and the four on-shell conditions.

The partial-wave inversion is the Legendre orthogonality identity
\[
  \int_{-1}^{1}P_\ell(z)P_{\ell'}(z)\,\dd z
  =
  \frac{2}{2\ell+1}\delta_{\ell\ell'}
\]
applied to \eqref{eq:qcd-unequal-mass-partial-wave-expansion}.  Finally the
two-body phase-space density in these conventions is
\(\rho_{12}(s)=2k_s(s)/\sqrt s\).  Applying \(S_\ell^\ast S_\ell=1\) to
\[
  S_\ell(s)=1+2\ii\rho_{12}(s)f_\ell(s)
\]
gives \eqref{eq:qcd-unequal-mass-elastic-unitarity}.

\begin{definition}[Roy--Steiner input]
\label{def:qcd-roy-steiner-input}
Roy--Steiner input for an unequal-mass two-hadron problem consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the masses, exact internal quantum numbers, and invariant amplitudes
  \(\mathbf T(s,t,u)\) in a declared basis of isospin or charge channels;
  \item the crossing matrices relating the chosen \(s\)-channel basis to the
  \(u\)- and \(t\)-channel bases;
  \item \(s\)-channel partial waves \(f_\ell^a(s)\) and crossed-channel
  partial waves \(g_\ell^c(t)\), each with an explicit normalization such as
  \eqref{eq:qcd-unequal-mass-partial-wave-expansion};
  \item a fixed-\(t\), fixed-\(u\), or hyperbolic dispersion domain in which
  the required subtracted Cauchy representations are valid as boundary values
  of holomorphic functions;
  \item subtraction constants, matching points, and high-energy/high-partial
  wave input sufficient to make all projected integrals converge.
\end{enumerate}
This input is a reconstruction coordinate for amplitudes.  It includes the
analyticity, crossing, subtraction, and asymptotic assumptions; QCD supplies
the channel Hilbert spaces and current or hadron matrix elements to which
those assumptions are applied.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Roy--Steiner projection construction]
\label{prop:qcd-roy-steiner-projection-construction}
Assume Roy--Steiner input in the sense of
Definition~\ref{def:qcd-roy-steiner-input}.  Let \(J_s\) and \(J_t\) be real
intervals below the first omitted inelastic thresholds in the \(s\)- and
crossed \(t\)-channels.  Then the retained \(s\)-channel partial waves have
the form
\begin{align}
  \operatorname{Re}f_\ell^a(s)
  &=
  k_\ell^a(s;\mathbf a)
  +
  \sum_{b,\ell'}
  \int_{s_+}^{\infty}\dd s'\,
  K_{\ell\ell'}^{ab}(s,s')\,\operatorname{Im}f_{\ell'}^b(s')
  \notag\\
  &\hspace{2.3cm}
  +
  \sum_{c,\ell'}
  \int_{t_{\rm th}}^{\infty}\dd t'\,
  G_{\ell\ell'}^{ac}(s,t')\,\operatorname{Im}g_{\ell'}^c(t'),
  \qquad s\in J_s,
  \label{eq:qcd-roy-steiner-s-channel-equation}
\end{align}
and the crossed-channel partial waves have analogous equations
\begin{align}
  \operatorname{Re}g_\ell^c(t)
  &=
  \widetilde k_\ell^c(t;\mathbf a)
  +
  \sum_{b,\ell'}
  \int_{s_+}^{\infty}\dd s'\,
  \widetilde G_{\ell\ell'}^{cb}(t,s')\,\operatorname{Im}f_{\ell'}^b(s')
  \notag\\
  &\hspace{2.3cm}
  +
  \sum_{d,\ell'}
  \int_{t_{\rm th}}^{\infty}\dd t'\,
  \widetilde K_{\ell\ell'}^{cd}(t,t')\,\operatorname{Im}g_{\ell'}^d(t'),
  \qquad t\in J_t.
  \label{eq:qcd-roy-steiner-t-channel-equation}
\end{align}
Here \(\mathbf a\) denotes the declared subtraction constants.  The kernels
\(K,G,\widetilde G,\widetilde K\) are the Legendre projections of the
subtracted Cauchy denominators after the crossed-channel discontinuities have
been rewritten with the declared crossing matrices.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Begin with the subtracted Cauchy representation in the chosen
Roy--Steiner domain.  Its discontinuity terms are located on the physical
cuts of the \(s\), \(u\), and \(t\) variables.  The right-hand \(s\)-channel
cut is already expressed in the basis whose partial waves are
\(f_\ell^a\).  The \(u\)- and \(t\)-channel cuts are first moved into their
physical variables and then rewritten in the chosen \(s\)-channel basis using
the crossing matrices included in the input.  This produces a fixed-angle
representation
\[
\begin{aligned}
  &\operatorname{Re}T^a(s,t(s,z_s),u(s,z_s))
  \\
  &\quad =
  P^a(s,z_s;\mathbf a)
  +\sum_{b,\ell'}\int_{s_+}^{\infty}\dd s'\,
    R_{\ell'}^{ab}(s,z_s;s')\,\operatorname{Im}f_{\ell'}^b(s')
  \\
  &\qquad\quad
  +\sum_{c,\ell'}\int_{t_{\rm th}}^{\infty}\dd t'\,
    H_{\ell'}^{ac}(s,z_s;t')\,\operatorname{Im}g_{\ell'}^c(t').
\end{aligned}
\]
The convergence part of the input justifies the interchange of the
partial-wave sums, dispersion integrals, and \(z_s\)-projection on \(J_s\).
Projecting with
\[
  \frac1{32\pi}\int_{-1}^{1}P_\ell(z_s)(\,\cdot\,)\,\dd z_s
\]
defines
\[
  k_\ell^a(s)=\frac1{32\pi}\int_{-1}^{1}P_\ell(z_s)P^a(s,z_s)\,\dd z_s,
\]
and similarly defines \(K_{\ell\ell'}^{ab}\) and
\(G_{\ell\ell'}^{ac}\) as the same projection of \(R_{\ell'}^{ab}\) and
\(H_{\ell'}^{ac}\).  This gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-roy-steiner-s-channel-equation}.  For the \(t\)-channel, use
the crossed-channel angle \(z_t\), the \(t\)-channel partial-wave
normalization, and the crossed basis of amplitudes before projection.  The
same subtracted Cauchy denominators then project to
\(\widetilde G_{\ell\ell'}^{cd}\) and
\(\widetilde K_{\ell\ell'}^{cd}\), while the polynomial part projects to
\(\widetilde k_\ell^c(t)\).  This gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-roy-steiner-t-channel-equation}.  No
additional dynamical assumption enters at the projection stage; all dynamical
input is already contained in the analytic domain, crossing matrices,
absorptive parts, and subtraction constants of the input.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Quarkonium, Baryon, and Hybrid Source Charts}
\label{subsec:qcd-quarkonium-baryon-hybrid-charts}

\begin{definition}[Quarkonium spectroscopy chart]
\label{def:qcd-quarkonium-spectroscopy-chart}
A neutral heavy quarkonium entry is a color-singlet \(Q\bar Q\) spectral
coordinate with flavor \(Q=c\) or \(Q=b\), radial label \(n\), orbital angular
momentum \(L=0,1,2,\ldots\), total heavy-quark spin \(S=0,1\), and total
angular momentum \(J\).  The spectroscopic notation is
\begin{equation}
  n\,{}^{2S+1}L_J,
  \qquad
  L=S,P,D,F,\ldots\quad\hbox{for}\quad L=0,1,2,3,\ldots .
  \label{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spectroscopic-notation}
\end{equation}
For hidden flavor, charge conjugation is an exact quantum number in the
isospin-symmetric QCD-plus-QED-decoupled convention.  The low-lying chart is:
\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\hbox{state type} & n\,{}^{2S+1}L_J & J^{PC} & \hbox{standard entries}\\
\hline
\hbox{pseudoscalar} & n\,{}^1S_0 & 0^{-+} & \eta_c(nS),\ \eta_b(nS)\\
\hbox{vector} & n\,{}^3S_1 & 1^{--} & J/\psi,\ \psi(nS),\ \Upsilon(nS)\\
\hbox{scalar triplet} & n\,{}^3P_0 & 0^{++} & \chi_{c0}(nP),\ \chi_{b0}(nP)\\
\hbox{axial triplet} & n\,{}^3P_1 & 1^{++} & \chi_{c1}(nP),\ \chi_{b1}(nP)\\
\hbox{tensor triplet} & n\,{}^3P_2 & 2^{++} & \chi_{c2}(nP),\ \chi_{b2}(nP)\\
\hbox{singlet \(P\)-wave} & n\,{}^1P_1 & 1^{+-} & h_c(nP),\ h_b(nP)
\end{array}
\]
The entries in the last column are names for QCD spectral levels or
sheet-labeled poles in the corresponding channels.  The chart by itself is
not a potential model.  A prediction of the level \(M_{n\,{}^{2S+1}L_J}\)
requires a regulator or an effective Hamiltonian with a stated heavy-quark
mass scheme, matching coefficients, ultrasoft treatment, and error estimate.
\end{definition}

\paragraph{Quarkonium \(J^{PC}\) rule.}
For a neutral \(Q\bar Q\) color-singlet state in the chart of
Definition~\ref{def:qcd-quarkonium-spectroscopy-chart}, the allowed angular
momenta are
\[
  J\in\{|L-S|,|L-S|+1,\ldots,L+S\},
\]
and the parity and charge-conjugation quantum numbers are
\begin{equation}
  P=(-1)^{L+1},
  \qquad
  C=(-1)^{L+S}.
  \label{eq:qcd-quarkonium-pc-rule}
\end{equation}
The angular-momentum statement is the Clebsch--Gordan decomposition of the
orbital representation \(L\) with the total spin representation \(S\).  For a
fermion-antifermion pair, intrinsic parities multiply to \(-1\).  The orbital
wavefunction contributes \((-1)^L\) under spatial inversion, giving
\[
  P=(-1)(-1)^L=(-1)^{L+1}.
\]
Charge conjugation exchanges the quark and antiquark.  In the center-of-mass
frame this exchange reverses the relative coordinate, contributing
\((-1)^L\).  The spin wavefunction contributes \(+1\) on the spin-singlet
state and \(-1\) on the spin-triplet state after the fermion exchange
convention is included; this factor is \((-1)^S\) relative to the orbital
factor in the standard \(Q\bar Q\) convention.  Therefore
\[
  C=(-1)^L(-1)^S=(-1)^{L+S}.
\]
Substitution gives the entries in
Definition~\ref{def:qcd-quarkonium-spectroscopy-chart}: for example
\({}^1S_0\) has \(0^{-+}\), \({}^3S_1\) has \(1^{--}\),
\({}^3P_J\) has \(J^{++}\), and \({}^1P_1\) has \(1^{+-}\).

Heavy quarkonium uses a different controlled coordinate system.  If
\[
  m_Q\gg m_Qv\gg m_Qv^2
\]
is a useful hierarchy, the pNRQCD Hamiltonian of the preceding sections
predicts the charmonium and bottomonium level spacings through a potential
coordinate, spin-dependent \(1/m_Q\) operators, and ultrasoft corrections.
The spin-averaged levels, hyperfine splittings, and fine structure are then
matrix elements in a stated effective Hamiltonian.  They are not predictions
of a nonrelativistic potential unless the matching coefficients, mass scheme,
and ultrasoft treatment have been fixed as part of the input.  The angular
momentum algebra that turns these matched operators into centroid, fine, and
hyperfine coordinates is the finite-dimensional content of the \(J^{PC}\)
rule above and the spin algebra paragraph.

Baryon spectroscopy is likewise a QCD spectral problem, not a three-body
mechanics problem imposed from outside.  For \(N_f=3\) light flavors, the
lowest baryons organize approximately into flavor \(SU(3)\) octet and
decuplet representations when the quark masses are close.  To first order in
an octet symmetry-breaking Hamiltonian, the octet masses may be written as
\begin{equation}
  M(Y,I)=M_0+aY
  +b\left(I(I+1)-\frac{Y^2}{4}\right),
  \label{eq:qcd-baryon-octet-gmo-chart}
\end{equation}
where \(Y\) is hypercharge and \(I\) is isospin.  This coordinate chart gives
the Gell-Mann--Okubo relation
\begin{equation}
  2(M_N+M_\Xi)=3M_\Lambda+M_\Sigma .
  \label{eq:qcd-baryon-gell-mann-okubo}
\end{equation}
For the decuplet, first-order octet breaking gives equal spacing along the
hypercharge ladder.  These relations are symmetry consequences of a stated
approximation; the actual QCD masses require lattice, dispersive, and chiral
extrapolation inputs.

Assume that first-order \(SU(3)\)-breaking baryon masses are described by
