\eqref{eq:qcd-baryon-octet-gmo-chart} in the octet and by
\(M_{10}(Y)=M_{10,0}+cY\) in the decuplet.  Then
\eqref{eq:qcd-baryon-gell-mann-okubo} holds and
\begin{equation}
  M_{\Sigma^\ast}-M_\Delta
  =
  M_{\Xi^\ast}-M_{\Sigma^\ast}
  =
  M_\Omega-M_{\Xi^\ast}.
  \label{eq:qcd-decuplet-equal-spacing}
\end{equation}
For the octet,
\[
  (Y,I)_N=(1,\tfrac12),\quad
  (Y,I)_\Lambda=(0,0),\quad
  (Y,I)_\Sigma=(0,1),\quad
  (Y,I)_\Xi=(-1,\tfrac12).
\]
Substitution in \eqref{eq:qcd-baryon-octet-gmo-chart} gives
\[
  M_N=M_0+a+\frac b2,\quad
  M_\Xi=M_0-a+\frac b2,\quad
  M_\Lambda=M_0,\quad
  M_\Sigma=M_0+2b,
\]
which implies \eqref{eq:qcd-baryon-gell-mann-okubo}.  For the decuplet the
hypercharges are \(1,0,-1,-2\).  A linear function of \(Y\) has equal
successive differences, giving \eqref{eq:qcd-decuplet-equal-spacing}.

In the large-\(N_c\) limit with \(N_f\) fixed, the baryon operator
\eqref{eq:qcd-baryon-local-source} contains \(N_c\) quark fields.  The
pair-counting argument around \eqref{eq:qcd-large-n-baryon-pair-counting}
gives a mass of order \(N_c\), while collective spin-flavor splittings are
typically \(O(1/N_c)\) in the rotor regime.  This is a controlled limit of QCD
under its own hypotheses, and it explains why baryons require a separate
large-\(N_c\) analysis from mesons.  It does not license importing
constituent-quark spectra as QCD predictions.

\begin{definition}[Baryon-meson resonance reconstruction data]
\label{def:qcd-baryon-meson-resonance-data}
Fix conserved quantum numbers: baryon number one, total isospin \(I\), total
strangeness \(S\), total angular momentum and parity \(J^P\), and any other
exact charges in the chosen QCD mass convention.  A two-body baryon-meson
resonance reconstruction data consist of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item a finite list of stable color-singlet two-body channels
  \(a=(B_a,M_a)\) in the chosen energy window, with baryon mass \(M_{B_a}\),
  meson mass \(m_{M_a}\), spin \(s_{B_a}\), meson spin \(s_{M_a}\), and
  intrinsic parities \(P_{B_a},P_{M_a}\);
  \item a list of retained orbital angular momenta \(L_a\) and spin couplings
  producing the declared \(J^P\);
  \item the infinite-volume partial-wave matrix \(t_{ab}^{J^P}(s)\), with
  phase-space matrix
  \[
    \rho_a(s)=
    \frac{2k_a(s)}{\sqrt s},
    \qquad
    \sqrt s=
    \sqrt{M_{B_a}^2+k_a(s)^2}
    +
    \sqrt{m_{M_a}^2+k_a(s)^2};
  \]
  \item a reconstruction method for \(t^{J^P}\), for example a
  coupled-channel finite-volume determinant or a Roy--Steiner representation;
  \item a sheet label \(\Sigma=\operatorname{diag}(\sigma_a)\), with
  \(\sigma_a=\pm1\), specifying which channel momenta have been continued
  through their unitarity cuts;
  \item pole positions \(s_\ast\) and residue vectors \(g_a\) defined by
  \begin{equation}
    t_{ab}^{(\Sigma),J^P}(s)
    =
    \frac{g_a g_b}{s_\ast-s}
    +h_{ab}(s),
    \label{eq:qcd-baryon-resonance-residue-vector}
  \end{equation}
  where \(h_{ab}\) is holomorphic at \(s_\ast\) on the same sheet.
\end{enumerate}
The invariant content is the pole position, the sheet, and the residue
projective vector \(g_a\), together with the operator and regulator data by
which the amplitude was obtained.  Names such as radial excitation,
molecule, compact multiquark configuration, or meson-baryon bound state are
interpretive coordinates on these data.
\end{definition}

\paragraph{Pseudoscalar-meson--baryon partial-wave quantum numbers.}
Let a positive-parity spin-\(\frac12\) baryon \(B\) scatter with a
pseudoscalar meson \(M\) of spin \(0\) and parity \(-1\).  In a two-body
partial wave of orbital angular momentum \(L\), the allowed total angular
momenta and parity are
\begin{equation}
  J\in
  \begin{cases}
    \{\frac12\},&L=0,\\
    \{L-\frac12,L+\frac12\},&L\ge1,
  \end{cases}
  \qquad
  P=(-1)^{L+1}.
  \label{eq:qcd-pseudoscalar-baryon-jp-rule}
\end{equation}
Consequently an \(S\)-wave channel has \(J^P=\frac12^-\), while a
\(P\)-wave channel has \(J^P=\frac12^+\) or \(J^P=\frac32^+\).
The two-body Hilbert space at fixed center-of-mass momentum decomposes under
spatial rotations as the tensor product of the orbital representation of spin
\(L\), the baryon spin representation \(\frac12\), and the meson spin
representation \(0\).  Therefore the total spin content is
\[
  L\otimes\frac12
  =
  \begin{cases}
    \frac12,&L=0,\\
    (L-\frac12)\oplus(L+\frac12),&L\ge1,
  \end{cases}
\]
which gives the allowed \(J\)'s.  Parity multiplies the intrinsic parities by
the orbital factor \((-1)^L\):
\[
  P=P_B P_M(-1)^L=(+1)(-1)(-1)^L=(-1)^{L+1}.
\]
The \(S\)- and \(P\)-wave cases are the first two values of \(L\).

This elementary representation-theoretic step is often where baryon
resonance nomenclature enters the analysis.  The \(\Delta(1232)\) channel is
the \(I=\frac32\), \(J^P=\frac32^+\) \(P\)-wave \(\pi N\) amplitude.  A
Roper-type nucleon resonance is a pole in the \(I=\frac12\),
\(J^P=\frac12^+\) channel, with residues into the retained \(\pi N\),
\(\eta N\), and multi-hadron channels determined by the chosen coupled-channel
amplitude.  The \(\Lambda(1405)\)-type channel has \(I=0\), \(S=-1\),
\(J^P=\frac12^-\), and its minimal two-body description couples the
\(\bar K N\) and \(\pi\Sigma\) \(S\)-wave channels.  In each case the QCD
statement is the sheet-labeled pole of
Definition~\ref{def:qcd-baryon-meson-resonance-data}.  A finite-volume
calculation supplies color-singlet energy levels through finite source-family
correlators; the pole information is then reconstructed only after a
coupled-channel quantization condition and analytic continuation have been
specified.  A dispersive
calculation supplies it through the corresponding analyticity and crossing
assumptions.

\begin{proposition}[Two-channel sheet continuation and residue vector]
\label{prop:qcd-two-channel-sheet-residue}
Fix a partial wave and an energy neighborhood in which two stable
color-singlet two-body channels are the only open channels retained in the
analysis.  Suppose that, in this neighborhood, the coupled-channel amplitude
admits a \(K\)-matrix representation
\begin{equation}
  t^{\rm phys}(s)
  =
  \left[
    K(s)^{-1}
    -\ii\,\operatorname{diag}\!\bigl(\rho_1(s),\rho_2(s)\bigr)
  \right]^{-1},
  \label{eq:qcd-two-channel-physical-kmatrix}
\end{equation}
where \(K(s)^{-1}\) is a complex-analytic symmetric matrix that is real
symmetric on the physical real interval, and each \(\rho_a(s)\) is the
chosen square-root phase-space branch for channel \(a\).  For a sheet label
\(\sigma=(\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\), \(\sigma_a=\pm1\), define
\begin{equation}
  D_\sigma(s)
  :=
  K(s)^{-1}
  -\ii\,\operatorname{diag}\!\bigl(\sigma_1\rho_1(s),\sigma_2\rho_2(s)\bigr),
  \qquad
  t^{(\sigma)}(s):=D_\sigma(s)^{-1}.
  \label{eq:qcd-two-channel-sheet-denominator}
\end{equation}
Then a resonance pole on this sheet is a zero of
\begin{equation}
  \Delta_\sigma(s):=\det D_\sigma(s).
  \label{eq:qcd-two-channel-pole-determinant}
\end{equation}
If \(s_\ast\) is a simple zero of \(\Delta_\sigma\) and
\(\operatorname{rank}D_\sigma(s_\ast)=1\), then
\begin{equation}
  t^{(\sigma)}(s)
  =
  -\,\frac{\operatorname{adj}D_\sigma(s_\ast)}
          {\Delta_\sigma'(s_\ast)}\,
    \frac1{s_\ast-s}
  +O(1).
  \label{eq:qcd-two-channel-residue-adjugate}
\end{equation}
Because \(D_\sigma(s_\ast)\) is complex symmetric, the adjugate in
\eqref{eq:qcd-two-channel-residue-adjugate} has rank one and can be written
as \(c\,v_av_b\), where \(v\) spans
\(\ker D_\sigma(s_\ast)\).  Thus the projective residue vector in
Definition~\ref{def:qcd-baryon-meson-resonance-data} is the null direction of
the analytically continued denominator, with the overall complex phase fixed
only after choosing a residue normalization.

In the constant local coordinate chart
\[
  K^{-1}=
  \begin{pmatrix}a&b\\ b&c\end{pmatrix},
  \qquad
  \rho_a(s)=\rho_a,
\]
the pole equation on sheet \(\sigma\) is
\begin{equation}
  (a-\ii\sigma_1\rho_1)(c-\ii\sigma_2\rho_2)-b^2=0.
  \label{eq:qcd-two-channel-local-pole-equation}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Equation~\eqref{eq:qcd-two-channel-physical-kmatrix} is the representation
assumed in the proposition.  On the physical interval it is equivalent to the
two-channel elastic-unitarity identity
\[
  \operatorname{Im}\bigl(t^{\rm phys}(s)^{-1}\bigr)
  =
  -\operatorname{diag}(\rho_1(s),\rho_2(s))
\]
on the physical interval.  Analytic continuation through the unitarity cut of
channel \(a\) changes the sign of the square root \(k_a(s)\), hence of
\(\rho_a(s)\), and leaves the other channel branches unchanged.  This gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-two-channel-sheet-denominator}.  Since the matrix inverse is
meromorphic wherever the entries are analytic, its poles are precisely the
zeros of \(\det D_\sigma\), unless the adjugate vanishes to sufficient order
to cancel the zero.  Under the stated rank-one and simple-zero hypotheses,
the adjugate does not vanish, and
\[
  D_\sigma(s)^{-1}
  =
  \frac{\operatorname{adj}D_\sigma(s)}
       {\Delta_\sigma(s)}
  =
  \frac{\operatorname{adj}D_\sigma(s_\ast)}
       {(s-s_\ast)\Delta_\sigma'(s_\ast)}
  +O(1),
\]
which is \eqref{eq:qcd-two-channel-residue-adjugate} after rewriting
\((s-s_\ast)^{-1}=-(s_\ast-s)^{-1}\).  A \(2\times2\) matrix of rank one has
rank-one adjugate; for a complex symmetric matrix the left and right null
directions agree, so this rank-one matrix is proportional to \(vv^T\).  The
constant formula \eqref{eq:qcd-two-channel-local-pole-equation} is the
determinant of the displayed \(2\times2\) denominator.
\end{proof}

This proposition is the minimal algebra behind statements about the
\(\Lambda(1405)\)-type \(\bar K N\)-\(\pi\Sigma\) sector, hidden-charm
pentaquark channels, and near-threshold heavy-meson channels.  The number of
poles, their locations, and their residues are outputs of a finite-volume or
dispersive reconstruction.  The phrase ``molecular'' can be used only after a
specific residue, pole-motion, or source-overlap coordinate has been declared;
it is not an independent QCD definition.

\begin{definition}[Light-baryon spectroscopy charts]
\label{def:qcd-light-baryon-spectroscopy-charts}
Work with baryon number \(B=1\) and three light flavors
\((u,d,s)\).  Let strangeness be denoted by \(S_{\rm str}\), so the
hypercharge used in \eqref{eq:qcd-baryon-octet-gmo-chart} is
\(Y=B+S_{\rm str}=1+S_{\rm str}\).  The ground-state flavor multiplet charts
used below are:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{c|c|c|c|c}
\textbf{multiplet} & \textbf{entry} & \(\mathbf I\) & \(\mathbf Y\) & \(\mathbf J^P\)\\
\hline
\(\mathbf 8\) & \(N=(p,n)\) & \(\frac12\) & \(1\) & \(\frac12^+\)\\
\(\mathbf 8\) & \(\Lambda\) & \(0\) & \(0\) & \(\frac12^+\)\\
\(\mathbf 8\) & \(\Sigma=(\Sigma^+,\Sigma^0,\Sigma^-)\) & \(1\) & \(0\) & \(\frac12^+\)\\
\(\mathbf 8\) & \(\Xi=(\Xi^0,\Xi^-)\) & \(\frac12\) & \(-1\) & \(\frac12^+\)\\
\hline
\(\mathbf {10}\) & \(\Delta\) & \(\frac32\) & \(1\) & \(\frac32^+\)\\
\(\mathbf {10}\) & \(\Sigma^\ast\) & \(1\) & \(0\) & \(\frac32^+\)\\
\(\mathbf {10}\) & \(\Xi^\ast\) & \(\frac12\) & \(-1\) & \(\frac32^+\)\\
\(\mathbf {10}\) & \(\Omega^-\) & \(0\) & \(-2\) & \(\frac32^+\)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The table is a chart of exact conserved quantum numbers and approximate
flavor-\(SU(3)\) organization.  The masses are QCD spectral values obtained
from the color-singlet Hamiltonian or from a regulator converging to it.
Equation~\eqref{eq:qcd-baryon-gell-mann-okubo} and
\eqref{eq:qcd-decuplet-equal-spacing} are first-order coordinates on these
spectral values; they are not definitions of the baryons.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Excited light-baryon channel chart]
\label{def:qcd-excited-light-baryon-channel-chart}
An excited light-baryon entry in this monograph is specified by:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item exact charges \(B=1\), \(I\), \(S_{\rm str}\), \(J^P\), and any
  additional exact discrete quantum numbers of the chosen mass convention;
\item a finite list of two-body and effective multi-hadron channels retained
  in the reconstruction of Definition~\ref{def:qcd-baryon-meson-resonance-data};
\item a sheet-labeled pole \(s_\ast\) of the corresponding color-singlet
  amplitude, or an isolated stable level if the state lies below every open
  channel in the stated volume and mass regime;
\item the residue projective vector into the retained channels, when the
  interpretation of the pole requires an overlap or composition coordinate.
\end{enumerate}
The following entries are the minimal light-baryon examples that must be
carried through any concrete coupled-channel analysis:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
\item \(\Delta(1232)\): charges
  \((I,S_{\rm str},J^P)=(\frac32,0,\frac32^+)\); retained channel
  \(\pi N\) in the \(P\)-wave; QCD output a nearby second-sheet pole of
  \(t_{\pi N,\pi N}^{3/2^+}\).
\item \(N(1440)\)-type channel: charges
  \((\frac12,0,\frac12^+)\); retained channels
  \(\pi N,\eta N,\pi\pi N\); QCD output a coupled-channel pole whose
  radial-label interpretation comes from pole motion and source overlaps.
\item \(N(1535)\)-type channel: charges
  \((\frac12,0,\frac12^-)\); retained channels
  \(\pi N,\eta N,K\Lambda,K\Sigma\); QCD output an \(S\)-wave pole with
  residue data.
\item \(\Sigma(1385)\): charges \((1,-1,\frac32^+)\); retained channels
  \(\pi\Lambda,\pi\Sigma,\bar K N\); QCD output a strange \(P\)-wave pole.
\item \(\Lambda(1405)\)-type channel: charges \((0,-1,\frac12^-)\);
  retained channels \(\bar K N,\pi\Sigma\); QCD output one or more
  sheet-labeled \(S\)-wave poles.
\item \(\Lambda(1520)\): charges \((0,-1,\frac32^-)\); retained channels
  \(\bar K N,\pi\Sigma\); QCD output a \(D\)-wave dominated pole coordinate.
\end{enumerate}
The words ``Roper'', ``\(\Lambda(1405)\)'', and similar labels are therefore
shorthand for entries in this chart.  A lattice calculation supplies the
finite-volume spectrum and operator overlaps; a dispersive or
Hamiltonian-scattering analysis supplies an analytic continuation.  Without
that continuation there is no invariant resonance mass or width.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Heavy-baryon QCD/HQET chart]
\label{def:qcd-heavy-baryon-hqet-chart}
Let \(Q=c\) or \(b\), and consider one-heavy-quark baryons \(Qqq\).  After
the heavy-quark velocity \(v^\mu\) and mass scheme for \(m_Q\) are fixed,
the color-singlet Hilbert-space sector admits an HQET expansion in which the
light degrees of freedom carry angular momentum \(j_\ell\) and flavor
quantum numbers.  The basic entries are:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{p{0.24\textwidth}|p{0.28\textwidth}|c|p{0.23\textwidth}}
\textbf{family} & \textbf{light flavor} & \(\mathbf{j_\ell}\) &
\textbf{\(J^P\) at leading order}\\
\hline
\(\Lambda_Q,\Xi_Q\) & \(\overline{\mathbf 3}\) of light flavor &
\(0\) & \(\frac12^+\)\\
\(\Sigma_Q,\Xi'_Q,\Omega_Q\) & \(\mathbf 6\) of light flavor &
\(1\) & \(\frac12^+,\frac32^+\)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The leading HQET statement is a spectral degeneracy at fixed \(j_\ell\) and
light-flavor representation, before \(1/m_Q\) chromomagnetic terms are
included.  Doubly heavy baryons such as \(\Xi_{cc}\), \(\Xi_{bc}\), and
\(\Omega_{cc}\) are QCD sectors with two heavy fields and one light field.
They may be organized by heavy-diquark variables only after a scale
separation and color-\(\overline{\mathbf 3}\) matching calculation has been
specified.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Near-threshold heavy spectroscopy chart]
\label{def:qcd-near-threshold-heavy-spectroscopy-chart}
Heavy-flavor spectroscopy contains stable baryon sectors and resonance or
near-threshold pole sectors.  The following chart fixes the QCD object before
any model language is introduced:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
\item \(\Xi_{cc},\Omega_{cc}\): exact charges \(B=1,\ C=2\); minimal
  sources \(ccq\); QCD output isolated color-singlet masses when the levels
  lie below the relevant strong thresholds.
\item \(\Lambda_b,\Sigma_b,\Xi_b,\Omega_b\): exact charges \(B=1\) with
  bottom flavor \(-1\); minimal sources \(bqq\); QCD output stable or narrow
  levels organized by the HQET chart above.
\item \(P_c\)-type hidden-charm baryon sector: exact charges \(B=1,\ C=0\)
  with hidden \(c\bar c\); retained channels
  \(J/\psi\,p,\Sigma_c\bar D,\Sigma_c\bar D^\ast,\ldots\); QCD output a
  sheet-labeled baryon-meson pole.
\item \(T_{cc}\)-type sector: exact charges \(B=0,\ C=2\); retained channels
  \(DD^\ast,D^\ast D^\ast,\ldots\); QCD output a near-threshold meson-meson
  pole or bound-state pole.
\item \(X(6900)\)-type sector: exact charges \(B=0,\ C=0\) with hidden
  \(c\bar c c\bar c\); retained channels
  \(J/\psi\,J/\psi,\eta_c\eta_c,\ldots\); QCD output a coupled
  heavy-quarkonium pole.
\end{enumerate}
The entries with \(B=0\) are included because they use the same pole-motion
and effective-range machinery as the baryon-number-one pentaquark channels.
Labels such as compact tetraquark, hadronic molecule, or diquark-antidiquark
are then coordinates on residues, pole motion under quark-mass variation,
large-\(N_c\) behavior, and source-overlap coordinates.  They are not primitive
spectral definitions.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Glueball and hybrid spectroscopy source families]
\label{def:qcd-glueball-hybrid-source-families}
Fix \(J^{PC}\), flavor quantum numbers, and a finite-volume regulator with a
transfer matrix.  A glueball source family is a finite-dimensional subspace
\(\mathcal V_G\) spanned by gauge-invariant pure-glue operators, such as
traces of small Wilson loops or local curvature polynomials after operator
renormalization.  A flavor-singlet meson source family is a subspace
\(\mathcal V_M\) spanned by color-singlet quark bilinears and multi-hadron
operators with the same exact quantum numbers.  A hybrid source family is a
subspace \(\mathcal V_H\) spanned by gauge-invariant sources in which quark
fields are connected by Wilson lines and one or more local curvature
insertions, for example representative operator families of the form
\(\bar q(x)\Gamma\,U(x,y)F_{\mu\nu}(y)U(y,z)q(z)\) after the endpoint and
composite-operator renormalizations are specified.

The QCD spectrum is the spectrum extracted from the full correlation matrix
on the span of these source spaces and their multi-hadron completions.  The
labels glueball, hybrid, and flavor-singlet meson are source-family
coordinates on eigenvectors and pole residues.  They become invariant only
after a supplementary limit or comparison is stated, for example the pure
Yang--Mills limit, the large-\(N_c\) limit, or a declared quark-mass
deformation path.
\end{definition}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Two-state mixing coordinate]
\label{ca:qcd-two-state-glueball-hybrid-mixing}
A two-state mixing matrix is a coordinate on a controlled finite-dimensional
projection of the transfer-matrix problem, not a definition of the QCD
spectrum.  It is admissible only after the source subspaces, the inner
product, the fitting window, and the error made by omitting other levels have
been stated.  Within such a projection, suppose two normalized basis vectors
\(|G\rangle\in\mathcal V_G\) and
\(|M\rangle\in\mathcal V_M\oplus\mathcal V_H\) give the self-adjoint matrix
\begin{equation}
  H_{\rm eff}(x)=
  \begin{pmatrix}
    M_G(x)&h(x)\\
    h(x)&M_M(x)
  \end{pmatrix},
  \label{eq:qcd-two-state-mixing-hamiltonian}
\end{equation}
where \(x\) is a declared deformation coordinate, such as a quark mass or
\(1/N_c\).
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{remark}[Avoided crossing in a two-state spectroscopy chart]
\label{rem:qcd-two-state-avoided-crossing}
In the controlled approximation
\ref{ca:qcd-two-state-glueball-hybrid-mixing}, the two projected energies are
\begin{equation}
  E_\pm(x)
  =
  \frac{M_G(x)+M_M(x)}2
  \pm
  \sqrt{
    \left(\frac{M_M(x)-M_G(x)}2\right)^2+h(x)^2
  }.
  \label{eq:qcd-two-state-avoided-crossing-eigenvalues}
\end{equation}
If \(M_G(x_0)=M_M(x_0)\) and \(h(x_0)\ne0\), the projected levels are
separated by \(2|h(x_0)|\).  Away from degeneracy, a real orthogonal
diagonalization angle \(\theta(x)\) may be chosen so that
\begin{equation}
  \tan 2\theta(x)=\frac{2h(x)}{M_M(x)-M_G(x)}.
  \label{eq:qcd-two-state-mixing-angle}
\end{equation}
\par
The characteristic polynomial of
\eqref{eq:qcd-two-state-mixing-hamiltonian} is
\[
  E^2-(M_G+M_M)E+M_GM_M-h^2 .
\]
Solving this quadratic gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-two-state-avoided-crossing-eigenvalues}.  At \(M_G=M_M\), the
square root is \(|h|\), so the separation is \(2|h|\).  For the angle, write
the rotated off-diagonal entry as
\[
  \frac12(M_G-M_M)\sin2\theta+h\cos2\theta .
\]
Setting it to zero gives
\((M_M-M_G)\sin2\theta=2h\cos2\theta\), which is
\eqref{eq:qcd-two-state-mixing-angle} when the denominator is nonzero.  At
degeneracy the diagonalizing angle is \(\theta=\pi/4\) modulo basis signs.
\end{remark}

The proposition explains why an eigenstate cannot be assigned an invariant
glueball or hybrid percentage from a two-by-two table alone.  The invariant
quantities are the QCD energies or pole positions and the declared matrix
elements.  The percentages are coordinates depending on the finite source
space, normalization, and deformation path.

\paragraph{Heavy-baryon spin average removes the chromomagnetic coordinate.}
Fix a one-heavy-quark baryon family with \(j_\ell>0\).  Suppose that, through
order \(1/m_Q\), the only spin-dependent term in the effective Hamiltonian
on the two-state multiplet \(J=j_\ell\pm\frac12\) is
\begin{equation}
  H_{\rm mag}
  =
  \frac{2\kappa_{j_\ell}}{m_Q}\,
  \mathbf S_Q\cdot\mathbf j_\ell ,
  \label{eq:qcd-heavy-baryon-chromomagnetic-hamiltonian}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathbf S_Q^2=\frac34\) and
\(\mathbf j_\ell^2=j_\ell(j_\ell+1)\).  Then the degeneracy-weighted
spin average
\begin{equation}
  \overline M_{j_\ell}
  :=
  \frac{(2j_\ell)M_{j_\ell-\frac12}
        +(2j_\ell+2)M_{j_\ell+\frac12}}
       {4j_\ell+2}
  \label{eq:qcd-heavy-baryon-spin-average}
\end{equation}
is independent of \(\kappa_{j_\ell}\) at this order.  In particular,
for the \(\Sigma_Q,\Sigma_Q^\ast\)-type doublet, \(j_\ell=1\) and
\begin{equation}
  \overline M_{\Sigma_Q}
  =
  \frac{M_{\Sigma_Q}+2M_{\Sigma_Q^\ast}}{3}
  \label{eq:qcd-sigma-heavy-spin-average}
\end{equation}
has no chromomagnetic \(1/m_Q\) contribution in the stated scheme.

On a state with total spin \(J\),
\[
  \mathbf S_Q\cdot\mathbf j_\ell
  =
  \frac12\left[J(J+1)-j_\ell(j_\ell+1)-\frac34\right].
\]
For \(J_-=j_\ell-\frac12\), this eigenvalue is
\[
  \frac12\left[(j_\ell-\tfrac12)(j_\ell+\tfrac12)
  -j_\ell(j_\ell+1)-\frac34\right]
  =
  -\frac{j_\ell+1}{2}.
\]
For \(J_+=j_\ell+\frac12\), it is
\[
  \frac12\left[(j_\ell+\tfrac12)(j_\ell+\tfrac32)
  -j_\ell(j_\ell+1)-\frac34\right]
  =
  \frac{j_\ell}{2}.
\]
The degeneracies are \(2J_-+1=2j_\ell\) and \(2J_++1=2j_\ell+2\).  Hence
\[
  (2j_\ell)\left(-\frac{j_\ell+1}{2}\right)
  +(2j_\ell+2)\left(\frac{j_\ell}{2}\right)=0 .
\]
The spin-average \eqref{eq:qcd-heavy-baryon-spin-average} therefore cancels
the coefficient \(\kappa_{j_\ell}\) independently of its value.  The remaining
terms are the heavy-quark mass coordinate, the spin-independent light-sector
energy, the kinetic \(1/m_Q\) coordinate, and higher-order corrections.

\begin{remark}[Large-\(N_c\) baryon catalog coordinate]
The large-\(N_c\) baryon discussion preceding
\eqref{eq:qcd-large-n-baryon-pair-counting} gives a second controlled
organization of baryon spectra.  Its invariant inputs are the QCD
Hamiltonian, baryon number one, fixed \(N_f\), and the large-\(N_c\) scaling
limit.  Under the Hartree and rotor hypotheses stated there, baryon masses
have an \(O(N_c)\) common part and \(O(1/N_c)\) spin-flavor splittings.  The
contracted \(SU(2N_f)\) algebra is a leading-order relation among baryon
matrix elements in this limit.  It complements the finite-\(N_c\) spectral
and coupled-channel charts above; it does not replace the QCD pole or
eigenvalue definitions.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Current Matrix Elements and Forward Sum Rules}
\label{subsec:qcd-current-matrix-elements-forward-sum-rules}

\begin{definition}[Nucleon current matrix elements]
\label{def:qcd-nucleon-current-matrix-elements}
Let \(|N(p,s)\rangle\) be an isolated one-nucleon state in the color-singlet
QCD Hilbert space, with \(p^2=-M_N^2\), \(p^0>0\), and spin label \(s\).  In
the mostly-plus spinor convention of Section~\ref{sec:spinor-conventions},
use the same Dirac--Pauli basis as in
Definition~\ref{def:qed-electron-electromagnetic-form-factors}.  For the Hermitian
electromagnetic current \(J_{\rm em}^\mu\), normalized by the flavor charges
of the quarks, define the nucleon Dirac and Pauli form factors by
\begin{equation}
  \langle N(p',s')|J_{\rm em}^\mu(0)|N(p,s)\rangle
  =
  \frac{\ii e}{(2\pi)^3}\,
  \bar u_{s'}(p')
  \left[
    \gamma^\mu F_1^N(k^2)
    +
    \frac1{M_N}S^{\mu\nu}k_\nu F_2^N(k^2)
  \right]
  u_s(p),
  \qquad k:=p-p',
  \label{eq:qcd-nucleon-dirac-pauli-form-factors}
\end{equation}
where \(e>0\) is the elementary charge and
\(S^{\mu\nu}=-\ii[\gamma^\mu,\gamma^\nu]/4\).  The charge normalization is
\[
  F_1^p(0)=1,\qquad F_1^n(0)=0.
\]
The anomalous magnetic moment coordinate is \(F_2^N(0)\), and the magnetic
moment in nuclear magnetons is \(F_1^N(0)+F_2^N(0)\) after the conventional
normalization by \(e/(2M_N)\).

For spacelike transfer set
\[
  Q^2:=-k^2>0,\qquad
  \tau:=\frac{Q^2}{4M_N^2}.
\]
The Sachs coordinates are the linear combinations
\begin{equation}
  G_E^N(Q^2)=F_1^N(-Q^2)-\tau F_2^N(-Q^2),
  \qquad
  G_M^N(Q^2)=F_1^N(-Q^2)+F_2^N(-Q^2).
  \label{eq:qcd-nucleon-sachs-form-factors}
\end{equation}
They are useful Breit-frame coordinates for elastic electron--nucleon
scattering, but the nonperturbative definition is the current matrix element
\eqref{eq:qcd-nucleon-dirac-pauli-form-factors}.  A lattice, dispersive, or
experimental extraction must state the current renormalization, finite-volume
matrix-element method, excited-state removal, and analytic continuation or
fit ansatz used to obtain the functions of \(Q^2\).
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Sachs and Dirac--Pauli coordinates]
\label{rem:qcd-nucleon-sachs-coordinate-transform}
For \(\tau\ne -1\), the coordinate change
\eqref{eq:qcd-nucleon-sachs-form-factors} is invertible:
\begin{equation}
  F_1^N(-Q^2)
  =
  \frac{G_E^N(Q^2)+\tau G_M^N(Q^2)}{1+\tau},
  \qquad
  F_2^N(-Q^2)
  =
  \frac{G_M^N(Q^2)-G_E^N(Q^2)}{1+\tau}.
  \label{eq:qcd-nucleon-sachs-inverse}
\end{equation}
At \(Q^2=0\),
\[
  G_E^N(0)=F_1^N(0),\qquad
  G_M^N(0)=F_1^N(0)+F_2^N(0).
\]
\par
The two equations in \eqref{eq:qcd-nucleon-sachs-form-factors} form the
linear system
\[
  \begin{pmatrix}G_E\\G_M\end{pmatrix}
  =
  \begin{pmatrix}1&-\tau\\ 1&1\end{pmatrix}
  \begin{pmatrix}F_1\\F_2\end{pmatrix}.
\]
The determinant is \(1+\tau\).  Inverting the matrix gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-nucleon-sachs-inverse}.  Setting \(Q^2=0\), hence \(\tau=0\),
gives the stated zero-transfer normalizations.  No model of nucleon
substructure enters this argument; it is only a change of coordinates on the
same current matrix element.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Isovector axial form factors]
\label{def:qcd-nucleon-axial-form-factors}
Let \(A_a^\mu\) be the renormalized isovector axial current, with
\(a=1,2,3\) and flavor generator \(\tau_a/2\).  Between one-nucleon states,
parity, Lorentz covariance, and isospin give the decomposition
\begin{equation}
  \langle N(p',s')|A_a^\mu(0)|N(p,s)\rangle
  =
  \frac{\ii}{(2\pi)^3}\,
  \bar u_{s'}(p')
  \left[
    \gamma^\mu\gamma_5\,G_A(Q^2)
    +
    \frac{k^\mu}{2M_N}\gamma_5\,G_P(Q^2)
  \right]
  \frac{\tau_a}{2}\,
  u_s(p),
  \label{eq:qcd-nucleon-axial-form-factors}
\end{equation}
again with \(Q^2=-k^2\).  The number \(g_A:=G_A(0)\) is the axial charge in
this current normalization.  The induced pseudoscalar form factor \(G_P\)
contains the pion-pole contribution dictated by the chiral Ward identity and
the pion effective theory of Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-21}; beyond that pole,
its regular part is another QCD matrix element.  Thus nucleon axial data are
part of the same ab initio program as the mass spectrum: they are not
defined by a quark-model wave function but by renormalized current insertions
between color-singlet Hilbert-space states.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Stable-current three-point extraction]
\label{prop:qcd-stable-current-three-point-extraction}
Let a reflection-positive finite-volume regulator of QCD on a spatial torus
\(\mathbb T_L^3\) be fixed, with Hilbert space \(\mathcal H_L\), vacuum
\(\Omega_L\), self-adjoint Hamiltonian \(H_L\ge0\), and momentum operators
\(\mathbf P_L\).  Let \(J_{\mathcal R}\) be a renormalized, gauge-invariant
current in a specified operator-renormalization scheme \(\mathcal R\), and let
\(J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}\) denote its spatial Fourier component carrying
momentum \(\mathbf q\).  Choose momenta
\(\mathbf p,\mathbf p'\in(2\pi/L)\mathbb Z^3\) with
\(\mathbf p'=\mathbf p+\mathbf q\).  Suppose that in the two relevant
baryon-number-one momentum sectors there are normalized one-nucleon eigenvectors
\[
  H_L|N,L;\mathbf p,r\rangle=E_L(\mathbf p)|N,L;\mathbf p,r\rangle,\qquad
  H_L|N,L;\mathbf p',r'\rangle=E_L(\mathbf p')|N,L;\mathbf p',r'\rangle,
\]
isolated from the rest of the spectrum in the same quantum-number channels by
positive gaps \(\Delta_L(\mathbf p)\) and \(\Delta_L(\mathbf p')\).  Here
\(r,r'\) label chosen rows in the relevant finite-volume symmetry irreducible
representations; after the \(L\to\infty\) limit these rows are matched to the
usual spin labels.  Let \(\mathcal O_{\mathbf p,r}^\dagger\) and
\(\mathcal O_{\mathbf p',r'}^\dagger\) be gauge-invariant baryon sources,
projected to the indicated momentum and row, and set
\[
  \psi_{\mathbf p,r}:=\mathcal O_{\mathbf p,r}^\dagger\Omega_L,\qquad
  \psi_{\mathbf p',r'}:=\mathcal O_{\mathbf p',r'}^\dagger\Omega_L.
\]
Assume their one-particle overlaps
\[
  Z_{\mathbf p,r}:=\langle N,L;\mathbf p,r|\psi_{\mathbf p,r}\rangle,\qquad
  Z_{\mathbf p',r'}:=
  \langle N,L;\mathbf p',r'|\psi_{\mathbf p',r'}\rangle
\]
are nonzero.  At fixed regulator, assume \(J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}\) is
bounded on the finite-energy subspace generated by these sources; on a lattice
with compact gauge variables and local fermion bilinears this is the ordinary
boundedness statement for the regulated local insertion.

Define the Euclidean two- and three-point functions
\begin{align}
  C_2(t;\mathbf p,r)
  &:=
  \langle\psi_{\mathbf p,r},e^{-H_Lt}\psi_{\mathbf p,r}\rangle,
  \label{eq:qcd-two-point-transfer-matrix-form}\\
  C_3^{J_{\mathcal R}}(t,\tau;\mathbf p',r';\mathbf p,r)
  &:=
  \langle
    \psi_{\mathbf p',r'},
    e^{-H_L(t-\tau)}J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}e^{-H_L\tau}
    \psi_{\mathbf p,r}
  \rangle,
  \qquad 0<\tau<t .
  \label{eq:qcd-three-point-transfer-matrix-form}
\end{align}
Then
\begin{equation}
  C_2(t;\mathbf p,r)
  =
  |Z_{\mathbf p,r}|^2e^{-E_L(\mathbf p)t}
  +R_2(t;\mathbf p,r),
  \qquad
  |R_2(t;\mathbf p,r)|
  \le
  \|\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\|^2
  e^{-(E_L(\mathbf p)+\Delta_L(\mathbf p))t},
  \label{eq:qcd-two-point-gap-estimate}
\end{equation}
where
\(\eta_{\mathbf p,r}:=(1-P_{\mathbf p,r})\psi_{\mathbf p,r}\) and
\(P_{\mathbf p,r}\) is the spectral projection onto
\(|N,L;\mathbf p,r\rangle\).  Moreover
\begin{align}
  C_3^{J_{\mathcal R}}(t,\tau;\mathbf p',r';\mathbf p,r)
  &=
  \overline{Z_{\mathbf p',r'}}Z_{\mathbf p,r}\,
  e^{-E_L(\mathbf p')(t-\tau)}e^{-E_L(\mathbf p)\tau}
  \langle N,L;\mathbf p',r'|
    J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}
  |N,L;\mathbf p,r\rangle
  \nonumber\\
  &\hspace{1cm}
  +R_3(t,\tau;\mathbf p',r';\mathbf p,r),
  \label{eq:qcd-three-point-gap-expansion}
\end{align}
with the explicit bound
\begin{align}
  |R_3|
  \le
  \|J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}\|
  \Big(&
    \|\eta_{\mathbf p',r'}\|\,|Z_{\mathbf p,r}|\,
    e^{-(E_L(\mathbf p')+\Delta_L(\mathbf p'))(t-\tau)}
    e^{-E_L(\mathbf p)\tau}
  \nonumber\\
  &+
    |Z_{\mathbf p',r'}|\,\|\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\|\,
    e^{-E_L(\mathbf p')(t-\tau)}
    e^{-(E_L(\mathbf p)+\Delta_L(\mathbf p))\tau}
  \nonumber\\
  &+
    \|\eta_{\mathbf p',r'}\|\,\|\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\|\,
    e^{-(E_L(\mathbf p')+\Delta_L(\mathbf p'))(t-\tau)}
    e^{-(E_L(\mathbf p)+\Delta_L(\mathbf p))\tau}
  \Big).
  \label{eq:qcd-three-point-gap-bound}
\end{align}
Consequently the ratio
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal R_{J_{\mathcal R}}(t,\tau)
  :=
  \frac{
    C_3^{J_{\mathcal R}}(t,\tau;\mathbf p',r';\mathbf p,r)}
  {
    \overline{Z_{\mathbf p',r'}}Z_{\mathbf p,r}\,
    e^{-E_L(\mathbf p')(t-\tau)}e^{-E_L(\mathbf p)\tau}}
  \label{eq:qcd-three-point-matrix-element-ratio}
\end{equation}
satisfies
\[
  \mathcal R_{J_{\mathcal R}}(t,\tau)
  =
  \langle N,L;\mathbf p',r'|
    J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}
  |N,L;\mathbf p,r\rangle
  +O(e^{-\Delta_L(\mathbf p')(t-\tau)})
  +O(e^{-\Delta_L(\mathbf p)\tau})
\]
as \(\tau\to\infty\) and \(t-\tau\to\infty\), with constants fixed by the
source norms, overlaps, and regulated-current norm above.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The proof is the spectral theorem for the finite-volume transfer-matrix
Hamiltonian.  We give the details because this is the mathematical content
behind the phrase ``extracting a form factor''.  Decompose the source vectors
into their one-particle components and orthogonal remainders,
\[
  \psi_{\mathbf p,r}
  =
  Z_{\mathbf p,r}|N,L;\mathbf p,r\rangle+\eta_{\mathbf p,r},
  \qquad
  \psi_{\mathbf p',r'}
  =
  Z_{\mathbf p',r'}|N,L;\mathbf p',r'\rangle+\eta_{\mathbf p',r'}.
\]
By the assumed spectral gaps, the spectral support of
\(\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\) lies in
\([E_L(\mathbf p)+\Delta_L(\mathbf p),\infty)\), and similarly for
\(\eta_{\mathbf p',r'}\).  Hence
\[
  \|e^{-H_Ls}\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\|
  \le
  e^{-(E_L(\mathbf p)+\Delta_L(\mathbf p))s}\|\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\|,
  \qquad s\ge0,
\]
and the corresponding estimate holds in the primed channel.  Substituting the
decomposition of \(\psi_{\mathbf p,r}\) into
\eqref{eq:qcd-two-point-transfer-matrix-form} gives the leading term
\(|Z_{\mathbf p,r}|^2e^{-E_L(\mathbf p)t}\).  The cross terms vanish because
\(\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\) is orthogonal to the one-particle eigenspace and
\(e^{-H_Lt}\) preserves the spectral decomposition.  The remaining
\(\eta\)-term is bounded by the preceding estimate, proving
\eqref{eq:qcd-two-point-gap-estimate}.

For the three-point function, insert the same decompositions on the sink and
source sides of \eqref{eq:qcd-three-point-transfer-matrix-form}.  The term in
which both spectral projections are one-particle projections is exactly the
first line of \eqref{eq:qcd-three-point-gap-expansion}.  The three remaining
terms contain an excited component on the sink side, on the source side, or on
both sides.  Applying the gap estimate to the side on which the excited
component propagates, and applying Cauchy's inequality together with the
regulated operator norm of \(J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}\), gives the three
terms in \eqref{eq:qcd-three-point-gap-bound}.  Division by the nonzero
leading overlap factor gives \eqref{eq:qcd-three-point-matrix-element-ratio}
and the stated asymptotic error.  Nothing in the argument assumes a constituent
description of the nucleon; the only inputs are reflection positivity,
spectral isolation, a renormalized gauge-invariant current insertion, and
nonzero overlap of the chosen source with the state.
\end{proof}

The continuum nucleon form factors of
Definition~\ref{def:qcd-nucleon-current-matrix-elements} are obtained
from the finite-volume matrix element in
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-stable-current-three-point-extraction} only after
the current-renormalization scheme has been fixed and the regulator and
volume limits have been taken with the chosen state normalization.  A plateau
in a ratio of Euclidean correlators is therefore evidence for the hypotheses
of the proposition in a numerical calculation; it is not itself the definition
of the form factor.

\begin{definition}[Forward Compton amplitude and polarizabilities]
\label{def:qcd-forward-compton-polarizabilities}
Let \(N\) be a stable proton or neutron state of mass \(M_N\) and spin
\(\frac12\).  Work in the nucleon rest frame and let a real photon have energy
\(\omega>0\), direction \(\mathbf n\in S^2\), and transverse polarization
representatives \(\boldsymbol\epsilon,\boldsymbol\epsilon'\) satisfying
\(\mathbf n\cdot\boldsymbol\epsilon
=\mathbf n\cdot\boldsymbol\epsilon'=0\).  The forward real-Compton amplitude
is the on-shell, connected, LSZ-reduced matrix element of two insertions of
the renormalized electromagnetic current \(J_{\rm em}^\mu\), with the photon
coupling and the one-nucleon state normalization fixed by the scattering
chapters.  For a spin state with unit spin vector \(\mathbf s\), define the
scalar forward amplitudes \(f_N(\omega)\) and \(g_N(\omega)\) by
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_{\gamma N\to\gamma N}^{\rm fwd}
  =
  \boldsymbol\epsilon'^{\,*}\!\cdot\boldsymbol\epsilon\, f_N(\omega)
  +
  \ii\,\mathbf s\cdot
  \bigl(\boldsymbol\epsilon'^{\,*}\times\boldsymbol\epsilon\bigr)\,
  g_N(\omega).
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-compton-fg-definition}
\end{equation}
This equation is a definition of the normalization of \(f_N,g_N\).  Let
\[
  f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega):=f_N(\omega)-f_N^{\rm Born}(\omega)
\]
denote the non-Born amplitude after subtracting the one-nucleon pole
contribution, whose normalization is specified in the low-energy expansion
below.  With this normalization the optical-theorem convention for the
absorptive non-Born amplitude is
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Im}f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega+\ii0)
  =
  \frac{\omega}{4\pi}\,
  \sigma_{\gamma N}^{\rm abs}(\omega),
  \qquad
  \omega\ge\omega_{\rm th},
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-compton-optical-theorem}
\end{equation}
where \(\omega_{\rm th}\) is the first inelastic threshold and
\(\sigma_{\gamma N}^{\rm abs}\) is the total real-photon absorption cross
section in the same convention, not the elastic Compton cross section.  The
spin-dependent optical theorem similarly uses the helicity-difference
absorption cross section
\(\Delta\sigma_{\gamma N}:=\sigma_{1/2}-\sigma_{3/2}\):
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Im}g_N(\omega+\ii0)
  =
  \frac{\omega}{8\pi}\,
  \Delta\sigma_{\gamma N}(\omega).
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-spin-compton-optical-theorem}
\end{equation}

The spin-independent electric-plus-magnetic polarizability is the coefficient
of the first non-Born term in the low-energy expansion
\begin{equation}
  f_N(\omega)
  =
  f_N^{\rm Born}(\omega)
  +
  \bigl(\alpha_E^N+\beta_M^N\bigr)\omega^2
  +O(\omega^4).
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-polarizability-definition}
\end{equation}
The Born amplitude is the one-nucleon pole contribution determined by the
charge \(F_1^N(0)\), magnetic moment \(F_1^N(0)+F_2^N(0)\), and the same
Compton Ward identity used in the QED external-state chapter.  Equation
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-polarizability-definition} defines only the sum
\(\alpha_E^N+\beta_M^N\).  Separating \(\alpha_E^N\) from \(\beta_M^N\)
requires either non-forward Compton amplitudes or a background-field
definition with separately specified electric and magnetic external fields.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Baldin sum rule as a forward-dispersion theorem]
\label{prop:qcd-baldin-forward-dispersion}
Assume that the spin-independent forward Compton amplitude
\(f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega)\) is an even function of \(\omega\) analytic in the
complex \(\omega\)-plane cut along
\((-\infty,-\omega_{\rm th}]\cup[\omega_{\rm th},\infty)\), real on the
real interval \(|\omega|<\omega_{\rm th}\), and sufficiently bounded at
infinity so that the once-subtracted Cauchy formula below has no boundary
term.  Then
\begin{equation}
  f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega)-f_N^{\rm nb}(0)
  =
  \frac{2\omega^2}{\pi}
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\operatorname{Im}f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega'+\ii0)}
       {\omega'(\omega'^2-\omega^2)}
  \,\dd\omega',
  \qquad |\omega|<\omega_{\rm th}.
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-compton-subtracted-dispersion}
\end{equation}
If the small-\(\omega\) expansion
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-polarizability-definition} exists and the integral may
be expanded at \(\omega=0\), then
\begin{equation}
  \alpha_E^N+\beta_M^N
  =
  \frac{1}{2\pi^2}
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\sigma_{\gamma N}^{\rm abs}(\omega')}{\omega'^2}\,\dd\omega' .
  \label{eq:qcd-baldin-sum-rule}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Set \(F(\omega):=f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega)-f_N^{\rm nb}(0)\).  By crossing in the
forward channel \(F\) is even.  Apply Cauchy's theorem to
\(F(z)/(z^2-\omega^2)\) on a contour surrounding the two cuts and use the
assumed large-\(|z|\) bound to drop the circle at infinity.  The discontinuity
on the positive cut is
\[
  F(\omega'+\ii0)-F(\omega'-\ii0)
  =
  2\ii\,\operatorname{Im}f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega'+\ii0).
\]
The negative cut gives the same contribution after the change
\(\omega'\mapsto-\omega'\), because \(F\) is even.  The residues at
\(z=\pm\omega\) then give
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-compton-subtracted-dispersion}.  For
\(|\omega|<\omega_{\rm th}\),
\[
  \frac{1}{\omega'^2-\omega^2}
  =
  \frac{1}{\omega'^2}
  +O(\omega^2),
\]
under the stated integrability assumption.  Therefore the coefficient of
\(\omega^2\) in \(F(\omega)\) is
\[
  \frac{2}{\pi}
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\operatorname{Im}f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega'+\ii0)}{\omega'^3}\,\dd\omega' .
\]
Using the optical theorem
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-compton-optical-theorem} gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-baldin-sum-rule}.  The proof shows precisely where the analytic
and high-energy hypotheses enter; QCD supplies the current matrix elements,
while the dispersion relation is an additional analyticity statement about the
real-photon forward amplitude.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Forward spin polarizabilities]
\label{def:qcd-forward-spin-polarizabilities}
Keep the normalization of the spin-dependent forward Compton amplitude
\(g_N\) in \eqref{eq:qcd-forward-compton-fg-definition} and the helicity
difference
\[
  \Delta\sigma_{\gamma N}(\omega)
  :=
  \sigma_{1/2}(\omega)-\sigma_{3/2}(\omega),
\]
where the subscript is the total \(\gamma N\) helicity in the rest frame of
the target.  Let \(F_1^N(q^2)\) and \(F_2^N(q^2)\) be the Dirac and Pauli form
factors in the current matrix element
\eqref{eq:qcd-nucleon-dirac-pauli-form-factors}, and set
\[
  Q_N:=F_1^N(0),\qquad
  \kappa_N:=F_2^N(0).
\]
Thus \(Q_p=1\), \(Q_n=0\), and \(\kappa_N\) is the anomalous magnetic moment
in units \(e/(2M_N)\) in the conventions of this chapter.  The
spin-dependent low-energy theorem fixes the term linear in \(\omega\):
\begin{equation}
  g_N(\omega)
  =
  -\,\frac{e^2\kappa_N^2}{8\pi M_N^2}\,\omega
  +\gamma_0^N\,\omega^3
  +O(\omega^5).
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-spin-low-energy-definition}
\end{equation}
Equation \eqref{eq:qcd-forward-spin-low-energy-definition} defines the
forward spin polarizability \(\gamma_0^N\) once the one-nucleon Born
normalization has been fixed by \(F_1^N(0)\) and \(F_2^N(0)\).  The absence of
a \(Q_N^2\) term in the coefficient of \(\omega\) is part of the low-energy
Ward-identity statement: the point-charge contribution is spin independent in
the forward limit, while the anomalous magnetic moment controls the leading
spin-dependent Born amplitude.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Gerasimov--Drell--Hearn and forward spin-polarizability
sum rules]
\label{prop:qcd-gdh-forward-spin-dispersion}
Assume that \(g_N(\omega)\), after the Compton Ward identity has combined the
\(s\)-channel, \(u\)-channel, and local Born pieces into a function regular at
\(\omega=0\), is an odd function of \(\omega\) analytic in the complex
\(\omega\)-plane cut along
\((-\infty,-\omega_{\rm th}]\cup[\omega_{\rm th},\infty)\), real on
\(|\omega|<\omega_{\rm th}\), and sufficiently bounded at infinity that the
unsubtracted odd dispersion relation below has no boundary term.  Assume also
that the threshold and high-energy behavior allow the first two terms of the
small-\(\omega\) expansion of the dispersion integral.  Then, in the
normalization of \eqref{eq:qcd-forward-spin-compton-optical-theorem},
\begin{equation}
  g_N(\omega)
  =
  \frac{2\omega}{\pi}
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\operatorname{Im}g_N(\omega'+\ii0)}
       {\omega'^2-\omega^2}\,\dd\omega',
  \qquad |\omega|<\omega_{\rm th},
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-spin-odd-dispersion}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{align}
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\Delta\sigma_{\gamma N}(\omega')}{\omega'}\,\dd\omega'
  &=
  -\,\frac{\pi e^2}{2M_N^2}\,\kappa_N^2
  =
  -\,\frac{2\pi^2\alpha_{\rm em}}{M_N^2}\,\kappa_N^2,
  \label{eq:qcd-gdh-sum-rule}\\
  \gamma_0^N
  &=
  \frac{1}{4\pi^2}
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\Delta\sigma_{\gamma N}(\omega')}{\omega'^3}\,\dd\omega' .
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-spin-polarizability-sum-rule}
\end{align}
Here \(\alpha_{\rm em}:=e^2/(4\pi)\).  The sign in
\eqref{eq:qcd-gdh-sum-rule} follows from the convention
\(\Delta\sigma_{\gamma N}=\sigma_{1/2}-\sigma_{3/2}\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let \(\omega\) lie in the cut plane with \(|\omega|<\omega_{\rm th}\).  Apply
Cauchy's theorem to \(g_N(z)/(z^2-\omega^2)\) on a contour encircling the two
cuts and small circles around \(z=\pm\omega\).  The residue contribution is
\[
  \frac{g_N(\omega)}{2\omega}
  +
  \frac{g_N(-\omega)}{-2\omega}
  =
  \frac{g_N(\omega)}{\omega},
\]
because \(g_N\) is odd.  The large circle gives no contribution by
hypothesis.  On the positive cut the discontinuity is
\[
  g_N(\omega'+\ii0)-g_N(\omega'-\ii0)
  =
  2\ii\,\operatorname{Im}g_N(\omega'+\ii0).
\]
On the negative cut, the change of variable \(\omega'\mapsto-\omega'\) gives
the same contribution, because oddness of \(g_N\) makes
\(\operatorname{Im}g_N(-\omega'+\ii0)=
\operatorname{Im}g_N(\omega'+\ii0)\) with the opposite orientation of the
cut.  Combining the two cuts gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-spin-odd-dispersion}.

For \(|\omega|<\omega_{\rm th}\),
\[
  \frac{1}{\omega'^2-\omega^2}
  =
  \frac{1}{\omega'^2}
  +
  \frac{\omega^2}{\omega'^4}
  +O(\omega^4)
\]
under the stated integrability assumption.  Hence
\[
  g_N(\omega)
  =
  \omega\,\frac{2}{\pi}
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\operatorname{Im}g_N(\omega'+\ii0)}{\omega'^2}\,\dd\omega'
  +
  \omega^3\,\frac{2}{\pi}
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\operatorname{Im}g_N(\omega'+\ii0)}{\omega'^4}\,\dd\omega'
  +O(\omega^5).
\]
Substitution of
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-spin-compton-optical-theorem} turns the coefficient of
\(\omega\) into
\[
  \frac{1}{4\pi^2}
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\Delta\sigma_{\gamma N}(\omega')}{\omega'}\,\dd\omega',
\]
and the coefficient of \(\omega^3\) into the right side of
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-spin-polarizability-sum-rule}.  Comparing the linear
coefficient with the low-energy theorem
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-spin-low-energy-definition} gives
\[
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\Delta\sigma_{\gamma N}(\omega')}{\omega'}\,\dd\omega'
  =
  4\pi^2\left(-\,\frac{e^2\kappa_N^2}{8\pi M_N^2}\right),
\]
which is \eqref{eq:qcd-gdh-sum-rule}.  Thus the sum rule is not an independent
model assumption about nucleon structure; it is the equality of two
definitions of the same coefficient, one from the low-energy current Ward
identity and one from the absorptive spectral representation, under the stated
analyticity and boundedness hypotheses.
\end{proof}

The practical hierarchy of spectroscopic control is therefore:
\begin{itemize}
  \item Stable mesons and baryons are isolated color-singlet mass eigenvalues;
  their controlled extraction uses the finite-volume transfer matrix and
  continuum extrapolation.
  \item Elastic resonances are second-sheet poles of partial waves; their
  controlled extraction uses Luscher, Roy, or Roy--Steiner reconstruction.
  \item Heavy quarkonium is a color-singlet \(Q\bar Q\) spectrum; its
  controlled extraction uses a matched NRQCD or pNRQCD Hamiltonian and
  lattice checks.
  \item Hybrids and glueballs are operator-overlap sectors and pole data; their
  controlled extraction uses declared color-singlet source families,
  finite-volume energies or scattering amplitudes, large-\(N_c\) scaling, and
  mixing analysis.
  \item Exotic near-threshold states are poles plus residues in coupled
  channels; their controlled extraction uses finite-volume coupled-channel
  amplitudes.
\end{itemize}
Every entry in this list is a statement about QCD observables.  The words
``quark model'', ``molecule'', ``diquark'', and ``flux-tube excitation'' may
summarize patterns in a chosen coordinate system, but the monograph treats
them as derived interpretations only after the corresponding spectral or pole
input has been defined.

\section{Euclidean Current Sum Rules and Borel Windows}
\label{sec:qcd-current-sum-rules-borel-windows}

QCD current sum rules are linear identities for gauge-invariant current
correlators.  Their mathematical core consists of a spectral representation, a
spacelike OPE, and a chosen linear functional that suppresses subtraction
constants and weights different parts of the spectrum.  A finite-parameter
spectral ansatz is an additional approximation layer, whose status is fixed by
the error estimates stated below.

Let \(J(x)\) be a renormalized local color-singlet operator with fixed
quantum numbers, for example \(J=\bar q\Gamma q\),
\(\operatorname{tr}F_{\mu\nu}F^{\mu\nu}\), or a baryonic color singlet.  In
Euclidean momentum notation \(Q^2>0\), define the connected two-point
function
\begin{equation}
  \Pi_J(Q^2;\mu)
  :=
  \int_{\mathbb R^4}\dd^4x\,
  \ee^{\ii Q\cdot x}
  \langle J(x)J^\dagger(0)\rangle_{\rm conn,\mu},
  \qquad Q^2:=Q_\mu Q_\mu .
  \label{eq:qcd-euclidean-current-correlator}
\end{equation}
When \(J\) carries Lorentz indices, \(\Pi_J\) denotes one scalar invariant
after projecting onto a specified tensor structure.  Positivity of the
Euclidean correlator for \(J^\dagger J\) gives a positive spectral measure in
channels where reflection positivity applies.  With enough subtractions, the
spacelike correlator has the form
\begin{equation}
  \Pi_J(Q^2;\mu)
  =
  P_N(Q^2;\mu)
  +
  \int_{s_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\rho_J(s;\mu)}{s+Q^2}\,\dd s ,
  \label{eq:qcd-current-dispersion-subtracted}
\end{equation}
where \(P_N\) is a polynomial fixed by the subtraction convention,
\(s_{\rm th}\) is the lowest physical threshold in the channel, and
\(\rho_J\) is the spectral density associated with the same current
normalization.  Equation~\eqref{eq:qcd-current-dispersion-subtracted} is a
dispersion representation of a color-singlet Wightman distribution.

At large spacelike \(Q^2\), the current product has an operator-product
expansion
\begin{equation}
  \Pi_J(Q^2;\mu)
  \sim
  \sum_a C_{J,a}(Q^2,\mu)\,
  \langle \mathcal O_a(0;\mu)\rangle ,
  \qquad Q^2\to+\infty ,
  \label{eq:qcd-current-correlator-ope}
\end{equation}
with local gauge-invariant operators \(\mathcal O_a\) of increasing dimension
and Wilson coefficients \(C_{J,a}\).  The symbol \(\sim\) means an asymptotic
expansion in a specified sector of the spacelike \(Q^2\)-plane, after the
renormalization scheme and operator basis have been fixed.  Vacuum
expectation values such as \(\langle\bar q q\rangle_\mu\) or
\(\langle\operatorname{tr}F^2\rangle_\mu\) are scheme-dependent coordinates of
the vacuum state.  They become physical only through the full renormalized
combination in a specified observable.

\begin{definition}[Borel--Laplace sum-rule functional]
\label{def:qcd-borel-laplace-sum-rule-functional}
For a function \(F(Q^2)\) whose large-\(Q^2\) behavior permits the limit, set
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal B_{M^2}[F]
  :=
  \lim_{\substack{n,Q^2\to\infty\\ Q^2/n=M^2}}
  \frac{(Q^2)^n}{(n-1)!}
  \left(-\frac{\dd}{\dd Q^2}\right)^n F(Q^2),
  \qquad M^2>0 .
  \label{eq:qcd-borel-transform-definition}
\end{equation}
The positive parameter \(M^2\) is the Borel or Laplace scale.  The associated
sum-rule coordinate is
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal S_J(M^2;\mu)
  :=
  \mathcal B_{M^2}\Pi_J
  =
  \frac1{M^2}\int_{s_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \ee^{-s/M^2}\rho_J(s;\mu)\,\dd s ,
  \label{eq:qcd-borel-spectral-coordinate}
\end{equation}
provided the Borel transform can be interchanged with the spectral integral.
\end{definition}

\paragraph{Borel transform of the subtracted dispersion kernel.}
The functional in Definition~\ref{def:qcd-borel-laplace-sum-rule-functional}
annihilates every polynomial in \(Q^2\).  For \(s\ge0\),
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal B_{M^2}\!\left[\frac1{s+Q^2}\right]
  =
  \frac1{M^2}\ee^{-s/M^2}.
  \label{eq:qcd-borel-kernel-result}
\end{equation}
For an integer \(m\ge1\),
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal B_{M^2}\!\left[(Q^2)^{-m}\right]
  =
  \frac{1}{(m-1)!\,(M^2)^m}.
  \label{eq:qcd-borel-inverse-power-result}
\end{equation}
If \(F(Q^2)\) is a polynomial of degree \(d\), then
\((-\partial_{Q^2})^nF=0\) for \(n>d\), so
\(\mathcal B_{M^2}F=0\).  For the dispersion kernel,
\[
  \left(-\frac{\dd}{\dd Q^2}\right)^n\frac1{s+Q^2}
  =
  \frac{n!}{(s+Q^2)^{n+1}}.
\]
Putting \(Q^2=nM^2\) gives
\[
  \frac{(Q^2)^n}{(n-1)!}
  \frac{n!}{(s+Q^2)^{n+1}}
  =
  \frac1{M^2}
  \left(1+\frac{s}{nM^2}\right)^{-n-1}
  \longrightarrow
  \frac1{M^2}\ee^{-s/M^2}.
\]
For \((Q^2)^{-m}\),
\[
  \left(-\frac{\dd}{\dd Q^2}\right)^n(Q^2)^{-m}
  =
  \frac{\Gamma(m+n)}{\Gamma(m)}(Q^2)^{-m-n}.
\]
The Borel expression is therefore
\[
  \frac{\Gamma(m+n)}{\Gamma(m)\Gamma(n)}
  (nM^2)^{-m}.
\]
Since \(\Gamma(n+m)/\Gamma(n)=n^m(1+O(n^{-1}))\) for fixed integer \(m\), the
limit is \eqref{eq:qcd-borel-inverse-power-result}.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[QCD Borel sum-rule window]
\label{ca:qcd-borel-sum-rule-window}
A Borel sum-rule analysis in a channel \(J\) consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item a renormalized current \(J\), tensor projection, and scheme at scale
  \(\mu\);
  \item a truncated OPE
  \(\Pi_J^{(D_{\max})}(Q^2;\mu)\) with a stated estimate for the omitted
  operator dimensions and perturbative orders after applying
  \(\mathcal B_{M^2}\);
  \item a spectral ansatz for \(\rho_J\), often a low-energy part with finitely
  many parameters plus a perturbative continuum above a threshold \(s_0\);
  \item a nonempty interval \(M^2\in[M_{\min}^2,M_{\max}^2]\) on which the
  omitted-OPE estimate and the spectral-tail estimate are both controlled.
\end{enumerate}
Only the equality
\eqref{eq:qcd-borel-spectral-coordinate} with the exact \(\rho_J\) is a
consequence of the dispersion representation and the Borel transform.  The
finite-parameter extraction of a mass, residue, or coupling is a controlled
approximation only after the spectral ansatz and the two error estimates above
have been supplied.
\end{controlledapproximation}

For a single isolated stable state in the channel, the spectral measure has an
atom \(Z_R\delta(s-m_R^2)\).  If the remaining spectral weight is represented
by a continuum model \(\rho_{\rm cont}(s)\), then
\eqref{eq:qcd-borel-spectral-coordinate} becomes
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal S_J(M^2)
  =
  \frac{Z_R}{M^2}\ee^{-m_R^2/M^2}
  +
  \frac1{M^2}\int_{s_{\rm cont}}^\infty
  \ee^{-s/M^2}\rho_{\rm cont}(s)\,\dd s .
  \label{eq:qcd-single-pole-plus-continuum-borel}
\end{equation}
The common pole-plus-continuum model sets
\(\rho_{\rm cont}(s)\) equal to a perturbative spectral density above a
fit threshold \(s_0\).  Its validity is an empirical and analytic control
question about the exact spectral measure, judged by stability under \(M^2\),
\(s_0\), current choice, OPE truncation, and comparison with regulator
observables such as lattice spectra.

For a finite retained spectral model
\[
  \mathcal S(\tau)=\sum_{r=1}^N Z_r e^{-\tau m_r^2},
  \qquad
  Z_r>0,\quad \tau:=1/M^2 .
\]
the logarithmic derivative used as a mass estimator is
\begin{equation}
  -\frac{\dd}{\dd\tau}\log\mathcal S(\tau)
  =
  \frac{\sum_r Z_r m_r^2 e^{-\tau m_r^2}}
       {\sum_r Z_r e^{-\tau m_r^2}} .
  \label{eq:qcd-borel-effective-mass-weighted-average}
\end{equation}
because the numerator is \(-\mathcal S'(\tau)\).  The right side is a
normalized average with positive weights \(Z_r e^{-\tau m_r^2}\).  It equals
\(m_R^2\) for a single retained atom and otherwise averages the squared masses
present in the retained spectral model.

Thus a Borel plateau diagnoses the weighted average in
\eqref{eq:qcd-borel-effective-mass-weighted-average} changes slowly over the
chosen interval after the declared continuum subtraction and OPE truncation.
Single-state dominance is a further spectral statement about the retained
model.  The object being computed remains the current correlator
\eqref{eq:qcd-euclidean-current-correlator}; the extracted spectral parameters
inherit all assumptions of the Borel window.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Duality and stability gate for SVZ extractions]
\label{ca:qcd-svz-duality-stability-gate}
Set \(\tau=1/M^2\).  After choosing a continuum threshold \(s_0\), the
continuum-subtracted OPE moments used to quote a hadron mass are
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal L_k^{(D_{\max})}(\tau,s_0)
  =
  \int_{s_{\rm th}}^{s_0}
  s^k \ee^{-\tau s}\rho_J^{\rm pert}(s;\mu)\,\dd s
  +
  \mathcal C_k^{(D_{\max})}(\tau,\mu),
  \qquad k=0,1,\dots ,
  \label{eq:qcd-svz-continuum-subtracted-moments}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal C_k^{(D_{\max})}\) denotes the Borel-transformed power
corrections retained in the declared OPE truncation.  The quoted effective
mass coordinate is
\begin{equation}
  m_{\rm eff}^2(\tau,s_0)
  :=
  \frac{\mathcal L_1^{(D_{\max})}(\tau,s_0)}
       {\mathcal L_0^{(D_{\max})}(\tau,s_0)} .
  \label{eq:qcd-svz-effective-mass-coordinate}
\end{equation}
A nonempty SVZ window is accepted only after the following finite controls are
declared on the same rectangle
\((\tau,s_0)\in I_\tau\times I_{s_0}\):
\begin{enumerate}
  \item \(\mathcal L_0^{(D_{\max})}>0\), together with a stated bound for any
  loss of positivity caused by truncating a positive exact spectral measure;
  \item an OPE-tail bound for the omitted operator dimensions and perturbative
  orders in the Borel-transformed moments;
  \item a continuum-duality remainder comparing the exact spectral weight above
  and near \(s_0\) with the perturbative continuum model in the same moments;
  \item a threshold-sensitivity budget for the allowed variation of \(s_0\);
  \item a plateau-slope budget in \(\tau\), interpreted as a spectral-width
  test rather than as a proof of a pole by itself.
\end{enumerate}
For the last two entries the finite formulas are part of the control.  If the
power terms are independent of \(s_0\), then
\begin{equation}
  \partial_{s_0}m_{\rm eff}^2
  =
  \frac{\ee^{-\tau s_0}\rho_J^{\rm pert}(s_0;\mu)}
       {\mathcal L_0^{(D_{\max})}(\tau,s_0)}
  \left(s_0-m_{\rm eff}^2(\tau,s_0)\right).
  \label{eq:qcd-svz-threshold-sensitivity}
\end{equation}
Thus a plateau obtained only by retuning \(s_0\) is not a stable mass
extraction; it has used the continuum threshold as an additional dynamical
fit coordinate.  If the retained moment is the Borel transform of a positive
spectral measure, with
\(\mathcal L_k=\int s^k e^{-\tau s}\dd\mu(s)\), then
\begin{equation}
  -\partial_\tau
  \left(\frac{\mathcal L_1}{\mathcal L_0}\right)
  =
  \frac{\mathcal L_2\mathcal L_0-\mathcal L_1^2}{\mathcal L_0^2}
  =
  \operatorname{Var}_{\tau}(s)
  \ge 0 .
  \label{eq:qcd-svz-plateau-variance}
\end{equation}
Flatness therefore measures the variance of the retained spectral distribution,
plus the declared OPE, continuum, threshold, and regulator remainders.  It is
not an independent argument for single-state dominance.

The pole-plus-continuum language has a precise finite form.  Suppose the exact
low-energy moment in the window can be decomposed as
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal L_0^{\rm exact}
  =
  F_H\ee^{-\tau m_H^2}+R_0,
  \qquad
  \mathcal L_1^{\rm exact}
  =
  F_H m_H^2\ee^{-\tau m_H^2}+R_1 ,
  \label{eq:qcd-svz-pole-remainder-moments}
\end{equation}
with \(F_H>0\).  If
\(F_H\ee^{-\tau m_H^2}>|R_0|\), then the exact logarithmic estimator obeys
\begin{equation}
  \left|
  \frac{\mathcal L_1^{\rm exact}}{\mathcal L_0^{\rm exact}}
  -m_H^2
  \right|
  \le
  \frac{|R_1|+m_H^2|R_0|}
       {F_H\ee^{-\tau m_H^2}-|R_0|}.
  \label{eq:qcd-svz-pole-remainder-bound}
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:qcd-svz-pole-remainder-bound} is the finite version of the
usual ``ground-state dominance'' sentence.  Without such a remainder bound, a
small visual slope in \(M^2\) is only a property of the chosen ansatz and
threshold, not a controlled QCD statement about the hadron spectrum.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Two-scale SVZ extraction window]
\label{ca:qcd-svz-two-scale-extraction-window}
The preceding gate becomes an extraction, rather than a set of local
diagnostics, only after the error components are propagated to the quoted
spectral coordinate.  Let
\(\Delta_k^{\rm win}(\tau,s_0)\) denote the aggregate difference between the
exact low-energy moment and the retained continuum-subtracted OPE moment:
\begin{equation}
  \widehat{\mathcal L}_k(\tau,s_0)
  =
  \mathcal L_k^{(D_{\max})}(\tau,s_0)
  +
  \Delta_k^{\rm win}(\tau,s_0),
  \qquad k=0,1 .
  \label{eq:qcd-svz-window-moment-residuals}
\end{equation}
Here \(\Delta_k^{\rm win}\) includes the omitted OPE tail, perturbative
truncation, continuum-duality error near the threshold, regulator or finite
volume residue, and any positivity defect introduced by using a truncated
coordinate for a positive spectral measure.  If
\(\mathcal L_0^{(D_{\max})}>|\Delta_0^{\rm win}|\), then the exact and
retained mass estimators obey
\begin{equation}
  \left|
  \frac{\widehat{\mathcal L}_1}{\widehat{\mathcal L}_0}
  -
  \frac{\mathcal L_1^{(D_{\max})}}{\mathcal L_0^{(D_{\max})}}
  \right|
  \le
  \frac{
    |\Delta_1^{\rm win}|
    +
    |m_{\rm eff}^2|\,|\Delta_0^{\rm win}|
  }{
    \mathcal L_0^{(D_{\max})}-|\Delta_0^{\rm win}|
  } .
  \label{eq:qcd-svz-window-mass-residual-bound}
\end{equation}
Indeed, subtracting the two quotients gives
\((\Delta_1^{\rm win}-m_{\rm eff}^2\Delta_0^{\rm win})/
(\mathcal L_0^{(D_{\max})}+\Delta_0^{\rm win})\).  Thus the \(k=0\)
moment error is as important as the \(k=1\) moment error: changing the
normalization denominator moves the logarithmic mass even when the first
moment error vanishes.

Choose a reference squared scale \(\Lambda_J^2\) for the channel and local
half-widths \(h_\tau,h_s\) inside the proposed rectangle
\(I_\tau\times I_{s_0}\).  A finite two-scale window score may be taken to be
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \mathfrak E_{\rm SVZ}
  :=
  \sup_{I_\tau\times I_{s_0}}
  \Bigg[
  &\frac{
    |\Delta_1^{\rm win}|
    +
    |m_{\rm eff}^2|\,|\Delta_0^{\rm win}|
  }{
    \bigl(\mathcal L_0^{(D_{\max})}-|\Delta_0^{\rm win}|\bigr)\Lambda_J^2
  }
\\
  &+
  \frac{h_\tau|\partial_\tau m_{\rm eff}^2|}{\Lambda_J^2}
  +
  \frac{h_s|\partial_{s_0}m_{\rm eff}^2|}{\Lambda_J^2}
  +
  \eta_{\rm pos}
  \Bigg],
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:qcd-svz-two-scale-window-score}
\end{equation}
where \(\eta_{\rm pos}\) records any normalized loss of positivity in the
retained moment.  The exact choice of norm is part of the analysis, but it
must have this structure: the OPE and continuum remainders are propagated
through the quotient, and the two independent window directions are tested
separately.  A quoted mass coordinate is then a pair consisting of a central
point \((\tau_\ast,s_{0,\ast})\) and an uncertainty budget dominated by
\(\Lambda_J^2\mathfrak E_{\rm SVZ}\), not just the value read from a graph.

This two-scale requirement rules out a common false plateau.  If the threshold
is allowed to move with \(\tau\), then along a chosen graph \(s_0=s_0(\tau)\)
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd}{\dd\tau}
  m_{\rm eff}^2(\tau,s_0(\tau))
  =
  \partial_\tau m_{\rm eff}^2
  +
  s_0'(\tau)\,\partial_{s_0}m_{\rm eff}^2 .
  \label{eq:qcd-svz-retuned-threshold-total-derivative}
\end{equation}
Whenever \(\partial_{s_0}m_{\rm eff}^2\ne0\), one can locally choose
\(s_0'=-(\partial_\tau m_{\rm eff}^2)/
(\partial_{s_0}m_{\rm eff}^2)\) and make the displayed derivative vanish.
Flatness along that retuned path is therefore not an independent physical
stability criterion.  It is acceptable only if the allowed threshold motion is
fixed by external spectral information and its contribution is included in
\eqref{eq:qcd-svz-two-scale-window-score}; otherwise the continuum threshold
has been used to absorb the same spectral information the sum rule was meant
to extract.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\section{Detector Observables and Energy Correlators}

A nonperturbative formulation of high-energy QCD final states begins with
detector measurements in the physical Hilbert space.  The calorimetric
observable is built from the renormalized, gauge-invariant stress tensor
\(T^{\mu\nu}\), whose normalization is fixed by the translation generators:
\[
  P^\nu=\int_{\R^3}\dd^3x\,T^{0\nu}(t,\mathbf x)
\]
on the common domain of finite-energy states where the integral is defined as
a quadratic form.

\begin{construction}[Energy-flow detector from the stress tensor]
\label{cons:qcd-energy-flow-detector}
For a real test function \(f\in C^\infty(S^2)\), define the formal
null-infinity flux quadratic form by
\begin{equation}
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(f)
  =
  \mathrm{w}\!-\!\lim_{R\to\infty}
  R^2
  \int_{-\infty}^{\infty}\dd t
  \int_{S^2}\dd\Omega(\mathbf n)\,
  f(\mathbf n)\,
  n_i\,\widehat T^{0i}(t,R\mathbf n).
  \label{eq:energy-flow-operator-smeared}
\end{equation}
The notation means that the limit is first tested between finite-energy
physical states.  The operation is part of the detector definition only after
the domain and closure properties below have been supplied.
\end{construction}

\begin{hypothesis}[Detector existence and self-adjointness]
\label{hyp:qcd-energy-flow-detector}
There is a dense scattering domain
\(\mathcal D_{\rm det}\subset\Hilb_{\rm phys}\), stable under finite products
of the smeared detector forms used below, such that for every real
\(f\in C^\infty(S^2)\) the weak limit
\eqref{eq:energy-flow-operator-smeared} exists on
\(\mathcal D_{\rm det}\), is symmetric there, and has a unique self-adjoint
closure.  For each pair \(\Psi,\Phi\in\mathcal D_{\rm det}\), the map
\[
  f\longmapsto
  \bra{\Psi}\widehat{\mathcal E}(f)\ket{\Phi}
\]
is a distribution of finite order on \(S^2\).  The constant test function
satisfies
\[
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(1)=H_{\mathrm{out}}
\]
on outgoing scattering states, where \(H_{\mathrm{out}}\) is the outgoing
Hamiltonian restricted to the physical scattering Hilbert space.  Finally,
for every angular patch \(U\subset S^2\), the quadratic form obtained by
testing \(\widehat{\mathcal E}(f)\) with \(\operatorname{supp}f\subset U\)
is the \(R\to\infty\) limit of a family of complete null-generator energy
integrals with nonnegative transverse smearings whenever \(f\ge0\).  This
last clause is the geometric detector/ANEC bridge; without it, ANEC and
calorimetric positivity are statements about different limiting operators.
\end{hypothesis}

\paragraph{Detector positivity from ANEC.}
Assume Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:qcd-energy-flow-detector}.  Assume in addition
that the stress tensor satisfies the averaged null energy condition as a
quadratic-form statement on the same scattering domain: for every future null
direction \(n^\mu\), every nonnegative transverse smearing
\(\varphi\), and every \(\Psi\in\mathcal D_{\rm det}\),
\[
  \int\dd^2x_\perp\,\varphi(x_\perp)
  \int_{-\infty}^{\infty}\dd\lambda\,
  \bra{\Psi}T_{\mu\nu}(x_\perp+\lambda n)n^\mu n^\nu\ket{\Psi}
  \geq0 .
\]
Then the self-adjoint closure of \(\widehat{\mathcal E}(f)\) is positive for
every \(f\geq0\).

Write a nonnegative smooth angular test function as a finite sum of functions
supported in coordinate patches on \(S^2\), using a partition of unity.  In
each patch, the large-\(R\) detector limit is the conformal or asymptotic
image of a null-energy integral along the complete generator labelled by
\(\mathbf n\), with transverse smearing determined by the angular support of
\(f\).  The Jacobian relating the angular measure to transverse measure is
positive.  The ANEC inequality therefore gives nonnegative quadratic form
values for each patch.  Summing the patch contributions gives
\[
  \bra{\Psi}\widehat{\mathcal E}(f)\ket{\Psi}\geq0
  \qquad (\Psi\in\mathcal D_{\rm det},\ f\geq0).
\]
Since the operator has a unique self-adjoint closure by
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:qcd-energy-flow-detector}, positivity of the quadratic
form on a core implies positivity of the closure by the spectral theorem.

\begin{remark}[Status in QCD and in conformal theories]
\label{rem:qcd-energy-flow-status}
For free massless fields, the limit in
\eqref{eq:energy-flow-operator-smeared} is obtained by inserting the mode
expansion and applying stationary phase at null infinity.  For conformal
field theories satisfying the light-transform hypotheses of
Chapter~\ref{ch:cft-light-ray-energy-correlators}, the detector is the
stress-tensor light-ray operator and positivity is supplied by the ANEC
theorem stated there.  In four-dimensional QCD, the detector is the expected
physical calorimeter observable, but its nonperturbative construction depends
on the existence of the continuum theory, the physical scattering space, and
the hadronic asymptotic completeness problem stated in
Open Problem~\ref{op:qcd-asymptotic-completeness}.  Perturbative KLN
cancellation proves finiteness of regulator-expanded coefficients for
IRC-continuous measurements after the relevant sums over degenerate states
and the required factorization steps have been made; it does not construct
the self-adjoint detector operator on the exact physical Hilbert space.
\end{remark}

\begin{openproblem}[Energy-flow operators in four-dimensional QCD]
\label{op:qcd-energy-flow-operator-construction}
Construct the operators \(\widehat{\mathcal E}(f)\) of
Construction~\ref{cons:qcd-energy-flow-detector} in continuum
four-dimensional QCD.  The construction should start from a nonperturbative
definition of the physical Hilbert space, identify a dense finite-energy
scattering domain, prove the null-infinity weak limits, prove essential
self-adjointness or specify the self-adjoint extension selected by detector
physics, prove positivity from an ANEC theorem in the same framework, and
show that \(\widehat{\mathcal E}(1)\) agrees with the outgoing Hamiltonian on
the hadronic scattering subspace.
\end{openproblem}

Here \(\mathbf n\in S^2\) is a unit spatial direction and \(\dd\Omega\) is the
rotation-invariant measure on \(S^2\).  The distribution
\(\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n)\) is defined by
\(\widehat{\mathcal E}(f)=\int_{S^2}\dd\Omega(\mathbf n)
f(\mathbf n)\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n)\).  On an outgoing state of
stable hadrons with momenta \(p_r\), species labels \(a_r\), and the
normalization conventions of scattering theory,
\begin{equation}
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(f)
  \ket{p_1,a_1;\ldots;p_N,a_N}_{\mathrm{out}}
  =
  \left(\sum_{r=1}^N p_r^0\,f(\widehat{\mathbf p}_r)\right)
  \ket{p_1,a_1;\ldots;p_N,a_N}_{\mathrm{out}},
  \qquad
  \widehat{\mathbf p}_r:=\frac{\mathbf p_r}{|\mathbf p_r|}.
  \label{eq:energy-flow-on-hadron-state}
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:energy-flow-on-hadron-state} is the spectral action of the
detector limit on physical hadronic asymptotic states.

\paragraph{Asymptotic multiplication model.}
The preceding formula has a precise operator-theoretic meaning once an
outgoing scattering representation has been chosen.  Let
\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{out}}\) be the physical outgoing scattering subspace and
write it as a direct integral over hadronic scattering configurations,
\[
  \mathcal H_{\mathrm{out}}
  \simeq
  \int_{\mathcal X_{\mathrm{out}}}^{\oplus}\mathcal K_Y\,\dd\nu(Y).
\]
Here \(Y\) specifies the number of stable hadrons, their species labels,
on-shell momenta, and the discrete or continuous degeneracy labels left after
the standard Bose--Fermi symmetrizations; \(\mathcal K_Y\) is the
corresponding finite or countable multiplicity space.  The outgoing
Hamiltonian is multiplication by
\[
  E_{\mathrm{tot}}(Y)=\sum_{r\in Y}p_r^0 .
\]
For a bounded Borel function \(f:S^2\to\mathbb C\), define
\begin{equation}
  m_f(Y):=\sum_{r\in Y}p_r^0 f(\widehat{\mathbf p}_r),
  \qquad
  \mathcal E_{\mathrm{mult}}(f):=M_{m_f},
  \label{eq:energy-detector-multiplication-symbol}
\end{equation}
where \(M_{m_f}\) is the direct-integral multiplication operator with maximal
domain
\[
  \operatorname{Dom} M_{m_f}
  =
  \left\{\Psi:
  \int_{\mathcal X_{\mathrm{out}}}
  |m_f(Y)|^2\|\Psi(Y)\|_{\mathcal K_Y}^2\,\dd\nu(Y)<\infty
  \right\}.
\]
If \(f\) is real, \(M_{m_f}\) is self-adjoint; if \(f\geq0\), it is positive;
and
\begin{equation}
  |m_f(Y)|\leq \|f\|_\infty E_{\mathrm{tot}}(Y),
  \qquad
  \operatorname{Dom} H_{\mathrm{out}}
  \subset
  \operatorname{Dom} \mathcal E_{\mathrm{mult}}(f).
  \label{eq:energy-detector-hamiltonian-bound}
\end{equation}
Moreover the family is strongly commuting, because all members are
multiplication operators on the same direct-integral space.  For bounded
\(f_1,\ldots,f_k\),
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal E_{\mathrm{mult}}(f_1)\cdots
  \mathcal E_{\mathrm{mult}}(f_k)
  =
  M_{\prod_{j=1}^k m_{f_j}},
  \qquad
  \operatorname{Dom} H_{\mathrm{out}}^k
  \subset
  \operatorname{Dom}
  \bigl(\mathcal E_{\mathrm{mult}}(f_1)\cdots
  \mathcal E_{\mathrm{mult}}(f_k)\bigr).
  \label{eq:energy-detector-product-domain}
\end{equation}
Indeed
\[
  \left|\prod_{j=1}^k m_{f_j}(Y)\right|
  \leq
  \left(\prod_{j=1}^k\|f_j\|_\infty\right)
  E_{\mathrm{tot}}(Y)^k ,
\]
which gives the displayed domain inclusion.  The stress-tensor flux operator
\(\widehat{\mathcal E}(f)\) of
Construction~\ref{cons:qcd-energy-flow-detector}, when it exists, is required
to agree with \(\mathcal E_{\mathrm{mult}}(f)\) after the outgoing wave
operator identifies finite-energy scattering states with their asymptotic
configurations.  This agreement is part of the nonperturbative detector
construction problem; perturbation theory may test its matrix elements after
the detector operator has been defined.

The corresponding eventwise calorimetric measure of the final state \(X\) is
\[
  \mu_X
  =
  \sum_{r\in X}p_r^0\,\delta_{\widehat{\mathbf p}_r},
  \qquad
  \widehat{\mathcal E}_X(f)=\int_{S^2}f\,\dd\mu_X .
\]
The detector observable depends on \(X\) only through the positive measure
\(\mu_X\).  The multiplication model also fixes the meaning of coincident
detectors.  For a finite configuration \(X\),
\begin{equation}
  \prod_{j=1}^k\widehat{\mathcal E}_X(f_j)
  =
  \int_{(S^2)^k}
  f_1(\mathbf n_1)\cdots f_k(\mathbf n_k)\,
  \dd\mu_X(\mathbf n_1)\cdots \dd\mu_X(\mathbf n_k).
  \label{eq:energy-detector-product-measure}
\end{equation}
Thus the product measure includes the diagonal strata
\(\mathbf n_i=\mathbf n_j\).  A separated-angle correlator is the restriction
of the resulting distribution away from these diagonals; deleting the
diagonal weight defines a different observable and must be declared as an
additional measurement prescription.

Given a normalized incoming physical state \(\Psi_{\mathrm{in}}\), or a state
prepared by a local color-singlet current and then evolved to future infinity,
the \(k\)-point energy correlator is the distribution on \((S^2)^k\)
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal G_k(f_1,\ldots,f_k;\Psi)
  =
  {}_{\mathrm{out}}\!\bra{\Psi}
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(f_1)\cdots
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(f_k)
  \ket{\Psi}_{\mathrm{out}} .
  \label{eq:energy-correlator-definition}
\end{equation}
After inserting a complete set of physical hadronic out-states, this becomes
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal G_k(f_1,\ldots,f_k;\Psi)
  =
  \sum_X
  |\braket{X,\mathrm{out}}{\Psi,\mathrm{out}}|^2
  \prod_{\ell=1}^k
  \left(
    \sum_{r\in X} p_r^0\,f_\ell(\widehat{\mathbf p}_r)
  \right),
  \label{eq:energy-correlator-hadron-sum}
\end{equation}
with the usual replacement of the displayed sum by direct integrals over
continuous multiparticle phase space.  This formula is nonperturbative: all
states in \(X\) are physical hadronic states, and the operator being measured
is built from \(T^{\mu\nu}\).

\paragraph{Connected cumulants and contact strata.}
Let \(\mathbb P_\Psi\) denote the probability measure on outgoing
configurations induced by the normalized state \(\Psi\) in the multiplication
model.  For bounded detector tests \(f_1,\ldots,f_k\), put
\[
  X_j(Y):=\mathcal E_Y(f_j)
  =
  \int_{S^2} f_j\,\dd\mu_Y .
\]
Then \(\mathcal G_k(f_1,\ldots,f_k;\Psi)\) is the raw moment
\[
  \mathbb E_{\mathbb P_\Psi}\!\left[X_1\cdots X_k\right].
\]
The connected energy correlator in this event-ensemble sense is the cumulant
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal G_k^{\rm conn}(f_1,\ldots,f_k;\Psi)
  =
  \sum_{\pi\in\Pi_k}
  (-1)^{|\pi|-1}(|\pi|-1)!
  \prod_{B\in\pi}
  \mathcal G_{|B|}\bigl((f_i)_{i\in B};\Psi\bigr),
  \label{eq:qcd-energy-correlator-cumulant}
\end{equation}
where \(\Pi_k\) is the set of set partitions of
\(\{1,\ldots,k\}\).  Thus, for example,
\[
  \mathcal G_2^{\rm conn}(f,g)
  =
  \mathcal G_2(f,g)-\mathcal G_1(f)\mathcal G_1(g),
\]
and \(\mathcal G_3^{\rm conn}\) is obtained by subtracting the three
one-block--two-block products and adding twice the product of the three
one-point functions.  This is a subtraction of event-to-event factorization
in the probability distribution of final states.

It is a different operation from removing coincident-detector contacts.  For
a fixed event \(Y\), the product measure \(\mu_Y^{\otimes k}\) decomposes
into strata labeled by coincidences among detector labels.  Already for three
detectors,
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \mathcal E_Y(f)\mathcal E_Y(g)\mathcal E_Y(h)
  &=
  \sum_{\substack{r,s,t\in Y\\ r,s,t\ {\rm distinct}}}
    E_rE_sE_t f_r g_s h_t                                      \\
  &\quad+
  \sum_{\substack{r,t\in Y\\ r\neq t}}
    E_r^2E_t f_r g_r h_t
  +
  \sum_{\substack{r,s\in Y\\ r\neq s}}
    E_r^2E_s f_r g_s h_r                                      \\
  &\quad+
  \sum_{\substack{r,s\in Y\\ r\neq s}}
    E_rE_s^2 f_r g_s h_s
  +
  \sum_{r\in Y}E_r^3 f_r g_r h_r ,
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:qcd-three-detector-contact-strata}
\end{equation}
where \(E_r=p_r^0\) and \(f_r=f(\widehat{\mathbf p}_r)\), etc.  The last
four terms are diagonal contact strata of the detector product; they are
present before the average over events is taken.  If
\(\mathbb P_\Psi\) is concentrated on a single event, all ensemble cumulants
of order \(k\geq2\) vanish, but the diagonal terms in
\eqref{eq:qcd-three-detector-contact-strata} remain in the raw detector
product.  Conversely, deleting diagonal strata produces a separated-detector
measurement prescription, not an ensemble-connected correlator.  A calculation
that quotes a ``connected'' or ``contact-subtracted'' energy correlator must
therefore state which of these two operations is being performed.

\paragraph{Soft and collinear continuity of smeared energy flow.}
Let \(f\in C^1(S^2)\).  Suppose a final-state calorimetric measure
\(\mu_X\) is changed either by adding one particle of energy \(\varepsilon\) at
direction \(\mathbf m\), or by replacing two particles of energies \(E_a,E_b\)
and directions \(\mathbf n_a,\mathbf n_b\) by one particle of energy
\(E_a+E_b\) in the direction
\[
  \mathbf n_{ab}
  =
  \frac{E_a\mathbf n_a+E_b\mathbf n_b}
       {|E_a\mathbf n_a+E_b\mathbf n_b|}.
\]
The resulting detector change obeys
\[
  \left|\Delta\widehat{\mathcal E}_X(f)\right|
  \leq
  \varepsilon \|f\|_\infty
\]
in the soft case, and
\[
  \left|\Delta\widehat{\mathcal E}_X(f)\right|
  \leq
  (E_a+E_b)\operatorname{Lip}(f)\,
  \operatorname{diam}\{\mathbf n_a,\mathbf n_b,\mathbf n_{ab}\}
\]
in the collinear case.
For a soft particle, the measure changes by
\(\varepsilon\delta_{\mathbf m}\), so the change of the detector value is
\(\varepsilon f(\mathbf m)\), whose absolute value is bounded by
\(\varepsilon\|f\|_\infty\).  For a collinear recombination, the change is
\[
  E_a f(\mathbf n_a)+E_b f(\mathbf n_b)
  -(E_a+E_b)f(\mathbf n_{ab}).
\]
Writing this as
\[
  E_a\bigl(f(\mathbf n_a)-f(\mathbf n_{ab})\bigr)
  +
