  E_b\bigl(f(\mathbf n_b)-f(\mathbf n_{ab})\bigr)
\]
and using the Lipschitz constant of \(f\) on the round sphere gives
\[
  |\Delta\widehat{\mathcal E}_X(f)|
  \leq
  E_a\operatorname{Lip}(f)d(\mathbf n_a,\mathbf n_{ab})
  +
  E_b\operatorname{Lip}(f)d(\mathbf n_b,\mathbf n_{ab}),
\]
which is bounded by the displayed diameter estimate.  Thus the smeared
detector is continuous for the weak calorimetric topology generated by
finite-energy measures tested against \(C^1(S^2)\) functions: soft additions
vanish with their energy, and collinear recombinations vanish uniformly on
bounded-energy sectors as the angular diameter tends to zero.

The same estimate applies to products
\(\prod_{\ell=1}^k\widehat{\mathcal E}_X(f_\ell)\) on any fixed
finite-energy sector by the elementary telescoping identity
\[
  \prod_{\ell=1}^k A_\ell-\prod_{\ell=1}^k B_\ell
  =
  \sum_{j=1}^k
  \left(\prod_{\ell<j}A_\ell\right)
  (A_j-B_j)
  \left(\prod_{\ell>j}B_\ell\right),
\]
with \(A_\ell=\widehat{\mathcal E}_{X'}(f_\ell)\) and
\(B_\ell=\widehat{\mathcal E}_X(f_\ell)\).  Thus smeared energy correlators
are continuous functions of the calorimetric measure for soft and collinear
degenerations.  Perturbative finiteness then has a precise theorem boundary:
at each fixed order in a regulator for which the Kinoshita--Lee--Nauenberg
cancellation and QCD factorization hold for the chosen inclusive channel,
measurement functions with the above continuity produce finite coefficients
after summing over degenerate final states and virtual corrections.  The
operator definition \eqref{eq:energy-correlator-definition} is the
nonperturbative observable; perturbation theory computes its short-distance
expansion in the regime where asymptotic freedom supplies a controlled small
coupling.

The unsmeared product
\(\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n_1)\cdots
\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n_k)\) is a distribution.  Coincident directions
carry contact singularities because several detector insertions can act on the
same hadron.  The separated-angle correlator is obtained by testing against
functions supported away from the coincidence diagonals in \((S^2)^k\); fully
smeared correlators include the contact terms determined by the detector
operator product itself.

\subsection{Energy-Energy Correlation in Electron-Positron Annihilation}

Let a color-singlet current create a state of total center-of-mass energy
\(Q\).  For each physical hadronic final state \(X\), write
\[
  z_r=\frac{p_r^0}{Q},
  \qquad
  \cos\chi_{rs}=
  \widehat{\mathbf p}_r\cdot\widehat{\mathbf p}_s .
\]
The normalized two-point energy-energy correlator is the distribution
\begin{equation}
  \mathrm{EEC}(\chi)
  =
  \frac{1}{\sigma_{\mathrm{tot}}}
  \sum_X
  \int \dd\sigma_X\,
  \sum_{r,s\in X}
  z_r z_s\,
  \delta(\cos\chi-\cos\chi_{rs}),
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-definition}
\end{equation}
where \(\dd\sigma_X\) is the differential cross-section measure for the
exclusive hadronic channel \(X\), and the sum is a direct integral over
continuous phase space.  The terms \(r=s\) are the coincident-detector contact
part at \(\chi=0\).  A convention that removes this contact part defines a
different distribution at \(\chi=0\) and the same separated-angle function for
\(0<\chi<\pi\).

Equation~\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-definition} is the detector form of the
Basham--Brown--Ellis--Love observable.  Its perturbative expansion in
asymptotically free QCD is a calculation of the current-created state and of
the detector insertions in the short-distance region.  The back-to-back limit
\(\chi\to\pi\) is controlled by soft and collinear radiation constrained by
transverse momentum conservation; the small-angle limit is controlled by a
collinear operator product of energy-flow insertions.  Both limits require
resummation because the separated-angle distribution contains large logarithms
of \(1+\cos\chi\) or \(1-\cos\chi\), respectively.

\paragraph{EEC moment sum rules and the contact term.}
Let \(X\) be a physical final state in the center-of-mass frame of a
color-singlet source, with total energy \(Q\) and total spatial momentum zero.
Set
\[
  z_r=\frac{p_r^0}{Q},
  \qquad
  \mathbf n_r=\frac{\mathbf p_r}{|\mathbf p_r|},
  \qquad
  \zeta_{rs}=\mathbf n_r\cdot\mathbf n_s .
\]
Define the eventwise two-point calorimetric distribution in
\(\zeta=\cos\chi\) by
\begin{equation}
  E_{2,X}(\zeta)
  =
  \sum_{r,s\in X}z_r z_s\,\delta(\zeta-\zeta_{rs}) .
  \label{eq:eventwise-eec-zeta-distribution}
\end{equation}
Then, as distributional moments on \([-1,1]\),
\begin{equation}
  \int_{-1}^{1} E_{2,X}(\zeta)\,\dd\zeta=1,
  \qquad
  \int_{-1}^{1}\zeta\,E_{2,X}(\zeta)\,\dd\zeta=0 .
  \label{eq:eventwise-eec-first-sum-rules}
\end{equation}
The coincident-detector contact part at \(\zeta=1\) has weight
\begin{equation}
  E_{2,X}^{\rm contact}(\zeta)
  =
  \left(\sum_{r\in X}z_r^2\right)\delta(\zeta-1).
  \label{eq:eventwise-eec-contact-weight}
\end{equation}
Consequently the cross-section averaged EEC of
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-definition}, including the \(r=s\) terms, satisfies the same
zeroth and first moment sum rules after division by \(\sigma_{\rm tot}\).

The total-energy condition gives
\[
  \sum_{r\in X}z_r=1.
\]
Testing \eqref{eq:eventwise-eec-zeta-distribution} against the constant
function \(1\) gives
\[
  \sum_{r,s}z_rz_s
  =
  \left(\sum_r z_r\right)^2
  =
  1.
\]
Testing against \(\zeta\) gives
\[
  \sum_{r,s}z_rz_s\,\mathbf n_r\cdot\mathbf n_s
  =
  \left|\sum_r z_r\mathbf n_r\right|^2.
\]
Since the source is in its center-of-mass frame,
\[
  \sum_r p_r^0\mathbf n_r=\sum_r\mathbf p_r=0,
\]
and the first moment vanishes.  The contact contribution is exactly the
subsum with \(r=s\), for which \(\zeta_{rr}=1\).  Averaging the eventwise
identities with the positive cross-section measure and dividing by
\(\sigma_{\rm tot}\) preserves the two moment identities.

\begin{remark}[Use of the sum rules]
\label{rem:eec-sum-rules-use}
The eventwise sum rules above are statements about the nonperturbative
detector observable, not about partons.  A fixed-order
calculation, a resummed endpoint formula, a lattice-inspired approximation, or
a parton shower that claims to represent the normalized EEC must specify how
the \(\zeta=1\) contact term is treated and must satisfy the moment identities
after the same convention is applied.  If the contact term is removed, the
remaining separated-angle distribution no longer has unit integral by itself;
the missing weight is \(\langle\sum_r z_r^2\rangle\).
\end{remark}

\paragraph{Legendre moments and calorimetric multipoles.}
The contact-inclusive two-detector distribution has stronger eventwise
constraints than the first two moments alone.  For every \(\ell\ge0\) define
\[
  M_{\ell,X}:=
  \int_{-1}^{1}P_\ell(\zeta)E_{2,X}(\zeta)\,\dd\zeta
  =
  \sum_{r,s\in X}z_rz_s P_\ell(\mathbf n_r\!\cdot\!\mathbf n_s).
\]
With the usual orthonormal complex spherical harmonics on \(S^2\), the
addition theorem gives
\[
  P_\ell(\mathbf n\!\cdot\!\mathbf m)
  =
  \frac{4\pi}{2\ell+1}
  \sum_{a=-\ell}^{\ell}
  Y_{\ell a}(\mathbf n)\overline{Y_{\ell a}(\mathbf m)} .
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
  M_{\ell,X}
  =
  \frac{4\pi}{2\ell+1}
  \sum_{a=-\ell}^{\ell}
  \left|
    \sum_{r\in X} z_rY_{\ell a}(\mathbf n_r)
  \right|^2
  \ge0 .
  \label{eq:eventwise-eec-legendre-positivity}
\end{equation}
This positivity is a property of the positive calorimetric measure
\(\sum_r z_r\delta_{\mathbf n_r}\).  It is not a property of the
separated-angle density after the coincident-detector atom has been removed.
Indeed, for \(\ell=1\),
\[
  M_{1,X}
  =
  \sum_{r,s}z_rz_s\,\mathbf n_r\!\cdot\!\mathbf n_s
  =
  \left|\sum_r z_r\mathbf n_r\right|^2,
\]
so the color-singlet center-of-mass condition sets the full moment to zero;
the separated part alone then has first Legendre moment
\(-\sum_r z_r^2\).  The contact atom is therefore forced by positivity and
momentum conservation, not by a cosmetic endpoint convention.

The next moment displays the quadrupole coordinate.  Put
\[
  Q_{ij}(X):=
  \sum_{r\in X}z_r
  \left(n_r^in_r^j-\frac13\delta_{ij}\right).
\]
Then
\[
  \operatorname{tr}Q(X)^2
  =
  \sum_{r,s}z_rz_s
  \left((\mathbf n_r\!\cdot\!\mathbf n_s)^2-\frac13\right),
  \qquad
  M_{2,X}
  =
  \frac32\,\operatorname{tr}Q(X)^2
  \ge0 .
\]
Cross-section averaging preserves
\eqref{eq:eventwise-eec-legendre-positivity}.  Thus any perturbative,
resummed, shower, or finite-resolution representation of the normalized EEC
must say which endpoint/contact convention realizes these multipole
positivity constraints.  A separated-angle approximation that fits the bulk
shape but gives a negative contact-inclusive \(M_{\ell}\) is not a positive
detector measure.

\paragraph{Three-detector moment and contact ledger.}
The same detector definition gives a genuinely higher-point distribution
before any partonic approximation is made.  For the same event \(X\), define
the ordered three-detector distribution on the three angular invariants
\(\zeta_{12},\zeta_{13},\zeta_{23}\) by
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  E_{3,X}(\zeta_{12},\zeta_{13},\zeta_{23})
  &:=
  \sum_{r,s,t\in X}
  z_rz_sz_t\,
  \delta(\zeta_{12}-\mathbf n_r\!\cdot\!\mathbf n_s)\,
  \delta(\zeta_{13}-\mathbf n_r\!\cdot\!\mathbf n_t)          \\
  &\hspace{6.3em}\times
  \delta(\zeta_{23}-\mathbf n_s\!\cdot\!\mathbf n_t).
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:eventwise-three-detector-distribution}
\end{equation}
Its support is not the whole cube \([-1,1]^3\), but the Gram-positive
region of triples of unit directions, plus the diagonal strata.  As moments
of this distribution,
\begin{equation}
  \int E_{3,X}=1,
  \qquad
  \int \zeta_{12}E_{3,X}
  =
  \int \zeta_{13}E_{3,X}
  =
  \int \zeta_{23}E_{3,X}
  =
  0
  \label{eq:eventwise-three-detector-moments}
\end{equation}
in a color-singlet center-of-mass event.  The proof is the same detector
algebra as above: the constant test gives
\((\sum_r z_r)^3=1\), while, for example,
\[
  \sum_{r,s,t}z_rz_sz_t\,\mathbf n_r\cdot\mathbf n_s
  =
  \left|\sum_r z_r\mathbf n_r\right|^2
  \left(\sum_t z_t\right)
  =
  0 .
\]
The other two pair moments are identical after relabeling the ordered
detectors.

The diagonal contact strata are now richer than in the EEC.  The completely
coincident stratum is
\begin{equation}
  \left(\sum_{r\in X}z_r^3\right)
  \delta(\zeta_{12}-1)\delta(\zeta_{13}-1)\delta(\zeta_{23}-1).
  \label{eq:eventwise-three-detector-total-contact}
\end{equation}
There are also three pair-coincidence strata.  For instance, the stratum
where detectors \(1\) and \(2\) hit the same hadron but detector \(3\) hits a
different hadron is
\begin{equation}
  \sum_{\substack{r,t\in X\\ r\neq t}}
  z_r^2z_t\,
  \delta(\zeta_{12}-1)
  \delta(\zeta_{13}-\zeta_{rt})
  \delta(\zeta_{23}-\zeta_{rt}),
  \qquad
  \zeta_{rt}=\mathbf n_r\cdot\mathbf n_t,
  \label{eq:eventwise-three-detector-pair-contact}
\end{equation}
with two analogous terms for \(1=3\) and \(2=3\).  Removing all these
diagonal strata defines a separated three-detector observable.  It does not
by itself obey \eqref{eq:eventwise-three-detector-moments}; the missing
weights are precisely the contact coordinates above.  Thus higher-point
energy correlators inherit the same lesson as the EEC: endpoint/contact
coordinates are part of the detector observable, not optional decorations
added after a partonic calculation.

\subsection{Light-Ray Interpretation and Endpoint Regimes}

The detector density \(\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n)\) is the QCD analogue
of the stress-tensor light transform developed in
Chapter~\ref{ch:cft-light-ray-energy-correlators}.  In a conformal theory the
light transform is an operator-valued distribution controlled by Lorentzian
conformal representation theory.  In QCD the coupling runs, so the same
formula is not a conformal operator identity.  It remains an asymptotic
detector definition in the physical Hilbert space, and the short-distance
limits are computed by matching the detector product onto operators whose
renormalization group evolution is controlled by QCD anomalous dimensions.

\paragraph{Proof-status architecture for the EEC program.}
The exact detector identities above and the endpoint formulae below live at
different levels of the argument.  First, the physical detector layer starts
from the stress-tensor flux limit or, on the outgoing scattering
representation, from multiplication by the calorimetric measure.  This layer
fixes positivity, total-energy moments, diagonal contact strata, multipole
positivity, and the distinction between ensemble cumulants and eventwise
contacts.  Second, the conformal fixed-point layer is the light-ray
operator framework of Chapter~\ref{ch:cft-light-ray-energy-correlators}: it
supplies representation-theoretic homogeneity, finite light-ray charts,
diagonal-contact extensions, and endpoint pushforwards only under the
Lorentzian analyticity and growth hypotheses stated there.  Third, the QCD
small-angle layer replaces fixed-point light-ray data by renormalized
Wilson-line/light-ray operator coordinates with ultraviolet and rapidity
subtractions, protected moment rows, finite chart changes, and projected
curvature or omitted-channel remainders.  Fourth, the perturbative endpoint
layer computes coefficients, anomalous dimensions, contact counterterms, and
matching functions in one declared scheme; the tree-level collinear
coefficients and cusp-log flatness check are tests of this layer, not the
full all-order light-ray OPE/mixing theorem.  Finally, the observable
prediction layer glues the separated bulk, small-angle endpoint,
back-to-back endpoint, and explicit endpoint atoms so that the detector
moment identities remain true.

Thus the dependency chain is
\[
  \begin{aligned}
  \text{detector measure and contacts}
  &\Longrightarrow
  \text{CFT or QCD light-ray endpoint chart} \\
  &\Longrightarrow
  \text{renormalized mixing/factorization calculation} \\
  &\Longrightarrow
  \text{endpoint gluing and observable prediction}.
  \end{aligned}
\]
Skipping any arrow changes the mathematical claim.  A separated-angle
fixed-order distribution without contact data is not the normalized detector
observable; a finite retained light-ray block without a curvature or
omitted-channel estimate is not an endpoint theorem; and a resummed endpoint
formula without the gluing and moment ledger is not yet a prediction for the
full normalized EEC on \([-1,1]\).

For \(0<\chi<\pi\), the EEC is a separated-angle distribution.  Two endpoint
regions have different expansions.  In the small-angle region set
\[
  \theta^2:=2(1-\cos\chi)\ll1 .
\]
The product of two nearby detector insertions is matched onto a sum of
collinear light-ray operators:
\begin{equation}
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n_1)\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n_2)
  \sim
  \sum_A C_A(\theta,Q,\mu)\,
  \mathbb O_A(\mathbf n,\mu),
  \qquad
  \mathbf n_1,\mathbf n_2\to\mathbf n .
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-ope-form}
\end{equation}
Here \(\mathbb O_A\) are light-ray operators in the collinear direction,
including twist-two energy-flow moments and their descendants in the
appropriate channel.  The symbol \(\sim\) denotes an asymptotic expansion
after smearing against angular test functions supported at
\(\theta\ll1\).  The coefficient functions \(C_A\) are perturbatively
computable at large transverse scale \(Q\theta\), and the evolution of
\(\mathbb O_A\) resums logarithms of \(\theta\).

In the back-to-back region set
\[
  z:=\frac{1-\cos\chi}{2},
  \qquad
  q_T^2:=Q^2(1-z)
  =
  \frac{Q^2}{2}(1+\cos\chi)\ll Q^2 .
\]
Momentum conservation forces the two measured energy deposits to recoil
against soft and collinear radiation of small total transverse momentum.  The
factorized form is the transverse-momentum resummation analogue
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd\sigma}{\dd q_T^2}
  =
  H(Q,\mu)
  \int \frac{\dd^2 b}{(2\pi)^2}\,
  \ee^{\ii b\cdot q_T}\,
  J_n(b,\mu,\nu)\,
  J_{\bar n}(b,\mu,\nu)\,
  S(b,\mu,\nu)
  +
  O(q_T/Q),
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-back-to-back-factorization}
\end{equation}
for a color-singlet source and in a rapidity-renormalization scheme with
rapidity scale \(\nu\).  The hard, jet, and soft functions have coupled
\(\mu\)- and \(\nu\)-evolution equations; solving them resums Sudakov
logarithms of \(q_T/Q\).  The power remainder and the absence or treatment of
Glauber exchanges are part of the factorization hypothesis.

Here and below \(\alpha_s(\mu):=g^2(\mu)/(4\pi)\) in the trace-delta gauge
coordinate of this chapter.  Whenever a coefficient is proportional to
\(\alpha_s C_F\), it is invariant under conversion to the common half-trace
generator convention because \(g_{\rm ht}^2C_F^{\rm ht}=g^2C_F\), as in
\eqref{eq:pnrqcd-tree-coulomb-potential}.

The leading double logarithm is fixed already by the lightlike cusp anomalous
dimension.  Let \(b=|b|\) in \eqref{eq:qcd-eec-back-to-back-factorization},
set
\[
  b_{\rm F}:=2\ee^{-\gamma_E},\qquad
  \mu_b:=\frac{b_{\rm F}}{b},\qquad
  L_b:=\log\frac{Q^2}{\mu_b^2}
  =
  \log\frac{Q^2b^2}{b_{\rm F}^2}.
\]
The constant \(b_{\rm F}\) is a Fourier-convention constant, not a new
physical scale.  In the trace-delta convention of this chapter the one-loop
quark cusp anomalous dimension is
\begin{equation}
  \Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g)
  =
  \frac{g^2C_F}{4\pi^2}+O(g^4)
  =
  \frac{\alpha_s C_F}{\pi}+O(\alpha_s^2),
  \label{eq:qcd-quark-cusp-one-loop-trace-delta}
\end{equation}
where \(C_F=(N_c^2-1)/N_c\).

Assume the back-to-back factorization datum
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-back-to-back-factorization} for a color-singlet
quark-current event shape, with the hard scale \(Q\), the impact-parameter
scale \(\mu_b=b_{\rm F}/b\), and a subtraction scheme in which the leading
large logarithms are generated by the quark cusp anomalous dimension
\eqref{eq:qcd-quark-cusp-one-loop-trace-delta}.  If running of \(g\) and all
non-cusp anomalous dimensions are omitted, the leading-logarithmic
impact-parameter kernel has the form
\begin{equation}
  W_{\rm LL}(b,Q)
  =
  W(b,\mu_b)\,
  \exp\!\left[
    -\frac12\,\Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g)\,L_b^2
  \right].
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-leading-sudakov-factor}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, at one loop,
\[
  W_{\rm LL}(b,Q)
  =
  W(b,\mu_b)\,
  \exp\!\left[
    -\frac{\alpha_s C_F}{2\pi}L_b^2
    +O(\alpha_s^2L_b^2)
  \right].
\]
Its content is the fixed-coupling leading-logarithmic component of the
factorization formula.  The factorized expression is an impact-parameter
representation of the
recoil constraint.  The hard matching is naturally made at scale \(Q\), while
the transverse-distance functions are naturally evaluated at scale
\(\mu_b\).  Cusp evolution between these two scales gives the logarithmic
exponent
\[
  S_{\rm LL}(Q,b)
  =
  \int_{\mu_b^2}^{Q^2}
  \frac{\dd\kappa^2}{\kappa^2}\,
  \Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g)\,
  \log\frac{Q^2}{\kappa^2}
\]
when \(g\) is held fixed and non-cusp anomalous dimensions are discarded.
Changing variables to
\[
  u=\log\frac{Q^2}{\kappa^2}
\]
turns the integral into
\[
  S_{\rm LL}(Q,b)
  =
  \Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g)
  \int_0^{L_b}u\,\dd u
  =
  \frac12\,\Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g)L_b^2.
\]
The kernel in \eqref{eq:qcd-eec-back-to-back-factorization} is suppressed by
the Sudakov no-resolved-recoil factor between the two scales; this fixes the
minus sign in \(\exp[-S_{\rm LL}]\) in the chosen evolution convention.
Substituting
\eqref{eq:qcd-quark-cusp-one-loop-trace-delta} gives the displayed one-loop
form.

\begin{remark}[Scope of the Sudakov formula]
\label{rem:qcd-eec-sudakov-scope}
The fixed-coupling display above supplies only the cusp-controlled double
logarithm inside a full back-to-back EEC theorem.  A complete perturbative
prediction must specify the rapidity regulator, the hard, jet, and soft
functions, their finite scheme constants, matching to the fixed
separated-angle distribution, running-coupling improvement, and the leading
power corrections in \(q_T/Q\).  The calculation isolates the universal
cusp-controlled double logarithm that any such consistent factorization scheme
must reproduce.
\end{remark}

\paragraph{Tested recoil chart and the large-\(b\) boundary.}
The impact-parameter formula becomes the measured contribution
\(\mathcal P_\tau^{\rm rec}\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-measured-eec-factorization-budget} only after it has been
turned into a detector-test functional.  One must first choose a
back-to-back endpoint window
\(0<q_T<q_0\) and pull angular tests back by
\begin{equation}
  \varphi_Q(q_T^2)
  :=
  \varphi\!\left(-1+\frac{2q_T^2}{Q^2}\right),
  \qquad
  q_T^2=\frac{Q^2}{2}(1+\zeta).
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-recoil-test-pullback}
\end{equation}
This is the pushforward of the standard EEC variable
\(z=(1-\zeta)/2\) together with \(1-z=q_T^2/Q^2\).  Equivalently,
\(\dd\sigma/\dd\zeta=(Q^2/2)\,\dd\sigma/\dd q_T^2\) at
\(q_T^2=Q^2(1+\zeta)/2\); in test-function form the same Jacobian is already
accounted for by pairing the \(q_T^2\)-distribution with
\(\varphi_Q(q_T^2)\).  The open recoil chart is then the distribution on
\(0<q_T<q_0\) obtained by pairing \(\varphi_Q\) with the Fourier kernel in
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-back-to-back-factorization}, after the overlap with the
fixed-order bulk chart has been subtracted.  Endpoint support at \(q_T=0\), or
equivalently \(\zeta=-1\), is carried by the separate endpoint atom
\(K_-^\tau\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-measured-eec-factorization-budget}.  This separation is
essential because a Born-level back-to-back contribution, a perturbative
recoil singularity, and a nonperturbative endpoint model are different
coordinates of the same measured distribution.

The Fourier integral also has a physical boundary absent from the displayed
leading logarithm.  Perturbation theory controls the factorized kernel only
while all transverse-distance functions are evaluated at scales safely above
\(\Lambda_{\rm QCD}\).  Large impact parameters \(b\gtrsim
\Lambda_{\rm QCD}^{-1}\), or bins with \(q_T\) of hadronic size, require a
nonperturbative shape function, a fitted large-\(b\) prescription, or an
excluded-bin remainder.  Changing from one such prescription to another
changes the long-distance input paired with the detector test, rather than
merely reshuffling the cusp logarithm.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Tested back-to-back EEC recoil chart]
\label{ca:qcd-eec-tested-back-to-back-recoil}
A back-to-back contribution to a measured calorimetric or selected-track EEC
is controlled only after the following data have been specified:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the endpoint window, angular test space, and pullback
  \eqref{eq:qcd-eec-recoil-test-pullback};
  \item the hard, jet, and soft functions in one ultraviolet and rapidity
  scheme, including the track-function or fragmentation lift when
  \(\tau\ne1\);
  \item the running-coupling, non-cusp, and rapidity evolution solving the
  same factorization equations as the fixed-order matching coefficients;
  \item the large-\(b\) prescription or shape input, together with the status
  of Glauber contributions and ordinary \(q_T/Q\) power corrections;
  \item the overlap subtraction with the separated-angle bulk chart and the
  endpoint atom convention for \(K_-^\tau\).
\end{enumerate}
If these choices give a recoil functional
\(\mathcal P_{\tau}^{\rm rec}[\varphi;Q]\), its contribution to the measured
residual in \eqref{eq:qcd-measured-eec-residual-bound} must be bounded in the
detector-test topology by a decomposition of the form
\begin{equation}
  \bigl|R_{\tau,Q}^{\rm rec}[\varphi]\bigr|
  \leq
  \epsilon_{\rm fac}^{\rm rec}(\varphi)
  +
  \epsilon_{\rm evo}^{\rm rec}(\varphi)
  +
  \epsilon_{\rm match}^{\rm rec}(\varphi)
  +
  \epsilon_{\rm large\text{-}b}^{\rm rec}(\varphi)
  +
  \epsilon_{\rm Glauber}^{\rm rec}(\varphi)
  +
  \epsilon_{\rm pow}^{\rm rec}(\varphi).
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-tested-recoil-residual-bound}
\end{equation}
Here \(\epsilon_{\rm fac}^{\rm rec}\) is the leading-power factorization
defect, \(\epsilon_{\rm evo}^{\rm rec}\) is the perturbative evolution and
truncation error, \(\epsilon_{\rm match}^{\rm rec}\) includes fixed-order
matching and overlap-subtraction errors, \(\epsilon_{\rm large\text{-}b}^{\rm rec}\)
is the nonperturbative impact-parameter contribution or excluded-bin error,
\(\epsilon_{\rm Glauber}^{\rm rec}\) records any failure or hypothesis of
Glauber cancellation, and \(\epsilon_{\rm pow}^{\rm rec}\) is the remaining
power correction.  The leading Sudakov factor
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-leading-sudakov-factor} supplies only the cusp-controlled
piece of the evolution item.  The recoil contribution to a measured EEC bin
additionally requires the tested chart, endpoint matching, large-\(b\)
input, and residual data listed above.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{lemma}[Tree-level collinear coefficient for the separated EEC]
\label{lem:qcd-eec-tree-collinear-coefficient}
Use the standard four-dimensional, azimuth-integrated, final-state collinear
splitting convention
\begin{equation}
  \dd P_{a\to bc}
  =
  \frac{\alpha_s}{2\pi}\,
  P_{a\to bc}(x)\,\dd x\,\frac{\dd\theta^2}{\theta^2},
  \qquad 0<x<1,
  \label{eq:final-state-collinear-splitting-convention}
\end{equation}
where \(x\) and \(1-x\) are the daughter energy fractions and \(\theta\) is
their small opening angle.  The real-emission contribution of this resolved
splitting to the ordered separated-angle EEC is weighted by
\begin{equation}
  w_{\rm EEC}(x)=2x(1-x).
  \label{eq:eec-ordered-collinear-weight}
\end{equation}
Consequently, for \(\zeta=\cos\chi\) and
\(\theta^2=2(1-\zeta)+O((1-\zeta)^2)\), the leading-power separated-angle
collinear density generated by a parent of type \(a\) has the form
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd P_a^{\rm EEC}}{\dd\zeta}
  =
  \frac{\alpha_s}{2\pi}\,
  \frac{\Gamma_a^{\rm EEC}}{1-\zeta}
  +
  \text{terms less singular as }\zeta\to1,
  \label{eq:eec-tree-collinear-density}
\end{equation}
with resolved real-kernel coefficients
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \Gamma_q^{\rm EEC}
  &=
  \int_0^1 2x(1-x)\,
  C_F\frac{1+x^2}{1-x}\,\dd x
  =
  \frac32\,C_F,                                      \\
  \Gamma_{g\to gg}^{\rm EEC}
  &=
  \int_0^1 2x(1-x)\,
  2C_A\left[
    \frac{x}{1-x}+\frac{1-x}{x}+x(1-x)
  \right]\dd x
  =
  \frac{14}{5}\,C_A,                                 \\
  \Gamma_{g\to q\bar q}^{\rm EEC}
  &=
  \int_0^1 2x(1-x)\,
  T_F\bigl(x^2+(1-x)^2\bigr)\dd x
  =
  \frac15\,T_F
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:eec-real-collinear-coefficients}
\end{equation}
per quark flavor in the last line.  The endpoint singularities of the real
splitting kernels are integrable in these coefficients because the detector
weight \(2x(1-x)\) vanishes when either daughter carries zero energy.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
For one parent of energy \(E\) splitting into two collinear daughters of
energies \(xE\) and \((1-x)E\), the ordered two-detector contribution at the
nonzero opening angle consists of the two ordered pairs \((b,c)\) and
\((c,b)\).  Its energy weight divided by \(E^2\) is therefore
\[
  x(1-x)+(1-x)x=2x(1-x),
\]
which proves \eqref{eq:eec-ordered-collinear-weight}.  The coincident
daughter terms have contact weight
\[
  x^2+(1-x)^2,
\]
and the identity
\[
  x^2+(1-x)^2+2x(1-x)=1
\]
is the local version of the zeroth-moment sum rule in
the eventwise EEC moment identities above: a collinear splitting redistributes
the parent's detector weight between the contact point and the separated small
angle without changing the total two-detector weight.

At leading collinear power the probability measure for the resolved splitting
is \eqref{eq:final-state-collinear-splitting-convention}.  Since
\[
  1-\zeta=1-\cos\theta=\frac{\theta^2}{2}+O(\theta^4),
\]
the positive measure \(\dd\theta^2/\theta^2\), pulled back to the
\(\zeta\)-line near \(\zeta=1\), is
\[
  \frac{\dd\theta^2}{\theta^2}
  =
  \frac{\dd\zeta}{1-\zeta}+O(1)\,\dd\zeta ,
\]
where the equality is an equality of positive densities on intervals
\(\zeta<1\), not an oriented one-form identity.
Multiplying the splitting probability by the ordered EEC weight and retaining
only the leading distribution as \(\zeta\to1\) gives
\eqref{eq:eec-tree-collinear-density} with
\[
  \Gamma_a^{\rm EEC}
  =
  \sum_{a\to bc}
  \int_0^1 2x(1-x)P_{a\to bc}(x)\,\dd x .
\]
Substituting the real tree-level kernels displayed in
\eqref{eq:eec-real-collinear-coefficients} reduces the three coefficients to
elementary polynomial integrals:
\[
  2C_F\int_0^1 x(1+x^2)\,\dd x=\frac32C_F,
\]
\[
  4C_A\int_0^1
  \bigl[x^2+(1-x)^2+x^2(1-x)^2\bigr]\dd x
  =
  \frac{14}{5}C_A,
\]
and
\[
  2T_F\int_0^1
  x(1-x)\bigl(x^2+(1-x)^2\bigr)\dd x
  =
  \frac15T_F .
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:eec-real-collinear-coefficients}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[What the tree coefficient does and does not prove]
\label{rem:eec-tree-collinear-coefficient-status}
Lemma~\ref{lem:qcd-eec-tree-collinear-coefficient} is a derivation of
the first resolved real-emission coefficient in the small-angle expansion
under the stated collinear splitting convention.  It is not the full
small-angle EEC theorem.  Beyond this leading coefficient, one must define the
renormalized light-ray operator basis, include virtual terms and contact
conventions, solve the mixing problem, and match the endpoint expansion to
the separated-angle distribution in a fixed regulator and subtraction scheme.
The exact observable remains the detector distribution
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-definition}.
\end{remark}

\paragraph{Small-angle light-ray OPE structure.}
The symbolic matching formula \eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-ope-form} becomes
a mathematical statement only after the operator coordinates, endpoint
variable, regulator, and contact convention have been declared.  Let
\[
  \rho:=1-\zeta=1-\cos\chi,\qquad
  \rho\simeq \frac{\theta^2}{2}
\]
in the small-angle region.  A renormalized QCD light-ray OPE structure for this
endpoint consists of the following ingredients:
\[
  \mathcal D_{\rm EEC}^{\rm coll}
  =
  \bigl(
    \mathfrak L_{\mathbf n},\{\mathbb O_A\},
    \mathcal S_{\rm UV},\mathcal S_{\rm rap},
    \gamma_{AB},\eta_{AB},C_A
  \bigr).
\]
Here \(\mathfrak L_{\mathbf n}\) is a linear space of gauge-invariant
renormalized light-ray operator-valued distributions in the null direction
specified by \(\mathbf n\).  The indexed family
\(\{\mathbb O_A(\mathbf n;\mu,\nu)\}\) is a chosen coordinate basis of this
space, including the leading twist energy-flow moments and any operators
that mix with them under the declared symmetries.  The symbols
\(\mathcal S_{\rm UV}\) and \(\mathcal S_{\rm rap}\) denote, respectively,
the ultraviolet subtraction scheme and, when a lightlike Wilson-line or
rapidity singularity is present, the rapidity subtraction scheme.  The scale
\(\mu\) is the ultraviolet renormalization scale and \(\nu\) is the rapidity
scale; if a scheme has no separate rapidity regulator, all \(\nu\)-dependent
objects below are omitted.  The kernels \(\gamma_{AB}\) and \(\eta_{AB}\)
are distributional mixing kernels in whatever momentum-fraction, Mellin, or
angular variables label the basis.  The coefficient \(C_A(\rho,Q,\mu,\nu)\)
acts on smooth endpoint test functions in \(\rho\), with its separated-angle
density, endpoint subtractions, and \(\delta(\rho)\) contact coefficient all
specified by the same subtraction scheme.

With column-vector operator convention, the renormalization equations are
\begin{equation}
  \mu\frac{\dd}{\dd\mu}\mathbb O_A
  =
  -\sum_B \gamma_{AB}\otimes\mathbb O_B,\qquad
  \nu\frac{\dd}{\dd\nu}\mathbb O_A
  =
  -\sum_B \eta_{AB}\otimes\mathbb O_B ,
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-operator-rg}
\end{equation}
where \(\otimes\) denotes the convolution product in the operator labels and
matrix multiplication in the discrete labels.  Since the product of
detectors is a physical operator-valued distribution after the detector
observable is normalized, the endpoint expansion
\[
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n_1)\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n_2)
  \simeq
  \sum_A C_A\otimes \mathbb O_A
\]
must be independent of \(\mu\) and of \(\nu\).  Differentiating this
identity and using \eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-operator-rg} gives the
coefficient equations
\begin{equation}
  \mu\frac{\dd}{\dd\mu}C_A
  =
  \sum_B C_B\otimes\gamma_{BA},\qquad
  \nu\frac{\dd}{\dd\nu}C_A
  =
  \sum_B C_B\otimes\eta_{BA}.
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-coefficient-rg}
\end{equation}
This sign and transpose convention fixes the cancellation between the
anomalous dimension of the coefficient row and the anomalous dimension of the
operator column.  In a Mellin basis where the convolution diagonalizes,
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-coefficient-rg} reduces to ordinary matrix
multiplication in the remaining operator indices.

The separated-angle real-emission coefficient in
Lemma~\ref{lem:qcd-eec-tree-collinear-coefficient} supplies the positive
density on \(\rho>0\).  The renormalized endpoint coefficient also contains
endpoint subtractions and coincident-detector contact data.  To state this
coefficient, fix a small but finite endpoint interval
\(0<\rho<\rho_0\).  The plus distribution on this interval is defined by
\begin{equation}
  \int_0^{\rho_0}
  \left[\frac1\rho\right]_{\rho_0,+}\varphi(\rho)\,\dd\rho
  :=
  \int_0^{\rho_0}
  \frac{\varphi(\rho)-\varphi(0)}{\rho}\,\dd\rho
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-rho-plus-definition}
\end{equation}
for every smooth test function \(\varphi\) on \([0,\rho_0]\).  Therefore the
first singular real coefficient
\[
  \frac{\alpha_s}{2\pi}\,
  \frac{\Gamma_a^{\rm EEC}}{\rho}
\]
is promoted, in a renormalized endpoint coefficient, to the distributional
form
\begin{equation}
  C_a^{(1)}(\rho)
  =
  \frac{\alpha_s}{2\pi}\,
  \Gamma_a^{\rm EEC}
  \left[\frac1\rho\right]_{\rho_0,+}
  +
  K_a^{(1)}(\rho_0,\mu,\nu)\,\delta(\rho)
  +
  C_{a,{\rm reg}}^{(1)}(\rho).
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-renormalized-endpoint-coefficient}
\end{equation}
The constant \(K_a^{(1)}\) and the regular distribution
\(C_{a,{\rm reg}}^{(1)}\) are scheme- and matching-dependent.  The plus
prescription carries the coincident-detector subtraction that makes the
endpoint distribution act on test functions with finite endpoint limits.  The
remaining finite \(\delta(\rho)\) coefficient is fixed after the virtual
terms, operator renormalization, and matching convention are specified in the
same scheme.  Thus the real coefficient \(\Gamma_a^{\rm EEC}\) is a
necessary local input to the small-angle OPE; the anomalous dimensions and
the full coefficient of a renormalized light-ray operator are determined by
the complete scheme-dependent endpoint datum.

The dependence on the endpoint resolution boundary is also distributional,
not verbal.  For \(0<\rho_a<\rho_b\), define
\[
  D_{\rho_*}(\rho)
  :=
  \left[\frac{\Theta(\rho_*-\rho)}{\rho}\right]_{+}
\]
by
\[
  \langle D_{\rho_*},\varphi\rangle
  =
  \int_0^{\rho_*}
  \frac{\varphi(\rho)-\varphi(0)}{\rho}\,\dd\rho
\]
for smooth endpoint tests.  Then, as distributions on \([0,\rho_b]\),
\begin{equation}
  D_{\rho_b}
  =
  D_{\rho_a}
  +
  \frac{\mathbf 1_{\rho_a<\rho<\rho_b}}{\rho}
  -
  \log\frac{\rho_b}{\rho_a}\,\delta(\rho).
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-plus-resolution-shift}
\end{equation}
Testing the right-hand side against \(\varphi\) gives
\[
  \int_0^{\rho_a}\frac{\varphi-\varphi(0)}{\rho}\,\dd\rho
  +
  \int_{\rho_a}^{\rho_b}\frac{\varphi(\rho)}{\rho}\,\dd\rho
  -
  \log\frac{\rho_b}{\rho_a}\varphi(0)
  =
  \int_0^{\rho_b}\frac{\varphi-\varphi(0)}{\rho}\,\dd\rho .
\]
Thus enlarging the endpoint chart by the annulus
\(\rho_a<\rho<\rho_b\) adds the ordinary separated-angle integral over that
annulus and simultaneously shifts the coincident-detector contact coordinate
by the logarithmic amount required to keep constant tests unchanged.  This is
the finite-resolution form of the endpoint contact convention: a statement
such as ``drop the contact term'' is incomplete until the endpoint resolution
boundary and the compensating \(\delta(\rho)\) coordinate have both been
declared.

The eventwise moment identity
\eqref{eq:eventwise-eec-first-sum-rules} imposes a useful check on this
bookkeeping.  Let \(M_A\) be the energy-sum functional on the chosen
light-ray operator basis, so that \(M_A\mathbb O_A\) extracts the component
that contributes to the zeroth EEC moment.  Conservation of total energy says
that this functional has zero anomalous dimension:
\begin{equation}
  \sum_A M_A\,\gamma_{AB}=0,
  \qquad
  \sum_A M_A\,\eta_{AB}=0
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-moment-functional-rg-invariance}
\end{equation}
in any scheme that preserves the detector normalization.  Combining
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-coefficient-rg} with
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-moment-functional-rg-invariance} shows that the RG
evolution cannot change the zeroth moment; only the declared redistribution
between separated-angle weight and the \(\delta(\rho)\) contact term can
change the displayed representative.  This is why every perturbative EEC
formula must specify whether it includes the coincident-detector contact
term.  Without that convention, even a formally correct endpoint singularity
does not define the same distribution as the nonperturbative observable
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-definition}.

\begin{proposition}[Timelike one-loop momentum sum rule for the EEC endpoint]
\label{prop:qcd-eec-timelike-momentum-sum-rule}
The protected row in
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-moment-functional-rg-invariance} is visible already in the
one-loop final-state quark--gluon splitting kernels.  Let
\[
  D_0(x)=\left(\frac1{1-x}\right)_+
\]
with
\[
  \int_0^1D_0(x)\varphi(x)\,\dd x
  =
  \int_0^1\frac{\varphi(x)-\varphi(1)}{1-x}\,\dd x .
\]
In the trace-delta convention of this chapter, the leading timelike singlet
kernel for a daughter parton \(i\in\{q,g\}\) carrying energy fraction \(x\)
inside a parent \(j\in\{q,g\}\) may be written
\begin{align}
  P^{T,(0)}_{q\leftarrow q}(x)
  &=
  C_F\bigl(2D_0(x)-1-x+\tfrac32\delta(1-x)\bigr),
  \notag\\
  P^{T,(0)}_{g\leftarrow q}(x)
  &=
  C_F\,\frac{1+(1-x)^2}{x},
  \notag\\
  P^{T,(0)}_{q\leftarrow g}(x)
  &=
  2N_fT_F\bigl(x^2+(1-x)^2\bigr),
  \notag\\
  P^{T,(0)}_{g\leftarrow g}(x)
  &=
  2C_A\left[
    xD_0(x)+\frac{1-x}{x}+x(1-x)
  \right]
  +
  \frac{11C_A-4T_FN_f}{6}\delta(1-x).
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-timelike-one-loop-kernels}
\end{align}
Here \(q\) denotes the flavor-singlet quark-plus-antiquark energy-flow
coordinate; the factor \(2N_f\) in \(P^{T,(0)}_{q\leftarrow g}\) sums over
quarks and antiquarks.  Define the first energy-fraction moments
\[
  K_{i\leftarrow j}:=\int_0^1x\,P^{T,(0)}_{i\leftarrow j}(x)\,\dd x .
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
  K
  =
  \begin{pmatrix}
  -\frac43C_F & \frac23N_fT_F\\[4pt]
   \frac43C_F & -\frac23N_fT_F
  \end{pmatrix},
  \qquad
  (1\ \ 1)K=(0\ \ 0).
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-timelike-momentum-matrix}
\end{equation}
Thus the one-loop timelike mixing kernel redistributes energy between the
quark-singlet and gluon light-ray coordinates without changing the total
energy-flow row.  This is the perturbative kernel-level version of
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-moment-functional-rg-invariance}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The plus prescription gives
\[
  \int_0^1x^mD_0(x)\,\dd x
  =
  \int_0^1\frac{x^m-1}{1-x}\,\dd x
  =
  -H_m,
  \qquad H_0=0,\quad H_m=\sum_{r=1}^m\frac1r .
\]
For a quark parent,
\[
  \int_0^1xP^{T,(0)}_{q\leftarrow q}(x)\,\dd x
  =
  C_F\left(-2-\frac12-\frac13+\frac32\right)
  =
  -\frac43C_F,
\]
while
\[
  \int_0^1xP^{T,(0)}_{g\leftarrow q}(x)\,\dd x
  =
  C_F\int_0^1\bigl(1+(1-x)^2\bigr)\,\dd x
  =
  \frac43C_F .
\]
For a gluon parent,
\[
  \int_0^1xP^{T,(0)}_{q\leftarrow g}(x)\,\dd x
  =
  2N_fT_F
  \int_0^1x\bigl(x^2+(1-x)^2\bigr)\,\dd x
  =
  \frac23N_fT_F,
\]
and
\[
\begin{aligned}
  \int_0^1xP^{T,(0)}_{g\leftarrow g}(x)\,\dd x
  &=
  2C_A\left(-H_2+\frac12+\frac1{12}\right)
  +
  \frac{11C_A-4T_FN_f}{6} \\
  &=
  -\frac23N_fT_F .
\end{aligned}
\]
The two column sums are therefore zero.  The \(\delta(1-x)\) coefficient in
the gluon kernel is essential: omitting it would leave an uncancelled
\(-11C_A/6\) in the gluon-parent energy column.  Likewise, plus-prescribing
the quark pole is what turns the soft real-emission endpoint into the
negative quark-parent moment \(-4C_F/3\) needed to cancel the resolved gluon
daughter.  Both endpoint subtractions are therefore part of the detector
normalization mechanism, not optional notation.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Finite renormalized light-ray mixing chart.}
The preceding equations describe the continuum endpoint expansion, whose full
operator basis is infinite and distributional.  In an actual calculation one
uses a finite coordinate chart on this space.  The following finite chart is
the algebraic core that every higher-order small-angle EEC calculation must
instantiate before its anomalous dimensions and matching coefficients can be
compared across schemes.

Fix a finite set of light-ray operator labels \(\mathcal I_L\), for example a
spin, twist, flavor, and derivative truncation, and let
\(\mathbb O^{\rm reg}_I(\Lambda,\nu_0)\), \(I\in\mathcal I_L\), be regulated
gauge-invariant light-ray composites with the endpoint and rapidity regulator
specified.  A finite renormalized chart consists of an invertible matrix
\(Z_{IA}(\Lambda,\mu,\nu;\mathcal R)\) and renormalized operator coordinates
defined by
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb O_A(\mu,\nu;\mathcal R)
  =
  \sum_{I\in\mathcal I_L}
  (Z^{-1})_{AI}(\Lambda,\mu,\nu;\mathcal R)\,
  \mathbb O_I^{\rm reg}(\Lambda,\nu_0),
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-finite-chart-renormalized-operators}
\end{equation}
after the regulator limit is taken in matrix elements in the declared test
space.  If the regulated coordinates are independent of \(\mu\) after the
regulator and bare parameters are held fixed, then differentiating
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-finite-chart-renormalized-operators} gives
\begin{equation}
  \gamma
  =
  Z^{-1}\mu\frac{\dd Z}{\dd\mu},
  \qquad
  \mu\frac{\dd}{\dd\mu}\mathbb O=-\gamma\,\mathbb O ,
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-finite-chart-gamma-from-z}
\end{equation}
with column-vector notation.  A regulated coefficient row \(C^{\rm reg}\)
that pairs with the regulated operators as \(C^{\rm reg}\mathbb O^{\rm reg}\)
therefore gives the renormalized coefficient row
\begin{equation}
  C(\rho,Q,\mu,\nu;\mathcal R)
  =
  C^{\rm reg}(\rho,Q,\Lambda,\nu_0)\,
  Z(\Lambda,\mu,\nu;\mathcal R),
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-finite-chart-coefficient-renormalization}
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
  \mu\frac{\dd C}{\dd\mu}=C\,\gamma .
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-finite-chart-coefficient-rg}
\end{equation}
This is the finite-matrix derivation of the sign and transpose convention in
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-operator-rg}--\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-coefficient-rg}.
No physical statement is attached to \(Z\) or \(C\) separately: only the
paired distribution \(C\mathbb O\), together with its endpoint contact
coordinate, represents the detector product.

Finite scheme changes are coordinate changes on the same renormalized
light-ray space.  Let \(R(\mu,\nu)\) be an invertible finite matrix and set
\[
  \mathbb O'=R^{-1}\mathbb O,\qquad C'=C R .
\]
Then \(C'\mathbb O'=C\mathbb O\), while the anomalous-dimension matrix
becomes
\begin{equation}
  \gamma'
  =
  R^{-1}\gamma R
  +
  R^{-1}\mu\frac{\dd R}{\dd\mu},
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-finite-chart-scheme-gamma}
\end{equation}
and \(C'\) obeys \(\mu\dd C'/\dd\mu=C'\gamma'\).  Thus a quoted
``light-ray anomalous dimension'' is incomplete until its operator coordinate
chart is specified.  If \(M\mathbb O\) is the protected total-energy moment,
then \(M\gamma=0\).  In the changed coordinates \(M'=M R\) and
\[
  \mu\frac{\dd M'}{\dd\mu}=M'\gamma' .
\]
The stronger condition that the displayed row \(M\) is unchanged is therefore
not automatic; it is a restriction on admissible schemes, \(M R=M\).  This is
the finite-coordinate version of the normalization convention behind
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-moment-functional-rg-invariance}.

\paragraph{Finite transport and two-scale consistency.}
The finite chart also makes precise what is meant by solving the light-ray
mixing problem.  Write
\[
  t=\log\mu,\qquad r=\log\nu .
\]
For a single ultraviolet scale, let \(U(t,t_0)\) be the matrix solution of
\begin{equation}
  \partial_tU(t,t_0)=U(t,t_0)\gamma(t),
  \qquad
  U(t_0,t_0)=\mathbf 1 .
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-transport-u}
\end{equation}
When \(\gamma(t)\) at different scales does not commute,
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-transport-u} is the definition of the
path-ordered product; no choice of ordered exponential is meaningful without
the side on which \(\gamma\) acts.  With the row/column convention of
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-finite-chart-gamma-from-z}--\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-finite-chart-coefficient-rg},
the transported coordinates are
\begin{equation}
  C(t)=C(t_0)U(t,t_0),
  \qquad
  \mathbb O(t)=U(t,t_0)^{-1}\mathbb O(t_0),
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-transport-pair}
\end{equation}
and the paired endpoint distribution is independent of \(t\):
\[
  C(t)\mathbb O(t)=C(t_0)\mathbb O(t_0).
\]
Indeed, differentiating \(U^{-1}U=\mathbf 1\) gives
\[
  \partial_tU^{-1}=-\gamma(t)U^{-1},
\]
because \(\partial_tU=U\gamma\).  Thus
\[
  \partial_t\mathbb O(t)=-\gamma(t)\mathbb O(t),
  \qquad
  \partial_tC(t)=C(t)\gamma(t),
\]
and the two terms in \(\partial_t(C\mathbb O)\) cancel.  If \(M(t)\) is the
coordinate row representing the protected total-energy moment, its transport
law in a moving chart is
\begin{equation}
  \partial_tM(t)=M(t)\gamma(t).
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-moment-transport}
\end{equation}
The convention \(M(t)=M(t_0)\) for all \(t\) is therefore equivalent to
\(M\gamma(t)=0\) in that fixed chart.  This is the all-order version of the
finite left-null-vector check in
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-moment-functional-rg-invariance}.

If both ultraviolet and rapidity scales are present, the operator column is
declared to obey
\[
  \partial_t\mathbb O=-\gamma(t,r)\mathbb O,
  \qquad
  \partial_r\mathbb O=-\eta(t,r)\mathbb O .
\]
The two scale evolutions define a path-independent endpoint coordinate only
if the connection is flat on the chart:
\begin{equation}
  \partial_t\eta-\partial_r\gamma+[\gamma,\eta]=0 .
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-flatness}
\end{equation}
This equation is not an optional aesthetic condition.  It is the equality of
mixed derivatives of the same renormalized operator coordinate.  To see the
sign, compute
\[
  \partial_r\partial_t\mathbb O
  =
  -(\partial_r\gamma)\mathbb O+\gamma\eta\,\mathbb O,
  \qquad
  \partial_t\partial_r\mathbb O
  =
  -(\partial_t\eta)\mathbb O+\eta\gamma\,\mathbb O .
\]
Equating the two expressions gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-flatness}.  In a finite chart with nonzero
curvature
\[
  \mathcal F_{tr}
  :=
  \partial_t\eta-\partial_r\gamma+[\gamma,\eta],
\]
transporting \(C\) and \(\mathbb O\) along two different paths in
\((\mu,\nu)\)-space produces different coordinate representatives unless the
curvature action is compensated by additional operators or by a prescribed
scheme-change wall.  A calculation that quotes separate \(\mu\)- and
\(\nu\)-anomalous dimensions for the EEC endpoint has therefore supplied a
consistent renormalized light-ray chart only after
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-flatness}, the protected moment row, and the
endpoint contact convention have been checked in the same scheme.

This paragraph gives the structural consistency condition.  It is not itself
a small-angle EEC loop calculation.  In a concrete rapidity-factorized scheme
one must display the regulated endpoint operator basis, compute the two
matrices \(\gamma(t,r)\) and \(\eta(t,r)\) with the same subtraction and
contact-term convention, and then verify
\(\partial_t\eta-\partial_r\gamma+[\gamma,\eta]=0\) on that basis.  If the
finite basis is a truncation of an infinite operator space, the check must
also state the projected curvature
\(P_L(\partial_t\eta-\partial_r\gamma+[\gamma,\eta])P_L\), the curvature
components that leave the retained subspace, and the contact-coordinate
terms that compensate endpoint scheme changes.  Vanishing only after
discarding an omitted operator is not flatness of the retained chart; it is
an approximation statement requiring an omitted-operator remainder.  The
finite matrix check recorded in the companion script verifies the sign and
row/column convention of the flatness equation, including the derivative
terms, but it does not replace this scheme-specific QCD calculation.

\paragraph{Projected curvature and omitted light-ray coordinates.}
The most common failure mode in a finite light-ray calculation is not an
incorrect commutator sign, but an omitted operator channel.  Let \(P_L\) be the
projection onto the retained light-ray labels and \(Q_L=1-P_L\).  In a fixed
chart write
\[
  \gamma_{LL}=P_L\gamma P_L,\qquad
  \gamma_{LQ}=P_L\gamma Q_L,\qquad
  \gamma_{QL}=Q_L\gamma P_L,
\]
and similarly for \(\eta\).  If the full connection is flat on the enlarged
operator space and \(P_L\) is scale-independent, then the curvature computed
from the retained block alone is
\begin{equation}
  \partial_t\eta_{LL}-\partial_r\gamma_{LL}
  +[\gamma_{LL},\eta_{LL}]
  =
  \eta_{LQ}\gamma_{QL}-\gamma_{LQ}\eta_{QL}.
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-projected-curvature-omitted-block}
\end{equation}
Indeed, insert \(P_L+Q_L=1\) between the two factors in the commutator part of
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-flatness}.  Thus a nonzero retained curvature is
not automatically an inconsistency of the full endpoint construction; it is an
explicit omitted-channel term.  A finite small-angle EEC calculation that keeps
only \(P_L\) must therefore either include the right-hand side of
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-projected-curvature-omitted-block} in its remainder estimate
or enlarge the light-ray/contact-coordinate chart until the flatness check is
performed on the enlarged block.

This statement is coordinate covariant.  For a finite change of retained
coordinates \(R_L(t,r)\),
\[
  \mathbb O'_L=R_L^{-1}\mathbb O_L,\qquad C'_L=C_LR_L,
\]
one has
\[
  \gamma'_{LL}=R_L^{-1}\gamma_{LL}R_L+R_L^{-1}\partial_tR_L,
  \qquad
  \eta'_{LL}=R_L^{-1}\eta_{LL}R_L+R_L^{-1}\partial_rR_L,
\]
and the retained curvature transforms by conjugation,
\[
  \mathcal F'_{LL}=R_L^{-1}\mathcal F_{LL}R_L .
\]
Consequently a retained curvature cannot be removed by changing finite
coordinates inside the same retained space.  What can change is the split
between an operator block and endpoint contact coordinates, in which case the
flatness equation must be checked in the enlarged chart and the induced change
of contact distribution must be recorded in the endpoint convention.

\paragraph{Endpoint observable transport budget.}
The last step in a finite endpoint calculation is not the display of
\(\gamma\), \(\eta\), or a coefficient row.  It is the statement that the
retained chart gives a stable distribution when paired with endpoint detector
tests.  The following finite proposition is the algebraic budget behind that
statement.

\begin{proposition}[Finite endpoint observable transport budget]
\label{prop:qcd-eec-finite-endpoint-observable-transport-budget}
Fix a finite retained light-ray label set \(L\), an endpoint test
\(\varphi\), and one logarithmic scale \(t=\log\mu\).  Suppose the retained
small-angle endpoint contribution in a fixed state is represented by
\begin{equation}
  V_L(\varphi;t)
  =
  C_L(\varphi;t)\,O_L(t)
  +
  K_L(\varphi;t),
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-finite-endpoint-observable-chart}
\end{equation}
where \(C_L(\varphi;t)\) is a row of coefficient distributions evaluated on
\(\varphi\), \(O_L(t)\) is the column of retained light-ray matrix elements,
and \(K_L(\varphi;t)\) is the explicit endpoint contact coordinate.  Let
\(\gamma_{LL}(t)\) be the retained anomalous-dimension matrix, and let
\(D_L(\varphi;t)\) be the row produced by a scale-dependent change of
endpoint extension convention, such as moving an annulus into a plus-chart.
Assume
\begin{align}
  \partial_tO_L
  &=
  -\gamma_{LL}O_L+E_O,
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-endpoint-budget-operator}\\
  \partial_tC_L(\varphi)
  &=
  C_L(\varphi)\gamma_{LL}
  +D_L(\varphi)
  +E_C(\varphi),
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-endpoint-budget-coefficient}\\
  \partial_tK_L(\varphi)
  &=
  -D_L(\varphi)O_L+E_K(\varphi).
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-endpoint-budget-contact}
\end{align}
Then
\begin{equation}
  \partial_tV_L(\varphi;t)
  =
  E_C(\varphi;t)O_L(t)
  +
  C_L(\varphi;t)E_O(t)
  +
  E_K(\varphi;t).
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-endpoint-budget-residual}
\end{equation}
Consequently, for any interval \([t_0,t_1]\),
\begin{equation}
  \bigl|V_L(\varphi;t_1)-V_L(\varphi;t_0)\bigr|
  \leq
  \int_{t_0}^{t_1}
  \left(
    \|E_C(\varphi;t)\|\,\|O_L(t)\|
    +
    \|C_L(\varphi;t)\|\,\|E_O(t)\|
    +
    |E_K(\varphi;t)|
  \right)\dd t
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-endpoint-budget-bound}
\end{equation}
for any dual pair of finite vector norms.  In particular, exact operator
transport, exact coefficient transport, and the matching contact shift make
the retained endpoint observable independent of \(t\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Differentiate \eqref{eq:qcd-eec-finite-endpoint-observable-chart} and insert
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-endpoint-budget-operator}--\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-endpoint-budget-contact}:
\[
\begin{aligned}
  \partial_tV_L
  &=
  (C_L\gamma_{LL}+D_L+E_C)O_L
  +
  C_L(-\gamma_{LL}O_L+E_O)
  -
  D_LO_L
  +
  E_K .
\end{aligned}
\]
The anomalous-dimension terms cancel because the coefficient is a row and the
operator is a column.  The endpoint-extension row \(D_L\) cancels only because
the contact coordinate in
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-endpoint-budget-contact} carries the compensating sign.
This gives \eqref{eq:qcd-eec-endpoint-budget-residual}.  Integrating in \(t\)
and applying the finite norm inequality for a row-column pairing gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-endpoint-budget-bound}.
\end{proof}

The rows \(D_L\) are not new anomalous dimensions.  They record changes of
distributional representative at \(\rho=0\), such as the shift in
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-plus-resolution-shift}.  The residuals \(E_O,E_C,E_K\)
are where an actual finite-basis endpoint calculation must place its omitted
operator channels, projected curvature, approximate loop-order truncation,
and endpoint matching defects.  A claimed all-order renormalized light-ray
OPE for the EEC must drive the right side of
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-endpoint-budget-bound} to zero in the declared detector-test
topology, or must state the resulting approximation error.  Thus a mixing
matrix and a list of endpoint plus distributions become an observable theorem
only after this transport budget is supplied.

\paragraph{Minimal cusp-log flatness check.}
A useful first check is the part of a rapidity-factorized endpoint chart that
is forced by a cusp logarithm.  Work in a finite block in which the cusp
endomorphism \(A\) is fixed and commutes with itself at different scales.  Let
\(\Gamma_{\rm cusp}(t)\) denote the cusp coefficient in the same trace and
coupling convention as the endpoint calculation, and suppose the rapidity
dependence of the ultraviolet anomalous dimension contains
\begin{equation}
  \gamma_{\rm cusp}(t,r)
  =
  \Gamma_{\rm cusp}(t)\, r\, A .
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-cusp-log-gamma-chart}
\end{equation}
Then the rapidity anomalous dimension in the same chart must contain a term
\begin{equation}
  \eta_{\rm cusp}(t,r)
  =
  G_{\rm cusp}(t)\,A,
  \qquad
  \frac{\dd G_{\rm cusp}}{\dd t}=\Gamma_{\rm cusp}(t),
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-cusp-log-eta-chart}
\end{equation}
up to pieces whose \(t\)-derivative is zero in this block.  Indeed,
\[
  \partial_t\eta_{\rm cusp}
  =
  \Gamma_{\rm cusp}(t)A
  =
  \partial_r\gamma_{\rm cusp},
  \qquad
  [\gamma_{\rm cusp},\eta_{\rm cusp}]=0 .
\]
Thus the cusp-logarithmic part of
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-flatness} is satisfied.  With the opposite sign in
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-cusp-log-eta-chart}, the curvature would be
\(-2\Gamma_{\rm cusp}(t)A\).  The sign statement belongs to the declared
operator convention \(\partial_t\mathbb O=-\gamma\mathbb O\),
\(\partial_r\mathbb O=-\eta\mathbb O\).  A full small-angle EEC calculation
must still compute the non-cusp matrices, endpoint contact counterterms, and
operator components beyond this cusp block in one declared rapidity scheme.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Finite light-ray mixing truncation]
\label{ca:qcd-eec-finite-light-ray-mixing-truncation}
A finite small-angle EEC calculation based on a label set \(\mathcal I_L\)
is a controlled approximation only after it supplies:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the regulated light-ray composites
  \(\mathbb O_I^{\rm reg}\) and the subtraction matrix \(Z\);
  \item the endpoint test-function space on which the coefficient
  distributions \(C_A(\rho)\), including plus distributions and contact
  coordinates, act;
  \item the matrices \(\gamma\) and, when present, \(\eta\), with the
  protected energy-moment row and its scheme convention;
  \item the transport matrices or path-ordered products solving
  \eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-transport-u}, and, in a two-scale scheme, the
  flatness condition \eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-flatness};
  \item a remainder functional \(R_L(\varphi,\Psi)\) for the omitted
  operators, stated in the topology of the matrix elements or cross-section
  distributions being computed.
\end{enumerate}
Without the last item, a finite light-ray basis is a useful coordinate
truncation but not an approximation theorem for the EEC distribution.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Perturbative EEC endpoint calculations]
\label{ca:qcd-eec-endpoint-calculations}
A perturbative endpoint calculation of the EEC consists of a declared
endpoint variable, a factorization or light-ray OPE formula such as
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-ope-form} or
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-back-to-back-factorization}, anomalous dimensions and
matching coefficients through specified orders, a prescription for matching
the endpoint expansion to the separated-angle fixed-order distribution, and a
power correction estimate in \(\theta\) or \(q_T/Q\).  The exact observable
remains the hadronic detector distribution
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-definition}.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\paragraph{Endpoint matching as distributional gluing.}
The endpoint formulae above live in different distribution charts.  A
prediction for the full normalized EEC on \([-1,1]\) requires a gluing prescription,
because the contact coefficient at \(\zeta=1\), the perturbative
back-to-back delta coordinate at \(\zeta=-1\), and the separated-angle
density contribute to the same moment sum rules.

Let \(\mathcal R(\zeta)\) be the distribution on the open interval
\((-1,1)\) obtained from the declared bulk expression and the
overlap-subtracted small-angle and back-to-back endpoint formulae, all tested
against smooth functions whose support avoids the two endpoints.  Suppose its
first two moments exist after the declared endpoint subtractions:
\begin{equation}
  I_0[\mathcal R]=\langle \mathcal R,1\rangle,
  \qquad
  I_1[\mathcal R]=\langle \mathcal R,\zeta\rangle .
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-open-interval-moments}
\end{equation}
If the two endpoint atoms are retained as explicit scheme coordinates, write
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal E_{\rm match}(\zeta)
  =
  \mathcal R(\zeta)
  +K_+\,\delta(1-\zeta)
  +K_-\,\delta(1+\zeta).
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-matched-distribution-contact-terms}
\end{equation}
Here \(K_+\) is the coincident-detector contact coordinate and \(K_-\) is the
back-to-back endpoint coordinate generated by the perturbative source and
recoil expansion.  Only \(K_+\) has the direct eventwise interpretation
\eqref{eq:eventwise-eec-contact-weight}.  The two exact detector moment
identities \eqref{eq:eventwise-eec-first-sum-rules} impose
\begin{equation}
  I_0[\mathcal R]+K_+ +K_-=1,
  \qquad
  I_1[\mathcal R]+K_+ -K_-=0.
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-matching-moment-equations}
\end{equation}
When both endpoint atoms are left as matching coordinates, the solution is
\begin{equation}
  K_+
  =
  \frac{1-I_0[\mathcal R]-I_1[\mathcal R]}{2},
  \qquad
  K_-
  =
  \frac{1-I_0[\mathcal R]+I_1[\mathcal R]}{2}.
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-matching-delta-solution}
\end{equation}
If \(K_+\) is instead fixed independently by the detector contact definition,
then \eqref{eq:qcd-eec-matching-moment-equations} becomes a consistency test
on the bulk, small-angle, and back-to-back calculations in the chosen
subtraction scheme.  A mismatch is a statement about truncation, missing
power corrections, or incompatible endpoint conventions, rather than a new
observable.  This is the minimal matching structure required before a
perturbative endpoint formula can be compared with the nonperturbative
distribution \eqref{eq:qcd-eec-definition}.

\subsection{Multipoint Correlators and Energy-Flow Polynomials}

For a jet or event with a chosen positive energy scale \(E_{\mathrm{ref}}\),
define \(z_i=E_i/E_{\mathrm{ref}}\) and
\(\theta_{ij}\) to be the angular distance between directions \(i\) and \(j\).
For \(\beta>0\), the \(N\)-point energy correlation function used in jet
substructure has the form
\begin{equation}
  e_N^{(\beta)}
  =
  \sum_{i_1<\cdots<i_N}
  z_{i_1}\cdots z_{i_N}
  \prod_{a<b}
  \theta_{i_a i_b}^{\beta}.
  \label{eq:qcd-energy-correlation-function-jet}
\end{equation}
The strict positivity of \(\beta\) makes the observable collinear continuous:
when two labels become collinear, every factor distinguishing the split
vanishes or recombines into the total energy weight.  The soft behavior is
linear in the soft energy weight.  Thus \eqref{eq:qcd-energy-correlation-function-jet}
is infrared and collinear safe in the sense of the soft/collinear continuity
estimate for smeared energy flow above.

More generally, a finite graph \(G\) with vertices
\(\{1,\ldots,N\}\) defines an energy-flow polynomial
\begin{equation}
  \mathrm{EFP}_G^{(\beta)}
  =
  \sum_{i_1,\ldots,i_N}
  z_{i_1}\cdots z_{i_N}
  \prod_{(a,b)\in E(G)}
  \theta_{i_a i_b}^{\beta}.
  \label{eq:qcd-energy-flow-polynomial}
\end{equation}
This is again a polynomial functional of the calorimetric measure and angular
kernel.  It is a useful coordinate system on infrared-collinear safe event
information because it is built from the same positive detector measure
\(\mu_X\) rather than from colored partonic labels.  In an exact QCD
calculation the final states are hadrons; in a short-distance approximation,
quark and gluon variables enter through factorized coefficient functions,
evolution kernels, and power corrections for this color-singlet observable.

\subsection{Track Selectors and Charged-Energy Correlators}
\label{subsec:qcd-track-energy-correlators}

Collider detectors often measure a selected part of the calorimetric final
state, for example the energy carried by long-lived charged hadrons.  The
nonperturbative definition again begins with physical hadronic final states.
Let \(\mathfrak A_{\rm st}\) be the label set of stable hadron species in the
scattering representation, and fix a selector
\[
  \tau:\mathfrak A_{\rm st}\longrightarrow[0,1].
\]
For an ideal charged-track selector, \(\tau(a)=1\) for the species whose
charged tracks are included in the measurement and \(\tau(a)=0\) for the
species omitted by the tracking system.  A detector with efficiencies or
acceptance weights is represented by intermediate values of \(\tau\), once
those weights have been calibrated independently of the QCD short-distance
calculation.

For a hadronic final state
\[
  X=\{(p_r,a_r)\}_{r=1}^{N_X},
  \qquad
  \mathbf n_r=\mathbf p_r/|\mathbf p_r|,
\]
define the selected calorimetric measure
\begin{equation}
  \mu_X^\tau
  =
  \sum_{r\in X}\tau(a_r)p_r^0\,\delta_{\mathbf n_r}.
  \label{eq:qcd-track-calorimetric-measure}
\end{equation}
It satisfies \(0\le\mu_X^\tau\le\mu_X\) as positive measures.  The smeared
track detector on the outgoing multiplication representation is therefore
\[
  \widehat{\mathcal E}_X^\tau(f)
  =
  \int_{S^2}f\,\dd\mu_X^\tau
  =
  \sum_{r\in X}\tau(a_r)p_r^0 f(\mathbf n_r).
\]
Products of track detectors are products of this selected measure:
\begin{equation}
  \prod_{j=1}^{k}\widehat{\mathcal E}_X^\tau(f_j)
  =
  \int_{(S^2)^k}
  f_1(\mathbf n_1)\cdots f_k(\mathbf n_k)\,
  \dd\mu_X^\tau(\mathbf n_1)\cdots\dd\mu_X^\tau(\mathbf n_k).
  \label{eq:qcd-track-detector-product-measure}
\end{equation}
Thus track energy correlators are physical detector observables once the
selector \(\tau\) and the detector calibration have been specified.

The exact moment identities are selected-energy identities.  In a
center-of-mass event with \(z_r=p_r^0/Q\), set
\[
  e_\tau(X)=\sum_{r}\tau(a_r)z_r,\qquad
  \mathbf p_\tau(X)=\sum_{r}\tau(a_r)z_r\mathbf n_r .
\]
The eventwise two-point selected-energy distribution
\[
  E_{2,X}^{\tau}(\zeta)
  =
  \sum_{r,s\in X}
  \tau(a_r)\tau(a_s)z_rz_s\,
  \delta(\zeta-\mathbf n_r\cdot\mathbf n_s)
\]
obeys
\begin{equation}
  \int_{-1}^{1}E_{2,X}^{\tau}(\zeta)\,\dd\zeta
  =
  e_\tau(X)^2,
  \qquad
  \int_{-1}^{1}\zeta E_{2,X}^{\tau}(\zeta)\,\dd\zeta
  =
  |\mathbf p_\tau(X)|^2.
  \label{eq:qcd-track-eec-selected-moments}
\end{equation}
For \(\tau\equiv1\) these reduce to
\eqref{eq:eventwise-eec-first-sum-rules}.  For a proper track selector they
are additional nonperturbative event variables: the selected charged energy
and selected charged three-momentum fluctuate from event to event even when
the total energy and total three-momentum are fixed.

Perturbative calculations of selected-energy correlators require
nonperturbative track functions.  In a factorization scheme, a track function
for a parton label \(i\) is a positive distribution \(T_i(x,\mu)\) on
\([0,1]\), normalized by
\[
  \int_0^1 T_i(x,\mu)\,\dd x=1,
\]
whose moment
\[
  M_i^{(n)}(\mu)
  =
  \int_0^1 x^nT_i(x,\mu)\,\dd x
\]
is the \(n\)-th moment of the selected-energy fraction carried by hadrons in a
collinear jet initiated by \(i\), in the chosen scheme.  The functions
\(T_i\) are nonperturbative light-ray/fragmentation data; perturbation theory
controls their evolution and their convolution with hard and jet
coefficients.

The local collinear bookkeeping is fixed by energy partition.  If a parent
parton \(i\) splits into daughters \(j,k\) with energy fractions
\(z,1-z\), and the selected fractions in the daughter collinear sectors are
\(x_j,x_k\), then the selected fraction of the parent sector is
\[
  x=z x_j+(1-z)x_k .
\]
Therefore the real-splitting contribution to the \(n\)-th selected-fraction
moment has the binomial form
\begin{equation}
  M_{i\to jk}^{(n)}(z)
  =
  \sum_{a=0}^{n}
  \binom{n}{a}
  z^a(1-z)^{n-a}
  M_j^{(a)}M_k^{(n-a)} .
  \label{eq:qcd-track-function-binomial-moment}
\end{equation}
In particular,
\[
  M_{i\to jk}^{(1)}(z)=zM_j^{(1)}+(1-z)M_k^{(1)}
\]
and
\[
  M_{i\to jk}^{(2)}(z)
  =
  z^2M_j^{(2)}
  +(1-z)^2M_k^{(2)}
  +2z(1-z)M_j^{(1)}M_k^{(1)} .
\]
The last line separates the contact and resolved two-detector weights in a
track EEC calculation:
\begin{equation}
  w_{\tau,{\rm contact}}(z;j,k)
  =
  z^2M_j^{(2)}+(1-z)^2M_k^{(2)},\qquad
  w_{\tau,{\rm sep}}(z;j,k)
  =
  2z(1-z)M_j^{(1)}M_k^{(1)} .
  \label{eq:qcd-track-eec-contact-separated-weights}
\end{equation}
For the full calorimeter, \(M_i^{(n)}=1\) for every parton label and every
\(n\), and the separated weight reduces to the ordinary EEC weight
\(2z(1-z)\) in \eqref{eq:eec-ordered-collinear-weight}.

A controlled track-energy calculation must specify the selector \(\tau\), the
operator or fragmentation definition of the track functions \(T_i\), the
factorization scheme and scale \(\mu\), the evolution equation for \(T_i\) in
that scheme, the endpoint/contact convention for the selected detector
products, and the power remainder that compares the selected hadronic
observable \eqref{eq:qcd-track-detector-product-measure} with the finite
partonic factorization formula.  The selected-energy observable is defined at
the hadron level; the partonic track functions are the bridge used for its
short-distance expansion.

\subsection{Measured EEC Prediction Budgets}
\label{subsec:qcd-measured-eec-prediction-budgets}

The preceding endpoint and track formulae become physics only after they are
assembled into a measured final-state observable.  Let \(W_X(Q)\) denote the
normalized inclusive weight of the hadronic final state \(X\) produced by a
color-singlet source at center-of-mass energy \(Q\).  For a smooth angular
test \(\varphi\) on \([-1,1]\), the exact selected EEC observable is
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal O_\tau[\varphi;Q]
  =
  \sum_X W_X(Q)\,
  \int_{-1}^{1}
  \varphi(\zeta)\,E_{2,X}^{\tau}(\zeta)\,\dd\zeta .
  \label{eq:qcd-measured-selected-eec-observable}
\end{equation}
This is a color-singlet hadronic quantity.  The special case
\(\tau\equiv1\) is the full calorimetric EEC; a charged-track measurement is
obtained only after the selector and calibration entering
\(\mu_X^\tau\) have been fixed.

The exact selected moment constraints are
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal O_\tau[1;Q]
  =
  A_\tau(Q),
  \qquad
  \mathcal O_\tau[\zeta;Q]
  =
  B_\tau(Q),
  \label{eq:qcd-selected-eec-measured-moments}
\end{equation}
where
\[
  A_\tau(Q):=\sum_XW_X(Q)\,e_\tau(X)^2,
  \qquad
  B_\tau(Q):=\sum_XW_X(Q)\,|\mathbf p_\tau(X)|^2 .
\]
For the full calorimeter in a color-singlet center-of-mass event,
\(A_1(Q)=1\) and \(B_1(Q)=0\).  For a track selector these are
nonperturbative selected-energy moments.  They may be measured, modeled, or
factorized using track functions, but they are not fixed by total
four-momentum conservation alone.

Choose a smooth partition of the angular line into a bulk chart, a
small-angle chart near \(\zeta=1\), and a back-to-back chart near
\(\zeta=-1\).  In such a declared distributional chart, a leading-power
perturbative prediction has the form
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \mathcal O_\tau[\varphi;Q]
  &=
  \mathcal P_{\tau}^{\rm bulk}[\varphi;Q,\mu]
  +
  \mathcal P_{\tau}^{\rm coll}[\varphi;Q,\mu,\nu]
  +
  \mathcal P_{\tau}^{\rm rec}[\varphi;Q,\mu,\nu]
  \\
  &\quad
  +
  K_{+}^{\tau}(Q)\,\varphi(1)
  +
  K_{-}^{\tau}(Q)\,\varphi(-1)
  +
  R_{\tau,Q}[\varphi].
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:qcd-measured-eec-factorization-budget}
\end{equation}
The three open-interval terms are understood to be overlap-subtracted in the
declared scheme.  The bulk term is the fixed-order separated-angle
coefficient.  The collinear term is the light-ray or jet endpoint expansion
near \(\zeta=1\), with the operator mixing, plus-distribution convention,
and contact coordinate discussed above.  The recoil term is the
back-to-back factorization chart, with its hard, jet, soft, rapidity, and
Sudakov data.  If \(\tau\ne1\), each partonic coefficient entering these
charts must be lifted by the track functions in the same factorization
scheme; diagonal detector slots use higher track moments as in
\eqref{eq:qcd-track-eec-contact-separated-weights}, not just first moments.

Let \(\mathcal P_{\tau}^{\rm open}\) be the sum of the three
overlap-subtracted open-chart terms in
\eqref{eq:qcd-measured-eec-factorization-budget}, and set
\[
  I_0^\tau=\mathcal P_{\tau}^{\rm open}[1],
  \qquad
  I_1^\tau=\mathcal P_{\tau}^{\rm open}[\zeta].
\]
If the endpoint atoms are retained as matching coordinates, the selected
moment constraints require
\begin{equation}
  I_0^\tau+K_+^\tau+K_-^\tau=A_\tau,
  \qquad
  I_1^\tau+K_+^\tau-K_-^\tau=B_\tau .
  \label{eq:qcd-selected-eec-endpoint-matching-equations}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
  K_+^\tau
  =
  \frac{A_\tau+B_\tau-I_0^\tau-I_1^\tau}{2},
  \qquad
  K_-^\tau
  =
  \frac{A_\tau-B_\tau-I_0^\tau+I_1^\tau}{2}.
  \label{eq:qcd-selected-eec-endpoint-atom-solution}
\end{equation}
For \(\tau\equiv1\) this reduces to
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-matching-delta-solution}.  For a track measurement,
\(K_+^\tau\) contains the coincident selected-detector contact coordinate,
whereas \(K_-^\tau\) is a back-to-back endpoint coordinate of the matched
prediction.  Confusing these two endpoint atoms hides the physical difference
between selected-energy fragmentation data and recoil factorization.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Measured EEC prediction]
\label{ca:qcd-measured-eec-prediction}
A controlled perturbative prediction for a calorimetric or selected-track EEC
must state:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the hadronic detector observable
  \eqref{eq:qcd-measured-selected-eec-observable}, including the event
  normalization, selector \(\tau\), and detector calibration;
  \item the angular test space or finite bins, together with the endpoint
  partition and overlap-subtraction convention;
  \item the separated-angle fixed-order coefficient, the small-angle
  light-ray or jet endpoint chart, and the back-to-back recoil factorization
  chart, all in compatible subtraction schemes;
  \item the nonperturbative leading-power inputs, such as track functions or
  fragmentation data, and their evolution when the measurement is not fully
  calorimetric;
  \item the endpoint atoms \(K_\pm^\tau\), fixed or tested by
  \eqref{eq:qcd-selected-eec-endpoint-matching-equations};
  \item a residual functional \(R_{\tau,Q}\) separating perturbative
  truncation, omitted operator channels, endpoint matching, hadronization or
  shape-function effects, and ordinary power corrections.
\end{enumerate}
If the claimed errors in the three open charts are
\(\epsilon_{\rm bulk}(\varphi)\), \(\epsilon_{\rm coll}(\varphi)\), and
\(\epsilon_{\rm rec}(\varphi)\), if the endpoint atoms are known up to
\(\epsilon_+\) and \(\epsilon_-\), and if the remaining power or
hadronization error is \(\epsilon_{\rm pow}(\varphi)\), then the detector-test
pairing must obey a bound of the form
\begin{equation}
  \bigl|
    R_{\tau,Q}[\varphi]
  \bigr|
  \leq
  \epsilon_{\rm bulk}(\varphi)
  +
  \epsilon_{\rm coll}(\varphi)
  +
  \epsilon_{\rm rec}(\varphi)
  +
  |\varphi(1)|\epsilon_+
  +
  |\varphi(-1)|\epsilon_-
  +
  \epsilon_{\rm pow}(\varphi).
  \label{eq:qcd-measured-eec-residual-bound}
\end{equation}
Endpoint bins that probe \(Q\theta\) or \(q_T\) at hadronic scales are
outside a purely perturbative endpoint chart; the corresponding term in
\eqref{eq:qcd-measured-eec-residual-bound} must then be supplied by an
explicit nonperturbative shape, fragmentation, or track-function input.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\section{Current Correlators and the Hadronic Tensor}

Deep inelastic scattering probes a hadron by a local current.  The process is
inclusive:
\[
  e^-(k,\sigma)+N(P,s)\longrightarrow e^-(k',\sigma')+X,
  \qquad
  q:=k-k',
\]
where \(N\) is the target hadron and \(X\) runs over all hadronic final states
with total momentum \(P_X=P+q\).  The exchange momentum is spacelike,
\[
  Q^2:=-q^2>0,
  \qquad
  x_B:=\frac{Q^2}{2P\cdot q}.
\]
The variable \(x_B\) is the Bjorken scaling variable.

Figure~\ref{fig:qcd-dis-inclusive-kinematics} fixes the inclusive DIS
kinematics used below: the current transfers spacelike momentum \(q\), the
hadronic final state is summed over \(X\), and \(x_B=Q^2/(2P\cdot q)\).

\begin{figure}[H]
  \centering
  \resizebox{0.86\textwidth}{!}{%
  \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1cm,y=1cm,every node/.style={font=\scriptsize},
    photon/.style={decorate,decoration={snake,amplitude=1.35pt,segment length=6pt},
      line width=0.8pt,blue!70!black},
    fermion/.style={line width=0.85pt},
    hadron/.style={line width=0.9pt}]
    \coordinate (eIn) at (-4.3,1.45);
    \coordinate (eV) at (-0.8,1.05);
    \coordinate (eOut) at (3.0,1.72);
    \coordinate (hIn) at (-4.3,-1.2);
    \coordinate (hV) at (-0.8,-0.95);
    \coordinate (hOut) at (3.0,-0.55);

    \draw[fermion,-{Latex[length=2mm]}] (eIn)--(eV);
    \draw[fermion,-{Latex[length=2mm]}] (eV)--(eOut);
    \draw[photon,-{Latex[length=2mm]}] (eV)--(hV);
    \draw[hadron,-{Latex[length=2mm]}] (hIn)--(hV);
    \draw[hadron,-{Latex[length=2mm]}] (hV)--(hOut);
    \fill (eV) circle (2pt);
    \fill (hV) circle (2pt);

    \node[above] at (-3.1,1.45) {\(k,\sigma\)};
    \node[above] at (1.42,1.55) {\(k',\sigma'\)};
    \node[right,blue!70!black] at (-0.63,0.05) {\(q=k-k'\)};
    \node[below] at (-3.1,-1.22) {\(P,s\)};
    \node[below] at (1.40,-0.72) {\(X\)};
    \node[left] at (-4.35,1.45) {electron};
    \node[left] at (-4.35,-1.2) {hadron \(N\)};
    \node[right,align=left] at (3.08,-0.55) {summed hadronic\\final state};
  \end{tikzpicture}
  }
  \caption{Inclusive deep inelastic scattering.  The lepton line is treated
  perturbatively in the electromagnetic coupling, while the hadronic part is
  the current-current matrix element in QCD.}
  \label{fig:qcd-dis-inclusive-kinematics}
\end{figure}

Let the electromagnetic current be
\[
  J^\mu(x)=\sum_I e_I\,\bar q_I(x)\gamma^\mu q_I(x),
\]
where \(e_I\) is the electric charge of flavor \(I\).  At leading order in the
electromagnetic coupling, the amplitude for a fixed hadronic final state has
the form
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_{\sigma'\!,X;\sigma,s}
  =
  \bar u_{\sigma'}(k')\,e\gamma_\mu\,u_{\sigma}(k)\,
  \frac{-\ii}{q^2-\ii\epsilon}\,
  \bra{X}J^\mu(0)\ket{P,s}.
  \label{eq:qcd-dis-leading-amplitude}
\end{equation}
After summing over all hadronic final states \(X\) with the fixed transferred
momentum \(q\), the QCD part of the differential cross section is the
spin-averaged positive tensor
\begin{equation}
  W^{\mu\nu}(P,q)
  =
  \frac12\sum_s
  \sum_X (2\pi)^4\delta^{(4)}(P_X-P-q)\,
  \bra{P,s}J^\nu(0)\ket{X}
  \bra{X}J^\mu(0)\ket{P,s}.
  \label{eq:hadronic-tensor-definition}
\end{equation}
where \(\sum_X\) denotes the sum over species and the invariant phase-space
integrals for a complete set of hadronic states, using the same state
normalization as in the scattering chapters.  Completeness and translation
covariance give the equivalent form
\begin{equation}
  W^{\mu\nu}(P,q)
  =
  \frac12\sum_s
  \int\dd^4x\,\ee^{-\ii q\cdot x}
  \bra{P,s}J^\nu(x)J^\mu(0)\ket{P,s},
  \label{eq:hadronic-tensor-current-product}
\end{equation}
in those conventions.  Thus \(W^{\mu\nu}\) is a Wightman matrix element
between hadron states.  Its positivity follows directly from the sum over
\(X\) in
\eqref{eq:hadronic-tensor-definition}.

Current conservation gives
\[
  q_\mu W^{\mu\nu}=q_\nu W^{\mu\nu}=0 .
\]
For an unpolarized target, Lorentz covariance, current conservation, and
parity give two scalar structure functions.  Define
\[
  \Pi^\mu(P,q)
  :=
  P^\mu-\frac{P\cdot q}{q^2}q^\mu .
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
  W^{\mu\nu}(P,q)
  =
  \left(\eta^{\mu\nu}-\frac{q^\mu q^\nu}{q^2}\right)W_1(\nu,Q^2)
  +
  \Pi^\mu(P,q)\Pi^\nu(P,q)\,W_2(\nu,Q^2),
  \qquad
  \nu:=\frac{P\cdot q}{M},
  \label{eq:qcd-dis-tensor-decomposition}
\end{equation}
where \(M^2=P^2\).  Other common normalizations absorb powers of \(M\) and
\(P\cdot q\) into \(W_1,W_2\).

The support condition is kinematic.  If \(N\) is the lightest hadron with the
chosen conserved quantum numbers, then
\[
  (P+q)^2=P_X^2\ge M^2 .
\]
Since \(q^2=-Q^2\), this implies
\[
  2P\cdot q\ge Q^2,
  \qquad
  0<x_B\le1
\]
for the physical inclusive region.

The time-ordered forward Compton amplitude is
\begin{equation}
  T^{\mu\nu}(P,q)
  =
  \frac{\ii}{2}\sum_s
  \int\dd^4x\,\ee^{-\ii q\cdot x}
  \bra{P,s}\operatorname T\,J^\nu(x)J^\mu(0)\ket{P,s}.
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-compton-amplitude}
\end{equation}
Its discontinuity in the energy variable is determined by the same Wightman
matrix elements:
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Disc}\,T^{\mu\nu}(P,q)
  =
  2\pi
  \left[
    W^{\mu\nu}(P,q)
    +W^{\nu\mu}(P,-q)
  \right],
  \label{eq:qcd-dis-discontinuity}
\end{equation}
with the second term absent in the physical region \(P\cdot q>0\) for the
spacelike process.  Thus the inclusive cross section is controlled by the
absorptive part of a time-ordered current-current amplitude, and the
observable tensor is the Wightman object
\eqref{eq:hadronic-tensor-definition}.

The Bjorken limit is
\[
  Q^2\to\infty,
  \qquad
  x_B\ \text{fixed}.
\]
The short-distance region \(x\to0\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-compton-amplitude} is then controlled by the operator
product expansion of the two currents:
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname T\,J^\mu(x)J^\nu(0)
  \sim
  \sum_a C_a^{\mu\nu}(x,\mu)\,\mathcal O_a(0,\mu).
  \label{eq:dis-current-ope}
\end{equation}
The Wilson coefficients \(C_a^{\mu\nu}\) are determined by short-distance
renormalization and can be computed in perturbation theory at large \(Q\).  The
matrix elements
