\(\bra{P}\mathcal O_a(0,\mu)\ket{P}\) are long-distance hadronic data.

\section{Twist, Parton Distributions, and Factorization}
\label{sec:qcd-twist-parton-distributions-factorization}

\subsection{Twist and Light-Ray Operator Definitions}
\label{subsec:qcd-twist-light-ray-operator-definitions}

For a local symmetric traceless operator of Lorentz spin \(s\) and scaling
dimension \(\Delta\), its twist is
\[
  \tau:=\Delta-s .
\]
In an interacting theory \(\Delta\) is a renormalized scaling exponent of the
chosen operator basis.  The word ``twist'' in this section is therefore a
statement about the renormalized leading-power expansion, not only about the
engineering dimension of a classical monomial.  In the Bjorken limit, the
leading terms in the OPE are the smallest-twist operators compatible with the
quantum numbers of the currents.  A convenient way to collect the tower of
leading-twist matrix elements is by light-ray operators.

Let \(n^\mu\) be a future-directed lightlike vector, \(n^2=0\), and choose the
normalization \(P\cdot n>0\) for the target momentum.  For a representation
\(R\) of the gauge group, define the straight Wilson transporter
\[
  W_R(\lambda n,0)
  =
  \mathcal P
  \exp\left\{\ii\int_0^\lambda
  n^\mu A_\mu^a(sn)t_R^a\,\dd s\right\}.
\]
Here \(A_\mu=A_\mu^at^a\) is the same connection coordinate used throughout the
chapter, with \(D_\mu=\partial_\mu-\ii A_\mu\) and
\(-\frac1{4g^2}\operatorname{tr}F_{\mu\nu}F^{\mu\nu}\).  The symbol
\(\mathcal P\) orders factors with larger parameter \(s\) to the left.

\paragraph{Gauge covariance of the open light-ray operator.}
Let \(U(x)\) be a smooth gauge transformation in the fundamental
representation, and let \(U_R(x)\) be its image in a representation \(R\).
With the transformation law
\[
  A_\mu\longmapsto U A_\mu U^{-1}-\ii(\partial_\mu U)U^{-1},
  \qquad
  q(x)\longmapsto U(x)q(x),
\]
the transporter satisfies
\begin{equation}
  W_R(\lambda n,0)
  \longmapsto
  U_R(\lambda n)W_R(\lambda n,0)U_R(0)^{-1}.
  \label{eq:qcd-wilson-transporter-gauge-transformation}
\end{equation}
Consequently
\[
  \bar q(\lambda n)W_{\square}(\lambda n,0)\gamma\cdot n\,q(0)
\]
is a color-singlet bilocal operator before renormalization, and its
renormalized descendants remain gauge invariant if the regularization and
subtraction scheme preserve background gauge covariance.

Let \(W_R(s,0)\) denote the partial transporter from \(0\) to \(sn\).  It is the
solution of
\[
  \frac{\dd}{\dd s}W_R(s,0)
  =
  \ii n^\mu A_\mu^a(sn)t_R^a W_R(s,0),
  \qquad
  W_R(0,0)=\mathbf 1 .
\]
After the gauge transformation, the product
\(U_R(sn)W_R(s,0)U_R(0)^{-1}\) obeys the same differential equation with the
transformed connection and has the same initial value at \(s=0\).  Uniqueness of
solutions to this finite-dimensional linear ordinary differential equation
gives the stated transformation law.  The endpoint factors cancel against the
transformations of \(\bar q(\lambda n)\) and \(q(0)\), because the gamma matrix
acts on spinor indices and is the identity in color space.

For an unpolarized target, write
\[
  \langle \mathcal X\rangle_{P,H}
  :=
  \frac12\sum_s\bra{P,s}\mathcal X\ket{P,s},
\]
with the one-particle normalization fixed in the scattering chapters.  The
renormalized quark light-ray operator and its parton distribution are
\begin{align}
  \mathbb O_q(\lambda n;\mu)
  &:=
  \left[
    \bar q(\lambda n)W_{\square}(\lambda n,0)\gamma\cdot n\,q(0)
  \right]_{\mu},
  \label{eq:qcd-quark-light-ray-operator}\\
  f_{q/H}(x,\mu)
  &:=
  \frac1{2P\cdot n}
  \int\frac{\dd\lambda}{2\pi}\,
  \ee^{-\ii x\lambda P\cdot n}
  \langle\mathbb O_q(\lambda n;\mu)\rangle_{P,H}.
  \label{eq:pdf-light-ray-definition}
\end{align}
The factor \(2P\cdot n\) fixes the convention so that a free quark target has
\(f_{q/q}(x)=\delta(1-x)\).  The antiquark distribution is defined by the
charge-conjugate bilocal with the fields interchanged and the transporter
running between the same endpoints.  The gluon distribution is defined from
the adjoint light-ray operator
\begin{align}
  \mathbb O_g(\lambda n;\mu)
  &:=
  \left[
    F^a_{n\rho}(\lambda n)
    W_{\rm ad}^{ab}(\lambda n,0)
    F_n^{b\rho}(0)
  \right]_{\mu},
  \qquad
  F_{n\rho}:=n^\mu F_{\mu\rho},
  \label{eq:qcd-gluon-light-ray-operator}\\
  f_{g/H}(x,\mu)
  &:=
  \frac1{2x(P\cdot n)^2}
  \int\frac{\dd\lambda}{2\pi}\,
  \ee^{-\ii x\lambda P\cdot n}
  \langle\mathbb O_g(\lambda n;\mu)\rangle_{P,H},
  \qquad 0<x<1 .
  \label{eq:qcd-gluon-pdf-definition}
\end{align}
The factor \(1/x\) is part of the conventional normalization of the gluon
light-ray distribution; it is what makes the \(N\)-th Mellin moment correspond
to the spin-\(N\) local gluon operator below.  Possible singular behavior at
\(x=0\) belongs to the small-\(x\) problem and is not hidden inside the
definition.

\begin{definition}[Renormalized integrated PDF coordinate]
\label{def:qcd-renormalized-integrated-pdf-datum}
For a hadron species \(H\), a renormalized integrated PDF coordinate consists of
the following objects.
\begin{enumerate}
  \item A nonperturbative QCD presentation, or a finite-regulator
  approximation to one, which supplies normalized color-singlet hadron states
  \(\ket{P,s}\) with \(P^2=M_H^2\) and \(P\cdot n>0\).
  \item A lightlike direction \(n^\mu\), an orientation of the straight
  segment from \(0\) to \(\lambda n\), and the representation labels of the
  Wilson transporters appearing in
  \eqref{eq:qcd-quark-light-ray-operator} and
  \eqref{eq:qcd-gluon-light-ray-operator}.
  \item A finite ultraviolet regulator \(\Lambda\) and regulated
  gauge-invariant bilocal composites
  \(\mathbb O_a^\Lambda(\lambda n)\), smeared in \(\lambda\) before any
  distributional limit is taken.
  \item A subtraction and factorization scheme at scale \(\mu\), encoded by
  a convolutional coordinate map \(Z_{ab}\) from
  \(\mathbb O_a^\Lambda\) to renormalized light-ray coordinates
  \(\mathbb O_b(\mu)\) in the sense of
  \eqref{eq:qcd-light-ray-renormalization-convolution}.
  \item A declared distribution space in the light-cone fraction variable
  \(x\), including the endpoint contact convention at \(x=0,1\), on which the
  Fourier transform in \(\lambda P\cdot n\) is paired with test functions.
\end{enumerate}
The integrated PDF \(f_{a/H}(x,\mu)\) is the resulting matrix-element
distribution.  In the conventions of
\eqref{eq:pdf-light-ray-definition} and
\eqref{eq:qcd-gluon-pdf-definition},
\begin{align}
  f_{q/H}(\,\cdot\,,\mu)
  &=
  \frac{1}{2P\cdot n}\,
  \mathcal F_{\lambda P\cdot n\to x}
  \bigl[\langle\mathbb O_q(\lambda n;\mu)\rangle_{P,H}\bigr],
  \label{eq:qcd-pdf-datum-quark-fourier-coordinate}\\
  f_{g/H}(\,\cdot\,,\mu)
  &=
  \frac{1}{2x(P\cdot n)^2}\,
  \mathcal F_{\lambda P\cdot n\to x}
  \bigl[\langle\mathbb O_g(\lambda n;\mu)\rangle_{P,H}\bigr],
  \label{eq:qcd-pdf-datum-gluon-fourier-coordinate}
\end{align}
where the second equality is an equality in the declared distribution space
on which multiplication by \(1/x\) has been specified.  The symbol
\(\mathcal F_{\lambda P\cdot n\to x}\) denotes the Fourier transform with
the phases displayed in the defining formulae above.  Equations
\eqref{eq:qcd-pdf-datum-quark-fourier-coordinate} and
\eqref{eq:qcd-pdf-datum-gluon-fourier-coordinate} define renormalized
operator coordinates.  Support in \(0\le x\le1\), positivity properties,
probability language, and the appearance of the same distribution in a
measured structure function are additional spectral, scheme, and
factorization statements; they are not part of the definition of the
renormalized light-ray matrix element.
\end{definition}

The preceding equations are nonperturbative operator definitions once the
underlying quantum field theory supplies the renormalized light-ray operators
\(\mathbb O_a(\lambda n;\mu)\) as operator-valued distributions, or at least as
matrix-element distributions between the hadron states under consideration.
They are not definitions in terms of on-shell quarks or gluons, and they do not
presuppose a colored particle interpretation.  In four-dimensional continuum
QCD this existence statement is tied to the still-open problem of constructing
the theory and to the additional ultraviolet problem of renormalizing lightlike
Wilson-line composites.  A gauge-invariant regulator can define finite
approximants, but the continuum lightcone limit, the operator-renormalization
limit, and the factorization theorem are separate assertions.  Equal-time
Euclidean bilocals used in lattice quasi-PDF or pseudo-PDF methods are therefore
matching observables for the light-ray definition, not the definition itself.

The subscript \(\mu\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-quark-light-ray-operator}--\eqref{eq:qcd-gluon-pdf-definition}
means that the singular lightlike bilocal has been defined in a specified
regularization and factorization scheme.  Let
\(\mathbb O_a^\Lambda(x)\) denote the Fourier-coordinate operator obtained
from the same gauge-invariant light-ray composite in a finite ultraviolet
regulator \(\Lambda\), after the path geometry, endpoint prescription, and
finite regulator have been fixed.  This cutoff-regulated operator is not a
new physical observable; it is the finite-regulator coordinate from which the
renormalized light-ray coordinate is obtained.  For integrated collinear PDFs,
the coordinate change is a convolution in the light-cone momentum fraction:
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb O^{\Lambda}_{a}(x)
  =
  \sum_b
  \int_x^1\frac{\dd z}{z}\,
  Z_{ab}\!\left(\frac{x}{z},\mu,\Lambda\right)
  \mathbb O_b(z;\mu),
  \label{eq:qcd-light-ray-renormalization-convolution}
\end{equation}
where \(a,b\) range over quarks, antiquarks, and gluons, and the convolution
is understood after pairing with test functions in a distribution space whose
endpoint contact conventions have been declared.  This equation is a
definition of the renormalized light-ray coordinates.  It separates
regularization, the introduction of the finite object
\(\mathbb O_a^\Lambda\), from renormalization, the choice of the finite
coordinate map \(Z\) and of the operator coordinate \(\mathbb O_b(\mu)\).
For TMDs or other observables with unresolved transverse momentum, an
additional rapidity renormalization is required; it is not part of the
integrated PDF definition used in inclusive DIS.

The DGLAP kernel is the infinitesimal form of this operator-coordinate map,
not a transition probability for physical colored asymptotic states.  Let
\(Z^{-1}\) be the convolution inverse in the chosen finite channel basis.
Differentiating
\eqref{eq:qcd-light-ray-renormalization-convolution} at fixed
\(\mathbb O^\Lambda\) gives
\[
  0
  =
  \sum_b(\mu\partial_\mu Z_{ab})\otimes\mathbb O_b(\mu)
  +
  \sum_b Z_{ab}\otimes\mu\partial_\mu\mathbb O_b(\mu),
\]
where \(\otimes\) denotes the same light-cone fraction convolution.  Hence
\begin{equation}
  \mu\partial_\mu\mathbb O_c(x;\mu)
  =
  \sum_b
  \int_x^1\frac{\dd z}{z}\,
  P_{cb}\!\left(\frac{x}{z},g(\mu)\right)
  \mathbb O_b(z;\mu),
  \qquad
  P_{cb}:=
  -\sum_a Z^{-1}_{ca}\otimes\mu\partial_\mu Z_{ab}.
  \label{eq:qcd-light-ray-operator-dglap-rg}
\end{equation}
Taking hadron matrix elements of
\eqref{eq:qcd-light-ray-operator-dglap-rg} gives
\eqref{eq:dglap-evolution} below.  The finite perturbative calculation of
\(P\) is a calculation of the ultraviolet coordinate change of the light-ray
operator.  The subsequent use of \(P\) in a measured DIS observable still
requires the leading-power factorization statement.

\paragraph{Local moments of the light-ray definition.}
The light-ray definition contains the local twist-two tower as its Taylor
coefficients at zero separation.  This statement is often quoted as a formal
identity between PDFs and partons; here it is only a statement about the
renormalized Wilson-line operator in
\eqref{eq:qcd-quark-light-ray-operator}.  Define the left covariant
derivative on the transported antiquark endpoint by
\[
  \bar q\,\overleftarrow D_n
  :=
  n^\mu\partial_\mu\bar q+\ii\,\bar q\,n^\mu A_\mu,
  \qquad n^2=0 .
\]
The sign is fixed by the same convention
\(D_\mu q=(\partial_\mu-\ii A_\mu)q\) used in the Wilson transporter above.
Since
\[
  \frac{\dd}{\dd\lambda}
  \bigl(\bar q(\lambda n)W_\square(\lambda n,0)\bigr)
  =
  \bigl(\bar q\,\overleftarrow D_n\bigr)(\lambda n)
  W_\square(\lambda n,0),
\]
iteration gives the short-distance expansion
\begin{equation}
  \bar q(\lambda n)W_\square(\lambda n,0)\gamma\cdot n\,q(0)
  =
  \sum_{N\ge0}\frac{\lambda^N}{N!}\,
  \bar q(0)(\overleftarrow D_n)^N\gamma\cdot n\,q(0)
  \label{eq:qcd-quark-light-ray-taylor-left}
\end{equation}
as a formal operator identity before subtraction, and as a renormalized
operator-coordinate identity after the corresponding local and bilocal
subtractions have been matched.  It is useful to absorb the endpoint sign into
the moment operator
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal O_{q,N}^{\leftarrow}(n;\mu)
  :=
  \left[
    \bar q(0)(-\ii\overleftarrow D_n)^N
    \gamma\cdot n\,q(0)
  \right]_{\mu}.
  \label{eq:qcd-quark-left-moment-operator}
\end{equation}
The minus sign is not optional: a free one-quark matrix element of
\(\bar q(\lambda n)\gamma\cdot n q(0)\) is proportional to
\(\exp(\ii\lambda P\cdot n)\), so \(-\ii\overleftarrow D_n\) has eigenvalue
\(P\cdot n\) on the left endpoint.  With the Fourier convention in
\eqref{eq:pdf-light-ray-definition}, the inverse distributional relation is
\[
  \frac{1}{2P\cdot n}
  \langle\mathbb O_q(\lambda n;\mu)\rangle_{P,H}
  =
  \int_{\mathbb R}\dd x\,
  \ee^{\ii x\lambda P\cdot n}f_{q/H}(x,\mu),
\]
whenever the pairing with test functions justifies inversion.  Differentiating
at \(\lambda=0\) therefore gives, for \(N\ge0\),
\begin{equation}
  \int_0^1\dd x\,x^N f_{q/H}(x,\mu)
  =
  \frac{
    \langle\mathcal O_{q,N}^{\leftarrow}(n;\mu)\rangle_{P,H}
  }{
    2(P\cdot n)^{N+1}
  } .
  \label{eq:qcd-quark-pdf-moment-left-operator}
\end{equation}
The familiar symmetric traceless tensor
\(\bar q\gamma^{(\mu_0}\ii D^{\mu_1}\cdots\ii D^{\mu_N)}q\) is obtained by
polarizing in the null vector \(n\) and changing from the left-endpoint
representative to a symmetric representative.  In forward matrix elements the
difference is a sum of total-derivative representatives with fixed momentum
transfer zero; in off-forward matrix elements those total derivatives are
precisely the terms that produce GPD polynomiality in
Section~\ref{sec:qcd-gpd-light-ray-matrix-elements}.  Thus
\eqref{eq:qcd-quark-pdf-moment-left-operator} is the convention-clean moment
statement for the present forward PDF definition, while the symmetric local
tensor is a different coordinate on the same leading-twist operator tower.

For the gluon definition the extra factor \(1/x\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-gluon-pdf-definition} shifts the moment index.  Let
\(\overleftarrow D_{n,{\rm ad}}\) be the left covariant derivative acting on
the adjoint field at \(\lambda n\), including the adjoint connection in the
same Wilson-transporter convention.  For \(N\ge1\), define
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal O_{g,N}^{\leftarrow}(n;\mu)
  :=
  \left[
    F^a_{n\rho}(0)
    (-\ii\overleftarrow D_{n,{\rm ad}})^{N-1}
    F_n^{a\rho}(0)
  \right]_{\mu},
  \label{eq:qcd-gluon-left-moment-operator}
\end{equation}
with the color contraction written after transporting the left endpoint to
zero.  The inverse relation following from
\eqref{eq:qcd-gluon-pdf-definition} is
\[
  \frac{1}{2(P\cdot n)^2}
  \langle\mathbb O_g(\lambda n;\mu)\rangle_{P,H}
  =
  \int_{\mathbb R}\dd x\,
  \ee^{\ii x\lambda P\cdot n}\,x f_{g/H}(x,\mu),
\]
and therefore
\begin{equation}
  \int_0^1\dd x\,x^N f_{g/H}(x,\mu)
  =
  \frac{
    \langle\mathcal O_{g,N}^{\leftarrow}(n;\mu)\rangle_{P,H}
  }{
    2(P\cdot n)^{N+1}
  },
  \qquad N\ge1 .
  \label{eq:qcd-gluon-pdf-moment-left-operator}
\end{equation}
Equations
\eqref{eq:qcd-quark-pdf-moment-left-operator} and
\eqref{eq:qcd-gluon-pdf-moment-left-operator} are moment identities inside a
specified renormalized operator scheme.  They do not assert positivity,
support, or factorization.  Positivity and support require the spectral
interpretation of the hadron matrix element in the relevant scattering
representation; factorization requires the separate leading-power hypothesis
stated below.

\subsection{Euclidean Spatial Bilocals and Large-Momentum Matching}
\label{subsec:qcd-euclidean-bilocals-quasi-pdfs}

Lattice access to the light-ray definitions
\eqref{eq:pdf-light-ray-definition}--\eqref{eq:qcd-gluon-pdf-definition}
uses different operator coordinates.  The basic object is a spacelike
equal-time bilocal, not a lightlike bilocal.  Let \(e_3\) be a fixed unit
spatial vector and let \(P^\mu=(E_P,0,0,P_3)\), \(P_3>0\), be a one-hadron
momentum in a finite-volume regulator with a transfer matrix and a
gauge-invariant Hilbert space.  For a Dirac matrix \(\Gamma\) and a real
spatial separation \(z\), define the regulated spatial Wilson-line operator
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal Q_\Gamma(z;\Lambda)
  :=
  \left[
    \bar q(z e_3)\,
    W_{\square}(z e_3,0)\,
    \Gamma\,q(0)
  \right]_{\Lambda}.
  \label{eq:qcd-spatial-bilocal-operator}
\end{equation}
Here \(\Lambda\) denotes the complete ultraviolet and finite-volume regulator
data, including the lattice spacing and box when the operator is realized on a
lattice.  The Wilson transporter is along the straight spatial segment.  Its
linear length divergence, endpoint divergences, and finite subtraction are
part of the operator-renormalization datum; they are not part of the
definition of the light-ray PDF.

At finite gauge-covariant regulator, the operator
\(\mathcal Q_\Gamma(z;\Lambda)\) is gauge invariant as a color-singlet
bilocal.  A background-gauge-covariant finite-part prescription therefore
produces a gauge-invariant renormalized spatial-bilocal matrix element.
This is the endpoint-cancellation argument of
the Wilson-transporter covariance calculation above, with the lightlike path
\(s n\) replaced by the spatial path \(s z e_3\), \(0\le s\le1\).  The
parallel transporter transforms as
\[
  W_{\square}(z e_3,0)
  \longmapsto
  U(z e_3)W_{\square}(z e_3,0)U(0)^{-1}.
\]
The factor \(U(0)^{-1}\) cancels the transformation of \(q(0)\), the factor
\(U(z e_3)\) cancels the transformation of \(\bar q(z e_3)\), and \(\Gamma\)
acts only on spinor indices.  The finite-part map changes regulator
coordinates and operator coordinates but carries no free color index when it
is background gauge covariant.

Let
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal M_{\Gamma/H}^{\mathcal R}(z,P_3)
  :=
  \frac{1}{2P_3}
  \bra{P,H}\mathcal Q_\Gamma^{\mathcal R}(z)\ket{P,H},
  \qquad
  \nu:=P_3z ,
  \label{eq:qcd-spatial-bilocal-matrix-element}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal R\) denotes a specified finite-part prescription.  A quasi-PDF
coordinate is the Fourier transform
\begin{equation}
  \widetilde f_{\Gamma/H}^{\mathcal R}(x,P_3)
  :=
  P_3\int_{\mathbb R}\frac{\dd z}{2\pi}\,
  \ee^{\ii xP_3z}\,
  \mathcal M_{\Gamma/H}^{\mathcal R}(z,P_3),
  \label{eq:qcd-quasi-pdf-coordinate}
\end{equation}
understood as a tempered distribution in \(x\) after smearing.  The prefactor
\(P_3\) fixes the inverse convention
\[
  \mathcal M_{\Gamma/H}^{\mathcal R}(z,P_3)
  =
  \int_{\mathbb R}\dd x\,
  \ee^{-\ii xP_3z}
  \widetilde f_{\Gamma/H}^{\mathcal R}(x,P_3)
\]
for distributions for which the Fourier inversion is valid.  A pseudo-PDF or
Ioffe-time coordinate instead regards the same matrix element as a function,
or distribution, of the Ioffe time \(\nu=P_3z\) and spacelike length
\(z^2>0\) in Euclidean notation:
\begin{equation}
  \mathfrak M_{\Gamma/H}^{\mathcal R}(\nu,z^2)
  :=
  \mathcal M_{\Gamma/H}^{\mathcal R}(z,P_3).
  \label{eq:qcd-pseudo-itd-coordinate}
\end{equation}
When \(\mathfrak M_{\Gamma/H}^{\mathcal R}(0,z^2)\ne0\), the reduced
Ioffe-time coordinate
\[
  \mathfrak M_{\rm red}(\nu,z^2)
  :=
  \frac{\mathfrak M_{\Gamma/H}^{\mathcal R}(\nu,z^2)}
       {\mathfrak M_{\Gamma/H}^{\mathcal R}(0,z^2)}
\]
cancels any multiplicative Wilson-line factor depending only on \(z^2\) in
that scheme.  It does not remove matching coefficients, target-mass effects,
or higher-twist matrix elements.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Large-momentum matching statement]
\label{ca:qcd-large-momentum-quasi-pdf-matching}
Fix a renormalized spatial-bilocal scheme \(\mathcal R\), a light-ray
factorization scheme at scale \(\mu\), and a test function
\(h\in C_c^\infty(\mathbb R)\).  A large-momentum matching statement for
\eqref{eq:qcd-quasi-pdf-coordinate} consists of kernels
\(C_{\Gamma a}^{\mathcal R}\), with \(a\) running over the light-ray operator
basis, such that
\begin{align}
  \left\langle
  \widetilde f_{\Gamma/H}^{\mathcal R}(\,\cdot\,,P_3),h
  \right\rangle
  &=
  \sum_a\int_0^1\dd y\, f_{a/H}(y,\mu)
  \int_{\mathbb R}\dd x\,h(x)\,
  \frac1y
  C_{\Gamma a}^{\mathcal R}
  \left(\frac{x}{y},\frac{\mu}{P_3}\right)
  \notag\\
  &\hspace{1.0cm}
  +R_{\Gamma,H}^{\mathcal R}[h;P_3,\mu].
  \label{eq:qcd-quasi-pdf-matching-distributional}
\end{align}
The statement is controlled only after the topology of the remainder has been
specified.  A typical leading-power version requires, for fixed compact
support of \(h\),
\begin{equation}
  |R_{\Gamma,H}^{\mathcal R}[h;P_3,\mu]|
  \le
  C_h
  \left(
    \frac{M_H^2}{P_3^2}
    +\frac{\Lambda_{\rm had}^2}{P_3^2}
  \right)
  +
  R_{\rm reg}[h;a,L,P_3],
  \label{eq:qcd-quasi-pdf-power-remainder}
\end{equation}
where \(M_H\) is the hadron mass, \(\Lambda_{\rm had}\) is a hadronic scale
attached to higher-twist matrix elements, and \(R_{\rm reg}\) records finite
lattice-spacing, finite-volume, and finite-operator-length errors before the
continuum and infinite-volume limits are taken.  Endpoint regions, small
\(x\), and threshold \(x\to1\) require additional test-function restrictions
or separate factorization data.
\end{controlledapproximation}

The kernels in
Controlled Approximation~\ref{ca:qcd-large-momentum-quasi-pdf-matching} are
short-distance coordinates.  In perturbation theory they are determined by
matching matrix elements of the spatial bilocal and the light-ray operator in
the same infrared state, so the infrared dependence cancels in the difference.
That perturbative statement is not, by itself, a nonperturbative theorem about
the large-\(P_3\) limit of QCD.  A theorem-level version would need a
renormalized construction of the spatial Wilson-line operator, a spacelike
short-distance OPE with remainder estimates uniform after hadron matrix
elements, and a proof that the large-momentum limit converts the spacelike
operator coordinates to the light-ray coordinates in the stated distributional
topology.

\paragraph{Scheme covariance of finite matching kernels.}
Let \(f\) denote the column vector of light-ray PDFs in a convolution algebra,
and suppose a quasi-PDF coordinate satisfies
\(\widetilde f=C\otimes f\) at leading power.  If a finite light-ray scheme
change is \(f'=R\otimes f\), where \(R\) has a convolution inverse, then the
same quasi-PDF coordinate is written in the primed scheme as
\[
  \widetilde f=C'\otimes f',
  \qquad
  C'=C\otimes R^{-1}.
\]
If a linear charge functional \(N(f)=\sum_a n_a\int_0^1 f_a(y)\,\dd y\) is
preserved by \(R\) and the matching kernel satisfies
\[
  \sum_i m_i\int_{\mathbb R} C_{ia}(\xi)\,\dd\xi=n_a
\]
for the corresponding quasi-PDF charge weights \(m_i\), then the matched
quasi-PDF has the same charge \(N\) at leading power.

Associativity of convolution gives
\[
  (C\otimes R^{-1})\otimes(R\otimes f)
  =
  C\otimes(R^{-1}\otimes R)\otimes f
  =
  C\otimes f.
\]
For the charge statement, integrate the matching formula over \(x\) with
weights \(m_i\).  The change of variables \(x=y\xi\), \(y>0\), gives
\[
  \sum_i m_i\int_{\mathbb R}\dd x\,\frac1y C_{ia}(x/y)
  =
  \sum_i m_i\int_{\mathbb R}\dd\xi\,C_{ia}(\xi)
  =
  n_a.
\]
The remaining \(y\)-integral is exactly \(N(f)\).  The assumed preservation of
\(N\) by \(R\) says that the same value is obtained in the primed light-ray
coordinates.

\subsection{DIS Factorization and DGLAP Evolution}
\label{subsec:qcd-dis-factorization-dglap}

Figure~\ref{fig:qcd-dis-ope-light-ray-factorization} records the operator
factorization used for inclusive DIS: the short-distance current product is
matched to renormalized light-ray operators whose convolutional
renormalization gives DGLAP evolution.

\begin{figure}[H]
  \centering
  \resizebox{0.96\textwidth}{!}{%
  \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1cm,y=1cm,every node/.style={font=\scriptsize}]
    \begin{scope}
      \node[font=\small] at (0,2.35) {current product};
      \fill[blue!70!black] (-1.05,0.55) circle (2.4pt);
      \fill[blue!70!black] (1.05,0.55) circle (2.4pt);
      \draw[blue!70!black,thick] (-1.05,0.55)--(1.05,0.55);
      \node[above] at (-1.05,0.65) {\(J^\mu(x)\)};
      \node[above] at (1.05,0.65) {\(J^\nu(0)\)};
      \draw[<->,orange!85!black,thick] (-1.05,0.16)--(1.05,0.16);
      \node[orange!85!black,below] at (0,0.16) {\(|x|\sim Q^{-1}\)};
      \node[align=center] at (0,-0.8)
        {short-distance coefficients\\\(C_a^{\mu\nu}(x,\mu)\)};
    \end{scope}

    \draw[-{Latex[length=2mm]},thick] (2.25,0.45)--(3.75,0.45);
    \node[align=center] at (3.0,0.88) {OPE};

    \begin{scope}[shift={(5.35,0)}]
      \node[font=\small] at (0,2.35) {local tower};
      \draw[thick] (-1.4,0.85)--(1.4,0.85);
      \foreach \x in {-1.05,-0.55,-0.05,0.45,0.95} {
        \draw[blue!65!black,thick,-{Latex[length=1.6mm]}] (\x,0.15)--(\x,0.78);
      }
      \node[align=center] at (0,-0.68)
        {\(\bar q\,\gamma^{(\mu_1}\ii D^{\mu_2}\cdots \ii D^{\mu_N)}q\),\\
        \(F^{(\mu_1}{}_{\rho}\ii D^{\mu_2}\cdots F^{\mu_N)\rho}\)};
    \end{scope}

    \draw[-{Latex[length=2mm]},thick] (7.85,0.45)--(9.25,0.45);
    \node[align=center] at (8.55,0.88) {resum\\on light ray};

    \begin{scope}[shift={(11.0,0)}]
      \node[font=\small] at (0,2.35) {renormalized light-ray operator};
      \draw[purple!70!black,thick,decorate,
        decoration={snake,amplitude=0.85pt,segment length=7pt}]
        (-1.75,0.52)--(1.75,0.52);
      \fill[blue!70!black] (-1.75,0.52) circle (2.3pt);
      \fill[red!70!black] (1.75,0.52) circle (2.3pt);
      \node[below] at (-1.75,0.35) {\(\bar q(\lambda n)\)};
      \node[below] at (1.75,0.35) {\(q(0)\)};
      \node[purple!70!black,above] at (0,0.78) {\(W[\lambda n,0]\)};
      \node[align=center] at (0,-0.72)
        {matrix element in \(\ket P\)\\defines \(f_{a/H}(x,\mu)\)};
    \end{scope}
  \end{tikzpicture}
  }
  \caption{The short-distance current product is first expanded into local
  renormalized operators.  The leading-twist tower can then be packaged into
  gauge-invariant light-ray operators whose hadron matrix elements define
  parton distributions.  The Wilson segment \(W[\lambda n,0]\) is the open
  transporter connecting the colored fields in the bilocal operator.}
  \label{fig:qcd-dis-ope-light-ray-factorization}
\end{figure}

The factorization assertion has two logically separate parts.  The first is
the exact definition of the hadronic tensor as the current-current Wightman
matrix element \eqref{eq:hadronic-tensor-current-product}.  The second is the
leading-power short-distance statement that, after the current OPE and
light-ray renormalization have been performed, the same observable can be
coordinatized by universal hadronic light-ray matrix elements and perturbative
coefficient functions.

\paragraph{Common dependency ladder for QCD factorization.}
The local definitions above and the boundary sections below are used through a
single comparison architecture.  For a process family \(\mathfrak P\), a
theorem-level factorization statement has to provide:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the exact color-singlet observable \(W_{\mathfrak P}\), usually a
  Wightman current tensor or a finite-regulator Euclidean matrix element;
  \item the gauge-invariant operator coordinates, including Wilson-line
  geometry and the ultraviolet, cusp, endpoint, or rapidity subtractions
  required by that geometry;
  \item the short-distance coefficient, impact-factor, or matching map in a
  stated distribution topology;
  \item the scale-transport equations and finite-scheme covariance making the
  auxiliary factorization coordinates cancel in the paired observable;
  \item the leading-region or boundary mechanism, including threshold,
  small-\(x\), soft, rapidity, \(Y\)-term, or Glauber items whenever the
  process probes them;
  \item a power-remainder estimate uniform on the declared test-function
  window;
  \item the continuum, infinite-volume, large-momentum, or rapidity-regulator
  limit when the preceding objects are first constructed at finite regulator.
\end{enumerate}
Equivalently, after pairing with a test function \(\varphi\) in the declared
topology, the comparison between the exact observable and the factorized
coordinate must be bounded by a sum of named errors,
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
&
\left|
  \left\langle
    W_{\mathfrak P,Q}-\mathcal F_{\mathfrak P,Q},
    \varphi
  \right\rangle
\right|
\le
\mathcal E_{\mathfrak P,Q}^{\rm fact}(\varphi),
\\
&
\mathcal E_{\mathfrak P,Q}^{\rm fact}
:=
\epsilon_{\mathfrak P,Q}^{\rm obs}
+\epsilon_{\mathfrak P,Q}^{\rm op}
+\epsilon_{\mathfrak P,Q}^{\rm sub}
+\epsilon_{\mathfrak P,Q}^{\rm coeff}
+\epsilon_{\mathfrak P,Q}^{\rm evol}
+\epsilon_{\mathfrak P,Q}^{\rm bdry}
+\epsilon_{\mathfrak P,Q}^{\rm rem}
+\epsilon_{\mathfrak P,Q}^{\rm lim}.
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:qcd-common-factorization-budget}
\end{equation}
Here \(\mathcal F_{\mathfrak P,Q}\) denotes the claimed factorized coordinate.
For compact-\(x\) inclusive DIS, the boundary term records the exclusion of
threshold and small-\(x\) regions.  For Drell--Yan and other TMD observables it
contains the rapidity subtraction, the \(Y\)-term, and the Glauber status.  For
small-\(x\) observables it contains the Wilson-line rapidity state, the
projective generator limit, and the impact-factor map to a measured process.
The finite calculations retained in this chapter check individual entries in
this ladder; they are not substitutes for a proof that every required entry can
be made small on a common directed window.

\begin{hypothesis}[Leading-twist DIS factorization hypothesis]
\label{hyp:qcd-dis-leading-twist-factorization}
Fix a factorization scheme and a compact interval
\(K\Subset(0,1)\) of Bjorken \(x\).  A leading-twist factorization hypothesis for an
inclusive structure function \(F_i\) consists of coefficient distributions
\(C_{i,a}\), renormalized integrated PDFs \(f_{a/H}\), and constants
\(C_{K,\varphi}\), \(\Lambda_{\rm HT}\), and \(p>0\), such that for every test
function \(\varphi\in C_c^\infty(K)\) the difference between the exact
structure function and the factorized expression obeys
\[
  \left|
  \left\langle
  F_i-\sum_a C_{i,a}\otimes f_{a/H},\varphi
  \right\rangle
  \right|
  \le
  C_{K,\varphi}
  \left(\frac{\Lambda_{\rm HT}}{Q}\right)^p
\]
for all sufficiently large \(Q\).  The convolution is the one displayed in
\eqref{eq:dis-factorization}.  The compact-\(x\) restriction excludes the
separate threshold \(x\to1\) and small-\(x\) limits, whose large logarithms
require additional factorization data.
\end{hypothesis}

Under this hypothesis, factorization expresses a structure function \(F_i\) in
the form
\begin{equation}
  F_i(x_B,Q)
  =
  \sum_{a}
  \int_{x_B}^{1}\frac{\dd z}{z}\,
  C_{i,a}\!\left(\frac{x_B}{z},\frac{Q}{\mu},g(\mu)\right)
  f_{a/H}(z,\mu)
  +
  R_i(x_B,Q),
  \label{eq:dis-factorization}
\end{equation}
where \(a\) runs over quark, antiquark, and gluon parton species, and the
remainder \(R_i\) satisfies the distributional power bound in
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:qcd-dis-leading-twist-factorization}.  The coefficients
\(C_{i,a}\) are short-distance kernels; the distributions \(f_{a/H}\) are
universal hadronic matrix elements for the chosen factorization scheme.  This
paragraph is not a statement about colored asymptotic particles.  The
``parton'' label \(a\) is a label in the light-ray operator basis and in the
coefficient algebra.

The role of the parton distributions in
\eqref{eq:dis-factorization} is also the point at which the nonabelian theory
departs from the abelian Bloch--Nordsieck construction of
Remark~\ref{rem:abelian-scope-bloch-nordsieck}.  A quark or gluon entering a
short-distance hard subprocess is a colored partonic variable, not a physical
asymptotic state.  Its collinear gluon cloud is tied to a color generator and
to the Wilson line in \eqref{eq:pdf-light-ray-definition}.  Summing over
unresolved final-state gluons gives the final-state part of an
infrared-collinear safe observable, but the singularities associated with a
massless incoming colored parton are absorbed into the renormalized light-ray
operator defining \(f_{a/H}\).  Equivalently, the collinear subtraction that
renormalizes the PDF is part of the definition of the factorized hadronic
observable.  The residual \(\mu\)-dependence of this subtraction is the
DGLAP evolution below.

The operator-coordinate RG equation
\eqref{eq:qcd-light-ray-operator-dglap-rg} gives the evolution equation
\begin{equation}
  \mu\frac{\dd}{\dd\mu} f_{a/H}(x,\mu)
  =
  \sum_b\int_x^1\frac{\dd z}{z}\,
  P_{ab}\!\left(\frac{x}{z},g(\mu)\right)f_{b/H}(z,\mu),
  \label{eq:dglap-evolution}
\end{equation}
where \(P_{ab}\) are splitting kernels, equivalently the anomalous-dimension
kernels of the renormalized light-ray operator coordinates in the sign
convention of
\eqref{eq:qcd-light-ray-operator-dglap-rg}.  This is the precise sense in
which short-distance quark and gluon variables control high-energy hadronic
observables while physical asymptotic states remain color singlets.  The
factorized observable is independent of the auxiliary scale only when the
coefficient functions obey the dual equation
\begin{equation}
  \mu\partial_\mu C_{i,b}
  =
  -\sum_a C_{i,a}\otimes P_{ab}.
  \label{eq:qcd-dis-coefficient-dual-rg}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
  \mu\partial_\mu
  \sum_a C_{i,a}\otimes f_{a/H}
  =
  \sum_b
  \left(
    \mu\partial_\mu C_{i,b}
    +
    \sum_a C_{i,a}\otimes P_{ab}
  \right)\otimes f_{b/H}
  =
  0
\]
inside the declared convolution algebra.  Any residual scale dependence in a
finite-order calculation is therefore a truncation or power-remainder effect,
not a change in the nonperturbative definition of the PDF.

\subsection{One-Loop Splitting Kernels and Sum-Rule Checks}
\label{subsec:qcd-one-loop-splitting-kernels-sum-rules}

At leading order, in the same convention as \eqref{eq:dglap-evolution},
\[
  P_{ab}(x,g)
  =
  \frac{g^2}{8\pi^2}P_{ab}^{(0)}(x)+O(g^4).
\]
For unpolarized distributions in the \(\overline{\mathrm{MS}}\) scheme,
\[
  C_F=\frac{N_c^2-1}{N_c},
  \qquad
  C_A=2N_c,
  \qquad
  T_R=1,
\]
in the trace normalization of \eqref{eq:qcd-casimir-definitions}.  These are
twice the standard half-trace numbers, while the overall perturbative
coefficient in \eqref{eq:dglap-evolution} is written in the corresponding
coupling coordinate.  Let
\begin{equation}
  D_0(x):=\left(\frac1{1-x}\right)_+
  \label{eq:qcd-d0-plus-distribution}
\end{equation}
be the plus distribution defined by
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,D_0(x)\,\varphi(x)
  =
  \int_0^1\dd x\,\frac{\varphi(x)-\varphi(1)}{1-x}
\]
for every smooth test function \(\varphi\).  Products such as \(xD_0(x)\) are
defined by multiplication of this distribution by the smooth function \(x\).
With this unambiguous convention, the nonzero leading kernels are
\begin{align}
  P_{q_iq_j}^{(0)}(x)
  &=
  \delta_{ij}\,
  C_F\left[
    2D_0(x)-1-x
    +\frac32\delta(1-x)
  \right],
  \notag\\
  P_{\bar q_i\bar q_j}^{(0)}(x)
  &=
  P_{q_iq_j}^{(0)}(x),
  \notag\\
  P_{q_i g}^{(0)}(x)
  &=
  P_{\bar q_i g}^{(0)}(x)
  =
  T_R\bigl[x^2+(1-x)^2\bigr],
  \notag\\
  P_{gq_i}^{(0)}(x)
  &=
  P_{g\bar q_i}^{(0)}(x)
  =
  C_F\,\frac{1+(1-x)^2}{x},
  \notag\\
  P_{gg}^{(0)}(x)
  &=
  2C_A\left[
    xD_0(x)
    +\frac{1-x}{x}
    +x(1-x)
  \right]
  +
  \frac{11C_A-4T_RN_f}{6}\delta(1-x).
  \label{eq:lo-dglap-splitting-kernels}
\end{align}
This notation avoids the common ambiguity between plus-prescribing the whole
rational function and plus-prescribing only the pole at \(x=1\).  For example,
\(2D_0-1-x\) is the distribution often abbreviated as
\((1+x^2)/(1-x)_+\) in particle-physics notation.  Equivalently, for the flavor
singlet quark distribution
\(\Sigma=\sum_{i=1}^{N_f}(q_i+\bar q_i)\),
\[
  \mu\frac{\dd}{\dd\mu}
  \begin{pmatrix}\Sigma\\ f_g\end{pmatrix}
  =
  \frac{g^2}{8\pi^2}
  \begin{pmatrix}
    P_{qq}^{(0)} & 2N_fP_{qg}^{(0)}\\
    P_{gq}^{(0)} & P_{gg}^{(0)}
  \end{pmatrix}
  \otimes
  \begin{pmatrix}\Sigma\\ f_g\end{pmatrix}
  +O(g^4),
\]
where \(\otimes\) denotes the convolution appearing in
\eqref{eq:dglap-evolution}.  Nonsinglet quark combinations evolve with the
same \(P_{qq}^{(0)}\) and do not mix with the gluon at this order.

The kernels in \eqref{eq:lo-dglap-splitting-kernels} obey the following
one-loop distributional sum-rule checks:
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,P_{qq}^{(0)}(x)=0,
\]
and the two momentum-column identities
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,x
  \bigl(P_{qq}^{(0)}(x)+P_{gq}^{(0)}(x)\bigr)=0,
  \qquad
  \int_0^1\dd x\,x
  \bigl(2N_fP_{qg}^{(0)}(x)+P_{gg}^{(0)}(x)\bigr)=0 .
\]
Thus nonsinglet quark number and the total light-cone momentum fraction are
preserved by the leading-order evolution.
For \(m\ge0\),
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,x^mD_0(x)
  =
  \int_0^1\dd x\,\frac{x^m-1}{1-x}
  =
  -H_m,
  \qquad
  H_m:=\sum_{r=1}^m\frac1r ,
\]
with \(H_0=0\).  The number sum rule is
\[
  C_F\left(2H_0-\int_0^1(1+x)\,\dd x+\frac32\right)=0.
\]
For a quark parent,
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,xP_{qq}^{(0)}(x)
  =
  C_F\left(-2-\frac12-\frac13+\frac32\right)
  =
  -\frac43C_F,
\]
while
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,xP_{gq}^{(0)}(x)
  =
  C_F\int_0^1\dd x\,\bigl[1+(1-x)^2\bigr]
  =
  \frac43C_F .
\]
For a gluon parent,
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,xP_{qg}^{(0)}(x)
  =
  T_R\int_0^1\dd x\,x\bigl[x^2+(1-x)^2\bigr]
  =
  \frac13T_R ,
\]
and
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,xP_{gg}^{(0)}(x)
  =
  2C_A\left(-H_2+\frac12+\frac1{12}\right)
  +\frac{11C_A-4T_RN_f}{6}
  =
  -\frac23T_RN_f .
\]
The two column sums therefore vanish.

\section{Transverse-Momentum Dependent Distributions and Rapidity Renormalization}
\label{sec:qcd-tmd-rapidity-renormalization}

Integrated PDFs are obtained after summing over all transverse momentum in the
collinear sector.  Observables differential in a transverse momentum, for
example color-singlet production with \(q_\perp^2\ll Q^2\), require a different
operator coordinate.  The relevant nonperturbative input is not the integrated
light-ray operator \eqref{eq:qcd-quark-light-ray-operator}; it is a
transverse-separated light-ray matrix element with Wilson lines whose geometry
creates rapidity divergences.  Rapidity subtraction is therefore part of the
definition, in the same sense that ultraviolet subtraction is part of the
definition of a renormalized local operator.

Let \(n,\bar n\) be future-directed lightlike vectors with
\(n\cdot\bar n=2\), and let \(b_\perp\) be transverse:
\[
  b_\perp\cdot n=b_\perp\cdot\bar n=0 .
\]
For a real parameter \(\lambda\), set
\[
  z^\mu=\lambda n^\mu+b_\perp^\mu .
\]
A finite rapidity regulator may be implemented by replacing lightlike Wilson
lines by Wilson lines along non-lightlike directions \(v,\bar v\), by an
analytic rapidity regulator, by a delta regulator, or by an equivalent
gauge-covariant subtraction.  The monograph denotes the regulator data
collectively by \(\rho\).  At finite \(\rho\) and finite ultraviolet cutoff
\(\Lambda\), let
\(\mathcal U^{[\eta]}_{v}(z,0;\rho,\Lambda)\) be a staple transporter from
\(0\) to \(z\), with longitudinal direction \(v\), transverse bridge
\(b_\perp\), and orientation \(\eta=+1\) for future-pointing and
\(\eta=-1\) for past-pointing staples.

\begin{definition}[TMD operator definition]
\label{def:qcd-tmd-operator-definition}
A quark TMD operator definition for a hadron \(H\) with momentum \(P\) consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the vectors \(n,\bar n\), a transverse separation \(b_\perp\), and an
  orientation \(\eta\) of the staple Wilson line;
  \item a finite rapidity regulator \(\rho\) and ultraviolet regulator
  \(\Lambda\), both chosen in a gauge-covariant way;
  \item the unsubtracted beam matrix element
  \[
    B^{\rm unsub}_{q/H}(x,b_\perp;\rho,\Lambda,\eta)
    =
    \frac1{2P\cdot n}
    \int\frac{\dd\lambda}{2\pi}\,
    \ee^{-\ii x\lambda P\cdot n}
    \Bigl\langle
    \bar q(z)\,
    \mathcal U^{[\eta]}_{v}(z,0;\rho,\Lambda)\,
    \gamma\cdot n\,q(0)
    \Bigr\rangle_{P,H};
  \]
  \item the vacuum soft factor
  \(S(b_\perp;\rho,\Lambda,\eta)\), defined by the trace of the closed Wilson
  geometry obtained by multiplying the corresponding \(v\)- and
  \(\bar v\)-staples in the vacuum;
  \item a finite-part prescription, denoted
  \(\operatorname{FP}_{\rho,\Lambda}\), which removes ultraviolet and rapidity
  regulator dependence and introduces the scales \(\mu\) and \(\zeta\).
\end{enumerate}
The renormalized TMD in this scheme is
\begin{equation}
  F_{q/H}^{[\eta]}(x,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta)
  =
  \operatorname{FP}_{\rho,\Lambda}
  \left[
    Z_q(\mu,\zeta;\rho,\Lambda)\,
    \frac{
      B^{\rm unsub}_{q/H}(x,b_\perp;\rho,\Lambda,\eta)
    }{
      S(b_\perp;\rho,\Lambda,\eta)^{1/2}
    }
  \right].
  \label{eq:qcd-renormalized-tmd-definition}
\end{equation}
The square root is a convention for assigning half of the soft subtraction to
each collinear sector.  A different finite assignment is a different TMD
scheme, related by a finite multiplicative transformation.  The variables
\(\mu\) and \(\zeta\) record, respectively, ultraviolet and rapidity
renormalization.  The orientation \(\eta\) is part of the operator definition;
time-reversal odd TMDs may change sign between future- and past-pointing
staples, as in semi-inclusive DIS versus Drell--Yan kinematics.
\end{definition}

At finite regulator, the numerator and soft factor in
\eqref{eq:qcd-renormalized-tmd-definition} are gauge invariant after taking
the color trace and endpoint fields into account.  Hence a background
gauge-covariant finite-part prescription produces a gauge-invariant
renormalized TMD matrix element.
Every Wilson segment transforms by multiplication with the gauge
transformation at its endpoints, as in
\eqref{eq:qcd-wilson-transporter-gauge-transformation}.  Along a staple, the
factors at internal junctions cancel between adjacent segments.  The remaining
endpoint factors at \(0\) and \(z\) cancel the gauge transformations of
\(q(0)\) and \(\bar q(z)\).  In the soft factor all Wilson lines are multiplied
inside a trace, so the residual base-point factor is removed by cyclicity of
the trace.  The finite-part map changes only regulator and scale coordinates;
if it is background gauge covariant, it cannot introduce an uncanceled color
index.

Rapidity evolution is the statement that changing the auxiliary rapidity
scale changes the coordinate description of the same physical transverse
momentum distribution.  It is most transparent in impact-parameter space,
where convolutions in transverse momentum become products.  Put
\[
  \ell_\mu:=\log\mu,
  \qquad
  \ell_\zeta:=\log\sqrt{\zeta}.
\]
For a fixed \(x\)-test function and fixed \(b_\perp\), suppose the paired TMD
matrix element is nonzero and obeys
\begin{align}
  \frac{\partial}{\partial\ell_\zeta}
  \log F_{q/H}^{[\eta]}(x,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta)
  &=
  \mathcal D_q(b_\perp;\mu),
  \label{eq:qcd-collins-soper-equation}\\
  \frac{\partial}{\partial\ell_\mu}
  \log F_{q/H}^{[\eta]}(x,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta)
  &=
  \gamma_F^q(g(\mu),\ell_\zeta-\ell_\mu).
  \label{eq:qcd-tmd-mu-evolution}
\end{align}
The first equation defines the Collins--Soper kernel
\(\mathcal D_q\) in the chosen convention.

\paragraph{Collins--Soper consistency condition.}
The two scale variables \(\ell_\mu\) and \(\ell_\zeta\) are coordinates on the
renormalized TMD scheme, so a differentiable TMD whose mixed scale derivatives
commute obeys the corresponding integrability condition.  Explicitly, if the
derivatives in
\eqref{eq:qcd-collins-soper-equation}--\eqref{eq:qcd-tmd-mu-evolution}
commute on the renormalized TMD distribution, then
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\partial}{\partial\ell_\mu}\mathcal D_q(b_\perp;\mu)
  =
  \frac{\partial}{\partial\ell_\zeta}
  \gamma_F^q(g(\mu),\ell_\zeta-\ell_\mu).
  \label{eq:qcd-collins-soper-integrability}
\end{equation}
In the convention
\[
  \gamma_F^q(g,\ell_\zeta-\ell_\mu)
  =
  \gamma_F^{q,0}(g)
  -2\Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g)(\ell_\zeta-\ell_\mu),
\]
this gives
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\partial}{\partial\log\mu}\mathcal D_q(b_\perp;\mu)
  =
  -2\Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g(\mu)).
  \label{eq:qcd-collins-soper-cusp}
\end{equation}
At small \(b_\perp\), the one-loop kernel compatible with the cusp
normalization of \eqref{eq:qcd-nonsinglet-large-n} is
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal D_q(b_\perp;\mu)
  =
  -\frac{g^2(\mu)C_F}{4\pi^2}
  \log\frac{\mu^2 b_\perp^2\ee^{2\gamma_{\rm E}}}{4}
  +O(g^4),
  \label{eq:qcd-collins-soper-kernel-one-loop}
\end{equation}
up to a finite \(b_\perp\)-dependent scheme term independent of \(\mu\).
The last display is a normalization check on the one-loop result:
\(\partial_{\log\mu}\log(\mu^2b_\perp^2\ee^{2\gamma_{\rm E}}/4)=2\), so
differentiating \eqref{eq:qcd-collins-soper-kernel-one-loop} gives
\(-g^2C_F/(2\pi^2)+O(g^4)\), which is
\(-2\Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g)+O(g^4)\) with
\(\Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g)=g^2C_F/(4\pi^2)+O(g^4)\) in the trace-delta
normalization.  The substantive QCD input is the regulated Wilson-line
operator definition, the existence and scheme dependence of rapidity
renormalization, and the perturbative or nonperturbative determination of
\(\Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q\) and \(\mathcal D_q\); the displayed consistency
relation only records the integrability of the chosen scale coordinates.

\begin{remark}[Finite TMD scheme changes]
\label{rem:qcd-tmd-finite-scheme-change}
Let \(R(b_\perp;\mu,\zeta)\) be a finite scalar function and set
\(F'=\ee^R F\).  Then
\[
  \mathcal D'=\mathcal D+\frac{\partial R}{\partial\ell_\zeta},
  \qquad
  \gamma_F'=\gamma_F+\frac{\partial R}{\partial\ell_\mu}.
\]
The consistency relation
\eqref{eq:qcd-collins-soper-integrability} is preserved.  Therefore the
separation of a rapidity-sensitive cross section into hard, TMD, and soft
coordinates is scheme dependent, whereas the final cross section is not.
\par
Take logarithms of \(F'=\ee^R F\) and differentiate with respect to
\(\ell_\zeta\) and \(\ell_\mu\).  The displayed transformations follow.  Taking
\(\partial_{\ell_\mu}\) of the first transformation and
\(\partial_{\ell_\zeta}\) of the second gives the same extra term
\(\partial_{\ell_\mu}\partial_{\ell_\zeta}R\).  Hence the difference between
the two sides of
\eqref{eq:qcd-collins-soper-integrability} is unchanged.
\end{remark}

\begin{hypothesis}[Small-\(q_\perp\) color-singlet TMD factorization hypothesis]
\label{hyp:qcd-tmd-factorization-hypothesis}
For a color-singlet final state of invariant mass \(Q\) produced in
hadron--hadron scattering, a leading-power small-\(q_\perp\) TMD
factorization hypothesis consists of TMD schemes for the two incoming hadrons, a
hard function \(H_{ij}(Q,\mu)\), rapidity scales satisfying
\(\zeta_A\zeta_B=Q^4\), a \(Y\)-term that matches the region
\(|q_\perp|\sim Q\), a statement about Glauber exchange, and a distributional
remainder estimate.  In the region
\(\Lambda_{\rm QCD}\lesssim |q_\perp|\ll Q\) the singular part has the
impact-parameter form
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd\sigma_{\rm sing}}{\dd Q^2\dd^2q_\perp}
  =
  \sum_{i,j}
  H_{ij}(Q,\mu)
  \int\frac{\dd^2 b_\perp}{(2\pi)^2}\,
  \ee^{\ii b_\perp\cdot q_\perp}
  F_{i/A}(x_A,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_A)
  F_{j/B}(x_B,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_B).
  \label{eq:qcd-tmd-factorization}
\end{equation}
The formula is a theorem only when the regulator construction, cancellation or
operator representation of Glauber exchange, and the topology of the
power-remainder estimate have all been supplied.
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Matched small-\(q_\perp\) TMD spectrum]
\label{ca:qcd-tmd-y-term-matching-window}
The TMD formula in
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:qcd-tmd-factorization-hypothesis} controls only the
singular small-\(q_\perp\) coordinate.  A physical prediction on a tested
transverse-momentum spectrum also needs the fixed-order large-\(q_\perp\)
remainder.  Let \(\varphi(q_\perp)\) be a smooth compactly supported test
function in a color-singlet Drell--Yan or vector-boson window, and write
\[
  \mathfrak T_Q[\varphi]
  =
  \left\langle
    \frac{\dd\sigma}{\dd Q^2\dd^2q_\perp},
    \varphi
  \right\rangle
\]
for the exact tested spectrum in a finite regulator.  At fixed perturbative
order \(N\), let \(\sigma_{\rm FO}^{(N)}\) denote the ordinary fixed-order
coordinate and let
\((\sigma_{\rm sing}^{\rm TMD})_{[N]}\) be the expansion of the TMD singular
coordinate through the same order, in the same ultraviolet, rapidity, and
finite-subtraction scheme.  The \(Y\)-term is the tested distribution
\begin{equation}
  Y^{(N)}[\varphi]
  :=
  \left\langle
    \sigma_{\rm FO}^{(N)}
    -
    (\sigma_{\rm sing}^{\rm TMD})_{[N]},
    \varphi
  \right\rangle .
  \label{eq:qcd-tmd-y-term-tested-definition}
\end{equation}
The matched coordinate is therefore
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal M_{\rm TMD}^{(N)}[\varphi]
  :=
  \left\langle
    \sigma_{\rm sing}^{\rm TMD,resum},
    \varphi
  \right\rangle
  +
  Y^{(N)}[\varphi].
  \label{eq:qcd-tmd-matched-tested-spectrum}
\end{equation}
This subtraction is load-bearing: omitting
\((\sigma_{\rm sing}^{\rm TMD})_{[N]}\) counts the singular fixed-order terms
once in the resummed TMD coordinate and again inside \(\sigma_{\rm FO}^{(N)}\).

Rapidity scale cancellation is part of the same tested statement.  Parametrize
\(\zeta_A=Q^2\ee^{2\eta}\), \(\zeta_B=Q^2\ee^{-2\eta}\).  With the convention
\(\ell_\zeta=\log\sqrt{\zeta}\), this means
\[
  \ell_{\zeta_A}=\log Q+\eta,
  \qquad
  \ell_{\zeta_B}=\log Q-\eta .
\]
If the two incoming TMDs use the same Collins--Soper kernel in the
color-singlet channel and the hard factor has no residual
\(\eta\)-dependence, then
\begin{equation}
  \partial_\eta
  \log\!\left[
    H(Q,\mu)\,
    F_{i/A}(b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_A)\,
    F_{j/B}(b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_B)
  \right]
  =
  \mathcal D_i(b_\perp;\mu)-\mathcal D_j(b_\perp;\mu).
  \label{eq:qcd-tmd-rapidity-split-derivative}
\end{equation}
The factor is one, not two, because the Collins--Soper derivative above is with
respect to \(\log\sqrt{\zeta}\).  For the diagonal channel
\(\mathcal D_i=\mathcal D_j\) this vanishes.  In a mixing problem the
corresponding statement is a cancellation of rapidity anomalous-dimension
matrices in the paired hard/beam/soft coordinate.  If the kernels are
mismatched, if the product \(\zeta_A\zeta_B=Q^4\) is not held fixed, or if the
\(Y\)-term is evaluated in a different subtraction scheme, the residual
rapidity dependence is a matching error, not a new physical dependence of the
color-singlet spectrum.

A theorem-level matched TMD prediction is the assertion that
\begin{equation}
  \left|
  \mathfrak T_Q[\varphi]
  -
  \mathcal M_{\rm TMD}^{(N)}[\varphi]
  \right|
  \le
  \epsilon_{\rm TMD}[\varphi]
  +\epsilon_Y[\varphi]
  +\epsilon_{\rm G}[\varphi]
  +\epsilon_{\rm pwr}[\varphi]
  +\epsilon_{\rm reg}[\varphi],
  \label{eq:qcd-tmd-matched-spectrum-residual-bound}
\end{equation}
where the terms respectively record the singular-coordinate construction,
fixed-order \(Y\)-term truncation and matching, Glauber status, power
corrections such as \(q_\perp/Q\) and hadron masses, and regulator or
large-\(b_\perp\) residuals.  The finite Collins--Soper checks above verify only
the scale-coordinate algebra inside this statement; they do not prove the
existence of the exact QCD decomposition or the smallness of the residuals in
\eqref{eq:qcd-tmd-matched-spectrum-residual-bound}.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\section{Drell--Yan Factorization and Glauber Status}
\label{sec:qcd-drell-yan-glauber-status}

Drell--Yan production is the timelike current analogue of DIS:
\[
  h_A(P_A)+h_B(P_B)\longrightarrow \ell^+\ell^-+X,
  \qquad q=p_{\ell^+}+p_{\ell^-},
  \qquad q^2=Q^2>0 .
\]
The QCD object is again a Wightman current matrix element, now between a
two-hadron incoming state.  For unpolarized hadrons define
\begin{equation}
  W_{AB}^{\mu\nu}(P_A,P_B,q)
  =
  \frac1{N_{\rm spin}}
  \sum_{\sigma_A,\sigma_B}
  \sum_X
  (2\pi)^4\delta^{(4)}(P_A+P_B-q-P_X)
  \bra{P_A,P_B}J^\mu(0)\ket{X}
  \bra{X}J^\nu(0)\ket{P_A,P_B}.
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-hadronic-tensor}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, by translation covariance and completeness,
\begin{equation}
  W_{AB}^{\mu\nu}(P_A,P_B,q)
  =
  \frac1{N_{\rm spin}}
  \sum_{\sigma_A,\sigma_B}
  \int\dd^4x\,\ee^{\ii q\cdot x}
  \bra{P_A,P_B}J^\mu(x)J^\nu(0)\ket{P_A,P_B},
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-current-product}
\end{equation}
with the same state-normalization convention as in the scattering chapters.
The partonic formulae below are short-distance coordinates for this tensor;
they are not definitions of a cross section with colored asymptotic states.

\paragraph{Drell--Yan leading-power kinematics.}
Let
\[
  s:=(P_A+P_B)^2,
  \qquad
  \tau:=\frac{Q^2}{s},
\]
and choose the hadron center-of-mass frame with the \(A\)-hadron moving in the
positive longitudinal direction.  At leading power in hadron masses and
transverse momentum, the longitudinal momentum fractions entering the
short-distance hard collision are
\begin{equation}
  x_A=\sqrt{\tau}\,\ee^y,
  \qquad
  x_B=\sqrt{\tau}\,\ee^{-y},
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-xa-xb}
\end{equation}
where
\[
  y:=\frac12\log\frac{q^0+q^3}{q^0-q^3}
\]
is the lepton-pair rapidity.  Hence
\[
  x_Ax_B=\tau,
  \qquad
  y=\frac12\log\frac{x_A}{x_B}.
\]

In light-cone coordinates adapted to the beam directions, write the leading
hadron momenta as
\[
  P_A^+=\sqrt{s},\quad P_A^-=0,
  \qquad
  P_B^-= \sqrt{s},\quad P_B^+=0,
\]
and neglect transverse components in the leading-power kinematic identity.
The active partons carry
\[
  q^+=x_AP_A^+,\qquad q^-=x_BP_B^-.
\]
Therefore \(Q^2=q^+q^-+O(q_\perp^2,M_{A,B}^2)=x_Ax_Bs+O(q_\perp^2,M_{A,B}^2)\),
which gives \(x_Ax_B=\tau\) at leading power.  The rapidity satisfies
\[
  y=\frac12\log\frac{q^+}{q^-}
  =
  \frac12\log\frac{x_A}{x_B}.
\]
Solving the two equations gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-xa-xb}.

\paragraph{Integrated collinear factorization coordinate.}
If the lepton-pair transverse momentum is not kept differential, the appropriate
leading-power coordinate is the integrated collinear factorization formula, not
the TMD formula below.  Fix a compact rapidity and invariant-mass window in
which \(x_A,x_B\in K\Subset(0,1)\) and the threshold and small-\(x\) boundaries
are excluded.  A leading-power integrated Drell--Yan factorization hypothesis
consists of renormalized integrated PDF coordinates
\(f_{i/A},f_{j/B}\), a short-distance coefficient distribution
\(C^{\rm DY}_{ij}\), and a distributional remainder bound such that
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd\sigma_{\rm DY}}{\dd Q^2\dd y}
  =
  \sum_{i,j}
  \int_{x_A}^{1}\frac{\dd \xi_A}{\xi_A}
  \int_{x_B}^{1}\frac{\dd \xi_B}{\xi_B}\,
  f_{i/A}(\xi_A,\mu)\,
  f_{j/B}(\xi_B,\mu)\,
  C^{\rm DY}_{ij}
  \!\left(\frac{x_A}{\xi_A},\frac{x_B}{\xi_B};
  Q,\mu\right)
  +
  R_{\rm DY}.
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-integrated-factorization}
\end{equation}
The PDFs in \eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-integrated-factorization} are the
Wilson-line light-ray matrix elements of
Definition~\ref{def:qcd-renormalized-integrated-pdf-datum}.  The
coefficient \(C^{\rm DY}_{ij}\) is a hard matching distribution in the same
factorization scheme; it includes the chosen flux, electroweak-current, and
Jacobian normalization.  The remainder \(R_{\rm DY}\) contains the declared
power corrections, threshold and small-\(x\) exclusions, perturbative truncation
remainder, and the Glauber item discussed below.  Thus the formula is not an
identity between colored partonic cross sections.  It is a comparison between
the exact color-singlet Wightman tensor
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-current-product} and a factorized coordinate built from
two incoming light-ray operator matrix elements.

\begin{proposition}[Born Drell--Yan rapidity-bin coefficient]
\label{prop:qcd-drell-yan-born-rapidity-bin}
At leading power and Born order for a single virtual photon, the integrated
coefficient in
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-integrated-factorization} is supported at
\(z_A=z_B=1\).  With \(N_c\) colors and electromagnetic quark charge \(e_q\),
\begin{equation}
  C_{q\bar q}^{\rm DY,0}(z_A,z_B;Q)
  =
  C_{\bar q q}^{\rm DY,0}(z_A,z_B;Q)
  =
  \frac{4\pi\alpha_{\rm em}^2e_q^2}
       {3N_c\,Q^2s}\,
  \delta(1-z_A)\delta(1-z_B),
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-born-coefficient}
\end{equation}
for the cross section differential in \(Q^2\) and \(y\), after integrating the
lepton-pair decay angles.  Consequently, for a compact test function
\(\varphi(Q^2,y)\) whose support keeps \(x_A,x_B\in(0,1)\),
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \mathfrak T_{\rm DY}^{0}[\varphi]
  &=
  \sum_q
  \int\dd Q^2\,\dd y\,
  \varphi(Q^2,y)\,
  \frac{4\pi\alpha_{\rm em}^2e_q^2}
       {3N_c\,Q^2s}                                     \\
  &\qquad{}\times
  \Bigl[
    f_{q/A}(x_A,\mu)f_{\bar q/B}(x_B,\mu)
    +
    f_{\bar q/A}(x_A,\mu)f_{q/B}(x_B,\mu)
  \Bigr],
  \qquad
  x_{A,B}=\sqrt{\frac{Q^2}{s}}\,\ee^{\pm y}.
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-born-tested-bin}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The color-averaged partonic annihilation
\(q\bar q\to\gamma^\ast\to\ell^+\ell^-\) has the Born angular distribution
\[
  \frac{\dd\hat\sigma_{q\bar q}^{0}}{\dd\cos\theta}
  =
  \frac{\pi\alpha_{\rm em}^2e_q^2}{2N_cQ^2}
  (1+\cos^2\theta),
\]
where the factor \(1/N_c\) is the color average of the singlet electromagnetic
current.  Integrating \(\cos\theta\in[-1,1]\) gives
\[
  \hat\sigma_{q\bar q}^{0}(\hat s=Q^2)
  =
  \frac{4\pi\alpha_{\rm em}^2e_q^2}{3N_cQ^2}.
\]
At Born level the pair has zero transverse momentum, so
\[
  Q^2=s\xi_A\xi_B,
  \qquad
  y=\frac12\log\frac{\xi_A}{\xi_B}.
\]
The change of variables \((\xi_A,\xi_B)\mapsto(Q^2,y)\) has
\[
  \left|
  \det\frac{\partial(Q^2,y)}{\partial(\xi_A,\xi_B)}
  \right|=s,
\]
which supplies the factor \(1/s\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-born-coefficient}.  The convolution measure in
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-integrated-factorization} is also part of the
normalization: for \(0<x<1\),
\[
  \int_x^1\frac{\dd\xi}{\xi}\,
  f(\xi)\,\delta\!\left(1-\frac{x}{\xi}\right)
  =
  f(x),
\]
because
\(\delta(1-x/\xi)=x\,\delta(\xi-x)\).  Inserting the two Born delta functions
therefore evaluates the two PDFs at \(x_A\) and \(x_B\), giving
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-born-tested-bin}.  This proposition instantiates the
factorized coordinate in one measured channel; the residuals of
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-drell-yan-tested-factorization-residual-budget}
remain the additional all-order QCD factorization data.
\end{proof}

The scale cancellation is the two-incoming-leg analogue of
\eqref{eq:qcd-dis-coefficient-dual-rg}.  In a Mellin or Laplace chart where the
two convolutions become products, let \(f_A(N_A,\mu)\) and \(f_B(N_B,\mu)\) be
column vectors in parton species, and write the factorized coordinate as
\begin{equation}
  \widetilde\Sigma_{\rm DY}(N_A,N_B;\mu)
  =
  f_A(N_A,\mu)^T
  \widetilde C_{\rm DY}(N_A,N_B;Q,\mu)
  f_B(N_B,\mu).
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-transform-coordinate}
\end{equation}
If
\[
  \mu\frac{\dd f_A}{\dd\mu}=P_A f_A,
  \qquad
  \mu\frac{\dd f_B}{\dd\mu}=P_B f_B,
\]
then auxiliary-scale independence of
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-transform-coordinate} requires
\begin{equation}
  \mu\frac{\dd \widetilde C_{\rm DY}}{\dd\mu}
  =
  -P_A^T\widetilde C_{\rm DY}
  -\widetilde C_{\rm DY}P_B .
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-coefficient-dual-rg}
\end{equation}
Indeed,
\[
  \mu\frac{\dd}{\dd\mu}
  \bigl(f_A^T\widetilde C_{\rm DY}f_B\bigr)
  =
  f_A^T
  \bigl(P_A^T\widetilde C_{\rm DY}
  +\mu\partial_\mu\widetilde C_{\rm DY}
  +\widetilde C_{\rm DY}P_B\bigr)
  f_B,
\]
which vanishes by
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-coefficient-dual-rg}.  A finite factorization-scheme
change \(f_A'=R_A f_A\), \(f_B'=R_B f_B\) preserves the same physical coordinate
only if
\[
  \widetilde C_{\rm DY}'=(R_A^{-1})^T\widetilde C_{\rm DY}R_B^{-1}.
\]
This matrix identity is the clean bookkeeping behind statements that the two
incoming collinear singularities have been absorbed into the PDFs.  A
factorization proof must still supply the leading-region analysis, soft
cancellation or soft factor, Glauber status, and the remainder topology; the
algebra above only fixes the paired RG structure once those objects exist.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Integrated Drell--Yan theorem boundary]
\label{ca:qcd-drell-yan-integrated-theorem-boundary}
The exact object in integrated Drell--Yan is a tested distribution obtained
from the color-singlet Wightman tensor
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-current-product}, not the partonic coordinate
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-integrated-factorization}.  Fix a compact
\((Q^2,y)\)-window \(K\), away from threshold and small-\(x\) boundaries, and
let \(\mathcal D_K\) be the corresponding test-function space.  A
leading-power integrated factorization theorem for this window must supply:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item a finite-regulator definition of the exact tested functional
  \(\mathfrak T_{\rm DY}[\varphi]\), \(\varphi\in\mathcal D_K\), from
  \eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-current-product};
  \item the renormalized light-ray PDF coordinates and the hard coefficient in
  the same subtraction scheme;
  \item a leading-region map from the exact current product to the two
  incoming collinear sectors, with its error measured in
  \(\mathcal D_K^\ast\);
  \item a soft-cancellation or soft-factor construction in the same regulator;
  \item a Glauber statement strong enough for the chosen measurement topology,
  such as a commutator or inclusive-projection bound of the form described
  below;
  \item a power-remainder topology, including hadron-mass, threshold,
  small-\(x\), and perturbative-truncation qualifications;
  \item a regulator-limit statement identifying which residuals vanish and
  which remain as declared approximation errors.
\end{enumerate}
Thus the formula
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-integrated-factorization} becomes a theorem only after
the residuals in this list are bounded for the exact tested Wightman functional.
The paired RG equation \eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-coefficient-dual-rg} is one
coordinate-transport check inside this boundary; it is not the boundary itself.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{proposition}[Tested Drell--Yan factorization residual budget]
\label{prop:qcd-drell-yan-tested-factorization-residual-budget}
In the setting of
Controlled Approximation~\ref{ca:qcd-drell-yan-integrated-theorem-boundary},
suppose the subtraction analysis represents the exact tested functional as
\begin{equation}
  \mathfrak T_{\rm DY}[\varphi]
  =
  f_A^T C_\varphi f_B
  +
  \Delta_{\rm lead}[\varphi]
  +
  \Delta_{\rm soft}[\varphi]
  +
  \Delta_{\rm G}[\varphi]
  +
  \Delta_{\rm pwr}[\varphi]
  +
  \Delta_{\rm reg}[\varphi],
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-tested-residual-decomposition}
\end{equation}
where \(f_A^TC_\varphi f_B\) is the tested version of
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-integrated-factorization}.  Assume that, on a window
\(Q\ge Q_0\),
\begin{equation}
  |\Delta_a[\varphi]|
  \leq
  \epsilon_a(Q_0)\,\|\varphi\|_{\mathcal D_K},
  \qquad
  a\in\{\mathrm{lead},\mathrm{soft},\mathrm G,\mathrm{pwr},\mathrm{reg}\}.
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-residual-component-bounds}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
  \left|
  \mathfrak T_{\rm DY}[\varphi]-f_A^TC_\varphi f_B
  \right|
  \leq
  \left(
  \epsilon_{\rm lead}
  +\epsilon_{\rm soft}
  +\epsilon_{\rm G}
  +\epsilon_{\rm pwr}
  +\epsilon_{\rm reg}
  \right)
  \|\varphi\|_{\mathcal D_K}.
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-tested-residual-budget-bound}
\end{equation}
If the paired PDF/coefficient transport
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-coefficient-dual-rg} is exact, then
\(f_A^TC_\varphi f_B\) is independent of the auxiliary factorization scale, but
the physical mismatch in
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-tested-residual-budget-bound} is controlled only by the
five residual norms above.  Scale covariance of the factorized coordinate does
not make any nonzero residual disappear.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Subtract the factorized coordinate from
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-tested-residual-decomposition} and apply the triangle
inequality together with
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-residual-component-bounds}.  The final statement is the
scale derivative calculation already displayed in
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-coefficient-dual-rg}: the derivative of
\(f_A^TC_\varphi f_B\) cancels between the two PDF legs and the dual hard
coefficient.  This cancellation concerns only the retained coordinate.  The
exact Wightman functional can agree with it in the declared topology only when
the listed residual functionals are separately bounded, or vanish in the
regulator and large-\(Q\) limits being claimed.
\end{proof}

\begin{hypothesis}[Drell--Yan small-\(q_\perp\) TMD factorization hypothesis]
\label{hyp:qcd-drell-yan-tmd-factorization-hypothesis}
A leading-power Drell--Yan TMD factorization hypothesis consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the renormalized current hard function \(H_{ij}(Q,\mu)\);
  \item past-pointing TMD operator data
  \(F_{i/A}^{[-]}(x_A,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_A)\) and
  \(F_{j/B}^{[-]}(x_B,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_B)\), in the notation of
  Definition~\ref{def:qcd-tmd-operator-definition};
  \item rapidity scales constrained by \(\zeta_A\zeta_B=Q^4\);
  \item a \(Y\)-term matching to the region \(|q_\perp|\sim Q\);
  \item a proof or controlled hypothesis for Glauber exchange;
  \item a distributional power-remainder estimate in \(q_\perp/Q\) and in the
  hadron-mass corrections.
\end{enumerate}
The singular small-\(q_\perp\) term is then represented as
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd\sigma_{\rm sing}}{\dd Q^2\dd y\,\dd^2q_\perp}
  =
  \sum_{i,j}
  H_{ij}(Q,\mu)
  \int\frac{\dd^2b_\perp}{(2\pi)^2}\,
  \ee^{\ii b_\perp\cdot q_\perp}
  F_{i/A}^{[-]}(x_A,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_A)
  F_{j/B}^{[-]}(x_B,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_B),
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-tmd-factorization}
\end{equation}
plus the stated \(Y\)-term and power remainder.  The past-pointing staple
orientation is part of the operator definition.  It is the operator-level
source of the sign reversal of time-reversal-odd TMD coordinates between
semi-inclusive DIS and Drell--Yan, once the relevant antiunitary
transformation and spin conventions are specified.
\end{hypothesis}

\paragraph{Finite unitarity model for Glauber cancellation.}
Let \(\mathcal H_{\rm obs}\) be a finite-dimensional observed Hilbert space,
let \(\mathcal H_{\rm un}\) be an unobserved Hilbert space, let
\(\rho\) be a trace-class density matrix on
\(\mathcal H_{\rm obs}\otimes\mathcal H_{\rm un}\), and let \(M\) be an
observable acting only on \(\mathcal H_{\rm obs}\).  If the effect of a
Glauber exchange on the unobserved degrees of freedom is represented by a
unitary \(U_G\) acting only on \(\mathcal H_{\rm un}\), then
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Tr}_{\rm obs,un}
  \left[
    (M\otimes\mathbf1)
    (\mathbf1\otimes U_G)\rho(\mathbf1\otimes U_G^\dagger)
  \right]
  =
  \operatorname{Tr}_{\rm obs,un}
  \left[
    (M\otimes\mathbf1)\rho
  \right].
  \label{eq:qcd-finite-glauber-unitarity-identity}
\end{equation}

Use cyclicity of the full trace and
\((\mathbf1\otimes U_G^\dagger)(M\otimes\mathbf1)(\mathbf1\otimes U_G)
=M\otimes\mathbf1\).  The result is
\[
  \operatorname{Tr}
  \left[
    \rho
    (\mathbf1\otimes U_G^\dagger)(M\otimes\mathbf1)(\mathbf1\otimes U_G)
  \right]
  =
  \operatorname{Tr}\left[\rho(M\otimes\mathbf1)\right],
\]
which is
\eqref{eq:qcd-finite-glauber-unitarity-identity}.
Equivalently, the partial trace over the unobserved Hilbert space is invariant
under unitary conjugation on that same unobserved factor.  The finite model
therefore isolates the algebraic input used in inclusive Glauber-cancellation
arguments: the observed measurement must be insensitive to the unitary acting
on the summed-over sector.

The same finite model also gives the residual which must be bounded when the
measurement is not fully inclusive.  For a general tested measurement
\(M_\varphi\) on
\(\mathcal H_{\rm obs}\otimes\mathcal H_{\rm un}\), define
\begin{equation}
  \Delta_{\rm G}^{\rm fin}[\varphi]
  =
  \operatorname{Tr}
  \left[
    \rho
    \bigl(
      (\mathbf1\otimes U_G^\dagger)
      M_\varphi
      (\mathbf1\otimes U_G)
      -
      M_\varphi
    \bigr)
  \right].
  \label{eq:qcd-finite-glauber-resolved-measurement-residual}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
  \Delta_{\rm G}^{\rm fin}[\varphi]=0
  \quad\hbox{if}\quad
  [M_\varphi,\mathbf1\otimes U_G]=0,
\]
and in finite dimension
\begin{equation}
  |\Delta_{\rm G}^{\rm fin}[\varphi]|
  \leq
  \|\rho\|_1\,
  \left\|
      (\mathbf1\otimes U_G^\dagger)
      M_\varphi
      (\mathbf1\otimes U_G)
      -
      M_\varphi
  \right\|_{\rm op}.
  \label{eq:qcd-finite-glauber-resolved-measurement-bound}
\end{equation}
Thus the integrated Drell--Yan Glauber residual
\(\Delta_{\rm G}[\varphi]\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-tested-residual-decomposition} is not a ceremonial
slot.  It asks whether, after the leading-region and contour-deformation
analysis has identified the regulated eikonal Glauber action, the tested
color-singlet observable is inclusive enough for the commutator to vanish, or
whether the remaining commutator is quantitatively small in the declared
measurement topology.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[What the finite Glauber calculation proves]
\label{ca:qcd-glauber-cancellation-status}
The finite unitarity calculation above is the algebraic identity that a
Drell--Yan factorization proof must realize after the leading regions, color
flow, rapidity regulator, and measurement topology have been fixed.  It does
not prove by itself that QCD Glauber exchanges act only on an unobserved
tensor factor, nor that the contour deformations needed to isolate the
leading regions are valid.  Those statements are part of the
Glauber item in Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:qcd-drell-yan-tmd-factorization-hypothesis}.  If the
observable measures hadronic radiation in a way that resolves the spectator
sector, or if a color exchange remains entangled with the measured hard
sector, the finite identity above no longer supplies the required
cancellation.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\section{Off-Forward Light-Ray Matrix Elements and GPDs}
\label{sec:qcd-gpd-light-ray-matrix-elements}

Generalized parton distributions are light-ray matrix elements between
different hadron momenta.  They do not require a rapidity subtraction in the
same way as TMDs, because the operator remains integrated over transverse
momentum.  Their new feature is off-forwardness.

Let \(p'\) and \(p\) be on-shell spin-\(\frac12\) hadron momenta, and define
\[
  P=\frac{p'+p}{2},
  \qquad
  \Delta=p'-p,
  \qquad
  t=\Delta^2,
  \qquad
  \xi=-\frac{\Delta\cdot n}{2P\cdot n}.
\]
For the symmetric light-ray separation
\[
  z^\mu=\lambda n^\mu ,
\]
define the quark vector GPDs \(H^q\) and \(E^q\) by
\begin{align}
  &\int\frac{\dd\lambda}{2\pi}\,
  \ee^{-\ii x\lambda P\cdot n}
  \bra{p',s'}
  \left[
  \bar q\!\left(\frac{\lambda n}{2}\right)
  W_{\square}\!\left(\frac{\lambda n}{2},-\frac{\lambda n}{2}\right)
  \gamma\cdot n\,
  q\!\left(-\frac{\lambda n}{2}\right)
  \right]_{\mu}
  \ket{p,s}
  \notag\\
  &\qquad =
  \bar u_{s'}(p')
  \left[
    \gamma\cdot n\,H^q(x,\xi,t;\mu)
    +\frac{\ii\sigma^{n\alpha}\Delta_\alpha}{2M}\,
    E^q(x,\xi,t;\mu)
  \right]
  u_s(p),
  \label{eq:qcd-gpd-definition}
\end{align}
where \(\sigma^{n\alpha}:=n_\mu\sigma^{\mu\alpha}\), and \(M\) is the hadron
mass.  The support and endpoint behavior of the distributions are properties
of the renormalized light-ray matrix elements and of the chosen hadronic
state; they are not imposed by a parton model.

\begin{lemma}[Polynomiality of GPD moments]
\label{lem:qcd-gpd-polynomiality}
Assume the renormalized twist-two local operators obtained from the light-ray
operator in \eqref{eq:qcd-gpd-definition} exist as local operator-valued
distributions between the hadron states under consideration.  Then the
\(N\)-th Mellin moments
\[
  \int_{-1}^{1}\dd x\,x^{N-1}H^q(x,\xi,t;\mu),
  \qquad
  \int_{-1}^{1}\dd x\,x^{N-1}E^q(x,\xi,t;\mu)
\]
are polynomials in \(\xi\) of degree at most \(N\), with coefficients that are
Lorentz-scalar form factors depending on \(t\) and \(\mu\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Expanding the symmetric light-ray operator in \(\lambda\) gives the local
twist-two tower
\[
  \bar q\,\gamma^{(\mu_1}
  \ii D^{\mu_2}\cdots\ii D^{\mu_N)}q-\text{traces},
\]
contracted with \(n_{\mu_1}\cdots n_{\mu_N}\).  Since \(n^2=0\), all trace
terms vanish after contraction with these \(n\)'s.  Lorentz covariance of the
off-forward matrix element gives a finite decomposition into symmetric tensors
made from \(P\), \(\Delta\), the metric, and the spinor bilinears
\(\bar u(p')\gamma^\alpha u(p)\) and
\(\bar u(p')\ii\sigma^{\alpha\beta}\Delta_\beta u(p)\).  After contraction
with \(n_{\mu_1}\cdots n_{\mu_N}\), each term contains
\[
  (P\cdot n)^{N-k}(\Delta\cdot n)^k
  =
  (P\cdot n)^N(-2\xi)^k
\]
for some \(0\le k\le N\), multiplied by a scalar form factor depending only on
\(t\) and \(\mu\).  Dividing by the overall powers of \(P\cdot n\) in the GPD
decomposition therefore gives a polynomial in \(\xi\) of degree no larger than
\(N\).  This argument uses only locality, Lorentz covariance, and the
existence of the renormalized local twist-two tower; it does not use a
probability interpretation.
\end{proof}

Deeply virtual Compton scattering and related exclusive processes use these
GPDs in coefficient-function convolutions.  As in inclusive DIS and TMD
factorization, the GPD itself is the renormalized hadronic light-ray matrix
element.  The factorization theorem connecting it to a measured exclusive
amplitude is an additional leading-power assertion with its own endpoint,
Glauber, and power-remainder data.

\section{Asymptotic Freedom and Exclusive Pion Amplitudes}
\label{sec:qcd-exclusive-pion-asymptotic-freedom}

\subsection{Pion Light-Ray Data and Factorization Scheme}
\label{subsec:qcd-pion-light-ray-factorization-scheme}

Inclusive DIS uses forward light-ray matrix elements.  Exclusive pion
amplitudes use light-ray matrix elements between the vacuum and a one-pion
state.  This is the part of the pion \(S\)-matrix where asymptotic freedom
gives a direct large-momentum prediction: the short-distance subgraph is a
perturbatively renormalized quark-gluon amplitude, while the pion appears only
through a renormalized gauge-invariant light-ray matrix element.  The statement
is not that a pion is a weakly bound pair of on-shell quarks.  The pion input is
the same hadronic state defined by the nonperturbative QCD sector; only the
coefficient multiplying its light-ray matrix element is perturbative.

Let \(P^\mu\) be the momentum of a charged pion and let \(n^\mu\) be a
future-directed lightlike vector with \(P\cdot n>0\).  In the isospin-symmetric
two-flavor theory, define the charged-pion light-cone distribution amplitude
by the renormalized bilocal matrix element
\begin{equation}
  \bra{\vac}
  \left[
  \bar d(\lambda n)\,
  W_{\square}(\lambda n,0)\,
  \gamma\cdot n\,\gamma_5\,u(0)
  \right]_{\mu}
  \ket{\pi^+(P)}
  =
  \ii f_\pi\,P\cdot n
  \int_0^1\dd x\,
  \ee^{-\ii x\lambda P\cdot n}\,
  \varphi_\pi(x,\mu).
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-lcda-definition}
\end{equation}
The Wilson transporter is the same path-ordered fundamental transporter used
in \eqref{eq:qcd-quark-light-ray-operator}.  The normalization of \(f_\pi\) is
the axial-current normalization of Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-21},
\[
  \bra{\vac}A_a^\mu(0)\ket{\pi^b(P)}
  =
  \ii f_\pi P^\mu\delta_a{}^b .
\]
Setting \(\lambda=0\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-pion-lcda-definition} therefore fixes
\begin{equation}
  \int_0^1\dd x\,\varphi_\pi(x,\mu)=1 .
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-lcda-normalization}
\end{equation}
The support interval \([0,1]\) is a property of the leading-twist light-ray
operator between the vacuum and the one-pion state.  It is not a probability
postulate.  The function \(\varphi_\pi\) is a renormalized distribution in
\(x\), depending on the factorization scheme and scale.

\begin{definition}[Exclusive pion factorization scheme]
\label{def:qcd-exclusive-pion-factorization-scheme}
An exclusive large-\(Q\) pion factorization statement consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item a renormalized QCD matrix element whose external hadrons and currents
  are gauge-invariant;
  \item a light-ray operator basis, here represented at leading twist by
  \(\varphi_\pi(x,\mu)\);
  \item a hard coefficient \(T_H\), computed with external collinear partons
  and subtracted in the same scheme as the light-ray operator;
  \item a convolution prescription in the momentum fractions;
  \item a topology for the remainder, for example
  \(O(\Lambda_{\rm QCD}^2/Q^2)\) after excluding endpoint regions by the
  stated hypotheses, together with the order in \(\alpha_s\) to which
  \(T_H\) is known.
\end{enumerate}
The scheme is part of the definition of the controlled approximation.  Without
it, a formula involving a pion distribution amplitude is only notation.
\end{definition}

\subsection{ERBL Evolution and Gegenbauer Coordinates}
\label{subsec:qcd-erbl-gegenbauer-coordinates}

The one-loop renormalization of the light-ray operator in
\eqref{eq:qcd-pion-lcda-definition} gives the Efremov--Radyushkin--Brodsky--
Lepage evolution equation
\begin{equation}
  \mu\frac{\dd}{\dd\mu}\varphi_\pi(x,\mu)
  =
  \frac{\alpha_s(\mu)}{2\pi}
  \int_0^1\dd y\,V(x,y)\varphi_\pi(y,\mu)
  +O(\alpha_s^2),
  \label{eq:qcd-erbl-evolution}
\end{equation}
where, in the trace-delta convention,
\begin{align}
  V(x,y)
  &=
  C_F
  \left[
  \theta(y-x)\frac{x}{y}
  \left(1+\frac1{y-x}\right)
  +
  \theta(x-y)\frac{1-x}{1-y}
  \left(1+\frac1{x-y}\right)
  \right]_+ .
  \label{eq:qcd-erbl-kernel}
\end{align}
The plus prescription acts on the \(x\)-variable:
\begin{equation}
  \int_0^1\dd x\,[K(x,y)]_+ f(x)
  :=
  \int_0^1\dd x\,K(x,y)\bigl(f(x)-f(y)\bigr),
  \label{eq:qcd-erbl-plus-prescription}
\end{equation}
for test functions smooth near \(x=y\).  Equation
\eqref{eq:qcd-erbl-plus-prescription} makes the conservation of the axial
current normalization manifest:
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,V(x,y)=0 .
\]

\begin{proposition}[Diagonalization of the leading ERBL kernel]
\label{prop:qcd-erbl-gegenbauer-diagonalization}
For \(n\ge0\), let \(C_n^{3/2}\) be the Gegenbauer polynomial orthogonal on
\([-1,1]\) with weight \((1-z^2)\).  The leading ERBL kernel preserves the
basis
\[
  \varphi_n(x):=6x(1-x)C_n^{3/2}(2x-1),
\]
and
\begin{equation}
  \int_0^1\dd y\,V(x,y)\varphi_n(y)
  =
  -\frac12\gamma_n^{(0)}\,\varphi_n(x),
  \label{eq:qcd-erbl-eigenvalue-equation}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
  \gamma_n^{(0)}
  =
  C_F\left[
  1-\frac{2}{(n+1)(n+2)}
  +4\sum_{k=2}^{n+1}\frac1k
  \right].
  \label{eq:qcd-erbl-anomalous-dimensions}
\end{equation}
In particular \(\gamma_0^{(0)}=0\) and
\(\gamma_n^{(0)}>0\) for every \(n\ge1\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Write
\[
  P_n(x):=C_n^{3/2}(2x-1),\qquad
  \varphi_n(x)=6x(1-x)P_n(x).
\]
The plus prescription in \eqref{eq:qcd-erbl-plus-prescription} subtracts the
same raw kernel with the first argument integrated.  Therefore, for any
polynomial \(P\), the singular action of \eqref{eq:qcd-erbl-kernel} on
\(\varphi_P(y):=6y(1-y)P(y)\) is the following finite polynomial:
\begin{align}
  \frac1{C_F}\int_0^1\dd y\,V(x,y)\varphi_P(y)
  &=
  6(1-x)\int_0^x\dd y\,y\bigl(P(y)-P(x)\bigr)
     \left(1+\frac1{x-y}\right)
     \notag\\
  &\quad
  +6x\int_x^1\dd y\,(1-y)\bigl(P(y)-P(x)\bigr)
     \left(1+\frac1{y-x}\right).
  \label{eq:qcd-erbl-finite-polynomial-action}
\end{align}
This identity is only the definition of the plus distribution written at fixed
\(x\): the factors \(y(1-x)\) and \(x(1-y)\) come from
\((1-x)\varphi_P(y)/(1-y)\) and \(x\varphi_P(y)/y\), while the delta
